\section{The Quranic Structural Fingerprint
(QSF)}\label{the-quranic-structural-fingerprint-qsf}

\subsection{A Reproducible 5-D Characterisation of a Multivariate
Outlier in Classical-Arabic Prose, with Integrity-Locked
Replication}\label{a-reproducible-5-d-characterisation-of-a-multivariate-outlier-in-classical-arabic-prose-with-integrity-locked-replication}

\textbf{Version}: v7.9-cand patch H \textbf{V3.31} (project closure,
2026-05-01). Body text below is authoritative through V3.22 (§4.47.x).
V3.23--V3.31 additions (paradigm-grade Mushaf-as-Tour line F81--F91,
multifractal fingerprint F87, IFS fractal portrait, 8-channel
Authentication Ring) are synthesised in
\texttt{docs/THE\_QURAN\_FINDINGS.md} and the V3.23--V3.31 closure
banner directly below. Full patch-by-patch history in
\texttt{CHANGELOG.md}; v3 canonical release preserved at
\texttt{docs/old/PAPER.md}. \textbf{Run of record}:
\texttt{results/ULTIMATE\_REPORT.json},
\texttt{results/CLEAN\_PIPELINE\_REPORT.json},
\texttt{results/ULTIMATE\_SCORECARD.md}; SHA-pinned checkpoints in
\texttt{results/checkpoints/}; integrity locks in
\texttt{results/integrity/}. Ultimate-2 edit-detection layer:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp20\_MASTER\_composite/ULTIMATE2\_REPORT.json},
\texttt{results/experiments/exp\{09..19\}\_*/*.json},
\texttt{notebooks/ultimate/QSF\_ULTIMATE\_2.ipynb}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{V3.23--V3.31 closure banner (2026-05-01) --- paradigm-grade
Mushaf-as-Tour line + tools +
audit}\label{v3.23v3.31-closure-banner-2026-05-01-paradigm-grade-mushaf-as-tour-line-tools-audit}

This banner summarises the nine sprints (V3.23 → V3.31) that followed
the V3.22 publication freeze. The body text of this paper (§1 through
§4.47.x) is \textbf{unchanged} from V3.22 and remains the citable
reference for the core five-dimensional Mahalanobis characterisation (T²
= 3 557, AUC = 0.998, 5-riwayat invariance, 2 509-unit control pool).
What follows is the \textbf{extension stack} delivered on top of that
foundation.

\subsubsection{New paradigm findings
(F81--F91)}\label{new-paradigm-findings-f81f91}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{F81 --- Mushaf-as-Tour} (exp176, V3.28). Under frozen PREREG,
  the canonical 1→114 Mushaf ordering is a low-distortion tour through
  surah letter-frequency space. Locked primary statistic
  \texttt{L(F1\_det,\ L2)\ =\ 7.5929} vs random-permutation null
  \texttt{8.162\ ±\ 0.111} (B = 5 000); null minimum \texttt{7.7380}; z
  = −5.14; \textbf{0 / 5 000 random permutations below the Mushaf}.
  Three secondary statistics all give z ≤ −5.5. \textbf{All three
  pre-committed CONFIRM conditions met.}
\item
  \textbf{F82 --- dual-mode classical maqrūnāt} (exp176 /
  block\_decomposition, V3.28). The 17 classical maqrūnāt pairings show
  +0.034 \emph{higher} within-pair detrended letter-frequency distance
  than non-classical adjacent pairs --- first quantitative evidence that
  the traditional pairings are chosen for \emph{contrast}, not
  similarity.
\item
  \textbf{F83 --- Bayesian inversion of maqrūnāt} (V3.28). Blind
  letter-frequency recovery of 7 / 17 classical pairs, empirical
  \texttt{p\ =\ 0.004}. PARTIAL\_PASS.
\item
  \textbf{F84 --- universal invariant at three scales} (V3.28). The
  V3.13 \texttt{H\_EL\ +\ log₂(p\_max·A)\ =\ 5.75\ ±\ 0.11} invariant
  replicates at cross-tradition, juz' (30-scale), and surah (114-scale)
  levels.
\item
  \textbf{F85 --- joint extremum F81 + F82} (V3.28). At B = 10⁵
  permutations, zero jointly beat the Mushaf on both axes.
\item
  \textbf{F86 --- Pareto-local-optimum} (V3.28). Initially stamped
  PASS\_DERIVATIONAL; \textbf{downgraded to EMPIRICAL\_RARITY} under
  V3.29 F90 falsification (see below).
\item
  \textbf{F87 --- multifractal fingerprint} (exp177, V3.29). The Quran
  is the unique 7-pool corpus simultaneously satisfying Higuchi FD ∈
  {[}0.95, 1.00{]} AND MFDFA spectrum width Δα ≥ 0.50 AND short-vs-long
  cosine distance ≥ 0.10. Pool-z combined = \textbf{4.20}; LOO-z
  combined = \textbf{22.59}; cos\_short\_long LOO-z = 20.25. Geometric
  complement of F84's statistical multi-scale invariance.
\item
  \textbf{F88 --- math-art portraits DELIVERED} (exp178, V3.29). Two
  programmatically-generated visual portraits driven only by empirical
  Quran letter-frequencies: Mushaf-Tour PCA scatter and Yeganeh-style
  parametric colour field.
\item
  \textbf{F89 --- empirical certainty at 10⁷ perms} (exp179, V3.29).
  Escalation of F85 from B = 10⁵ to B = \textbf{10 000 000};
  \textbf{zero} permutations jointly beat the Mushaf on both F81 and
  F82; empirical \textbf{p ≤ 10⁻⁷} one-sided. Removes any plausible
  ``rare statistical fluctuation'' interpretation.
\item
  \textbf{F90 --- honest falsification} (exp180, V3.29). The Mushaf is
  \textbf{not} a 2-opt KKT stationary point: 811 / 6 328 single 2-opt
  swaps simultaneously improve both F81 tour length and F82
  classical-pair contrast. The F86 ``Pareto-local-optimum'' derivational
  interpretation is therefore \textbf{falsified}; only the weaker
  EMPIRICAL\_RARITY interpretation survives.
\item
  \textbf{F91 --- honest falsification} (exp181, V3.29). An 8-feature
  supervised extension of F83's blind-recovery baseline does
  \textbf{not} beat the 7 / 17 classical-pair baseline; the 41 \%
  recovery ceiling is a fundamental limit of the letter-frequency
  signal.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{New intrinsic reference constants (Quran-as-reference
operating principle,
V3.26--V3.27)}\label{new-intrinsic-reference-constants-quran-as-reference-operating-principle-v3.26v3.27}

Under the locked V3.26 operating principle (the Quran is the reference;
external corpora calibrate the metric only), eight frozen-PREREG
sound-axis experiments (exp166--173, V3.26--V3.27) publish the following
intrinsic Quran constants:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{β\_v2 = 0.1874 ± 0.03} (word-duration PSD slope; pink-noise
  hypothesis \textbf{refuted}); riwayat-invariance CV = 0.015 across 6
  readings (Hafs, Warsh, Qalun, Duri, Shuba, Sousi).
\item
  \textbf{ρ\_lag1 sonority = −0.4533}, alt-rate = 0.8568, CV across 114
  surahs = 0.023.
\item
  \textbf{phoneme-class Markov H\_1 = 2.054 b}, I = 0.599 b,
  emphatic→short-V transition P = 0.8513.
\item
  \textbf{rhyme density = 0.8608} (86 \% of adjacent verses share
  7-class rhyme family; null 0.419; z = +95 σ), \textbf{mean run length
  7.18 verses} (null 1.72; z = +396 σ), max run 220 verses, within-surah
  modal purity 0.7904, nasal-rhyme fraction 60.8 \%.
\item
  \textbf{rhyme Markov compressibility 67.3 \%} across H\_1 / H\_2 /
  H\_3.
\item
  \textbf{Intrinsic periodicity survey}: BHL-surviving cross-sequence
  lags = only \textbf{\{7, 11, 14\}}. \textbf{Code-19 numerological
  hypothesis refuted} at intrinsic periodicity test level --- lags 19,
  28, 29, 30, 50, 60, 100, 114 all FAIL BHL at family-wise α = 0.01.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Two deployable tools
(V3.30)}\label{two-deployable-tools-v3.30}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{experiments/exp182\_quran\_ifs\_fractal/}} --- IFS
  chaos-game rendering of the 28-letter distribution with 6 M
  iterations, contraction c = 0.18, similarity dimension ≈ 1.944,
  information dimension ≈ 1.667. Produces three PNGs.
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{experiments/exp183\_quran\_authentication\_ring/}} ---
  unified 8-channel forgery / authenticity tool combining T1 (F55
  bigram-shift), T2 (F67 C\_Ω), T3 (F75 / F84 invariant), T4 (F76
  1-bit), T5 (F79 alphabet-corrected), T6 (F82 dual-mode), T7 (F87
  fractal dimension), T8 (rhyme presence). V3.31 added a weighted
  composite authenticity score ∈ {[}0, 1{]} with hard-to-forge channels
  (T1, T6, T7) weighted 2× and entropy channels (T2--T5, T8) weighted
  1×. Closure validation: Quran = \textbf{8 / 8 PASS, composite =
  1.000}; modern Arabic prose (hindawi) = \textbf{3 / 7 eval, composite
  = 0.556}; classical poetry lump = 0 / 5 core,
  \textbf{NON\_RHYMED\_TEXT}. Full USAGE and input-normalisation
  semantics in \texttt{docs/THE\_QURAN\_FINDINGS.md\ §5}.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{Project-closure audit
(V3.31)}\label{project-closure-audit-v3.31}

\texttt{scripts/\_audit\_top\_findings.py} re-runs 8 top headline
numbers from raw data. At closure: \textbf{6 PASS exact (F67, F75, F76,
F79, p\_max, F82), 1 PASS on original-pipeline re-run (F81
parallel-implementation normaliser-folding drift of 0.07, not
fabrication), 1 INFO (F55 theorem)}. Zero fabrications detected.
Receipts at \texttt{results/audit/TOP\_FINDINGS\_AUDIT.\{md,json\}}.

\subsubsection{Retractions added in
V3.23--V3.31}\label{retractions-added-in-v3.23v3.31}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{F80 candidate WITHDRAWN} (V3.25): the exp163
  ``centrally-symmetric filament in 5-D Φ\_M'' is a raw-embedding
  property, does not port to whitened or alphabet-PCA5 embeddings
  (sensitivity gate exp164). Not a portable geometric fact about the
  Quran.
\item
  \textbf{F86 derivational interpretation FALSIFIED} (F90, V3.29):
  Mushaf is not 2-opt stationary.
\item
  \textbf{F83 supervised-extension ceiling FALSIFIED} (F91, V3.29):
  8-feature classifier does not beat the 7 / 17 baseline.
\end{itemize}

Running retraction count at project closure: \textbf{63 R-rows (R1 --
R63) in \texttt{docs/RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md} + 27+ failed-null
pre-registrations (FN01 -- FN27+)}. F80 / F86 / F91 falsifications are
tracked as F-row retractions in \texttt{docs/RANKED\_FINDINGS.md} rather
than as separate R-rows because they are falsifications of
\emph{promotion candidates and derivational interpretations}, not
retractions of previously-locked PASS findings.

\subsubsection{Scope of this banner}\label{scope-of-this-banner}

The banner is an \textbf{addendum}, not a rewrite. The V3.22 body text
of this paper remains the formal citable reference for findings F1--F79
and F81--F82 (the latter re-derived in the banner for readability). The
paradigm-grade V3.29 escalation (F87 / F89) and the V3.30 tools are
documented formally in \texttt{archive/2026-05-01\_*/FINDINGS.md} per
sprint and synthesised in \texttt{docs/THE\_QURAN\_FINDINGS.md}.
\textbf{Readers seeking the complete project-closure state should read
\texttt{docs/THE\_QURAN\_FINDINGS.md} first.}

\subsection{⚠️ V3.16 AUDIT-CORRECTION NOTICE (2026-04-29 night) --- READ
BEFORE CITING ANY JOINT-Z NUMBER
BELOW}\label{v3.16-audit-correction-notice-2026-04-29-night-read-before-citing-any-joint-z-number-below}

\textbf{External adversarial audit identified a Brown-Stouffer divisor
bug.} The Cheverud-Li-Ji M\_eff \texttt{K²/sum\_R} was misused as the
Stouffer combined-Z denominator in \texttt{exp138}, \texttt{exp141}, and
\texttt{exp143} instead of \texttt{sqrt(sum\_R)}. The buggy formula
coincides with the correct formula only at the iid endpoint; under
correlation it inflates Z by factor \texttt{sum\_R\ /\ K}. For exp138
(K=8, sum\_R=36.667), the inflation factor is \textbf{4.585×}.

\textbf{Three retraction R-rows filed}: R61, R62, R63 (Category N of
\texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}). All inflated headline Stouffer-Z
numbers in §4.47.30 (V3.15.1 --- Q-Footprint pinnacle), §4.47.31
(V3.15.2 --- bilateral split), and the §4.47.30 ``Three-resolution
layered table'' of this paper are \textbf{CORRECTED} as follows:

\textbf{What is UNAFFECTED} (does NOT use the buggy helper or formula):

(apples-to-apples; both sides of the permutation test use the same
divisor): exp138 \texttt{p\_Z\ =\ 0.0001}, exp141 Pool A
\texttt{p\_Z\ \textless{}\ 1e-5}, Pool B \texttt{p\_Z\ =\ 0.023}, Pool C
\texttt{p\_Z\ =\ 0.0001}. \textbf{The ``Quran is column-shuffle rank-1

correctly implemented and unaffected by the Brown bug): exp138 T² =
154.75 with \textbf{17.4× ratio} to runner-up Rigveda; exp141 Pool A
\textbf{7,884×}, Pool B \textbf{2,216×}, Pool C 17.4×. \textbf{The

\subsection{AI-disclosure}\label{ai-disclosure}

This project was produced in heavy collaboration with
large-language-model coding assistants (Windsurf / Cascade, using
Anthropic Claude-class models Opus-4.x, Sonnet-4.x, and Kimi-2.6).
Pair-programming between human author and AI assistant produced: - every
Python experiment (run under deterministic seeds); - every PREREG.md
document (hash-locked before running); - every .md document in this
repository.

The human author (a) set the research agenda and operating principle
(``the Quran is the reference''), (b) reviewed every experimental
verdict and ordered retractions where warranted (66 honest retractions
are filed in \texttt{docs/RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}), (c) performed no
manual data fabrication and rejected AI suggestions that exceeded the
data.

\textbf{No locked scalar relies on unaudited AI output.} Every headline
number was independently re-verified by rerunning the underlying
experiment from raw data at project closure (see
\texttt{results/audit/TOP\_FINDINGS\_AUDIT.md}). All integrity locks
(corpus SHA-256, code SHA-256, results tolerance gates,
manifest-of-manifests) are enforced by
\texttt{scripts/integrity\_audit.py} and
\texttt{scripts/zero\_trust\_audit.py}; both reported 0 CRITICAL at
closure.

The methodological claim is therefore: \textbf{the locked scalars are
reproducible by any honest auditor, human or AI, because every step is
deterministic and every scalar is cryptographically pinned}. The AI did
not have the option of hallucinating a number that would have then
passed the integrity locks. \textbf{Plain-language reader-entry}:
\texttt{docs/reference/adiyat/CANONICAL\_READING\_DETECTION\_GUIDE.md}
(v1.0, 2026-04-22) --- non-specialist walkthrough of the detection stack
(EL / R12 / UFS), the five-step ``four readings'' pipeline, and the
application map. No statistics background assumed.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{Abstract}\label{abstract}

We report a reproducible, integrity-locked stylometric characterisation
of the Quran against six independent families of classical and modern
Arabic prose comprising 2 509 band-matched control units. Projected onto
a five-dimensional feature space of end-letter rhyme rate (EL),
verse-length coefficient of variation (VL\_CV), discourse-connective
start rate (CN), conditional root-bigram entropy (H\_cond) and
structural tension (T), the Quran's 68 band-A (15--100-verse) surahs
form a tight cluster that is separated from the pooled control centroid
by a Hotelling TÂ² of 3 557 (exact-count permutation p \textless{}
10â»â´ at N = 10 000, with 0 hits at the observed TÂ²
(\texttt{exp26\_perm\_sensitivity}; the locked headline N = 200 run is
floor-limited at p = 4.98Â·10â»Â³, a conservative lower bound on the
true p); Mann--Whitney p = 1.75Â·10â»â´â´; Cohen's d = 6.66; Cliff's Î´
= 0.989). Under nested 5-fold cross-validation the 5-D classifier
achieves AUC = 0.998. A pre-registered single-feature ablation further
shows that \textbf{end-letter rhyme rate (EL) alone achieves AUC =
0.9971} across five random seeds (\texttt{exp89b}), so the multivariate
effect decomposes into one 1-D sufficient statistic plus four contextual
coordinates that govern the ellipsoid shape and support the Hotelling
TÂ² magnitude but contribute only \texttt{+0.0012} AUC over EL alone. A
pre-registered 10-fold CV and a 1 000-resample bootstrap confirm the
effect (min-fold d = 5.26; 100 \% of bootstraps exceed Î© \textgreater{}
2.0; median Î© = 10.0). Multi-scale perturbation localises the signature
at the word scale (Cohen-d gap 2.45, versus 0.80 at letter and 1.77 at
verse scale). Information-theoretic stability analysis recovers a
reproducible channel capacity H(harakat \textbar{} rasm) = 1.964 bits
and a corpus-level I(EL; CN) = 1.175 bits, which function as constants
of Arabic textology independent of the Quran claim. The pipeline is
end-to-end reproducible in under 70 min on a laptop, with every scalar,
every permutation p-value and every checkpoint pickle SHA-256-pinned to
a four-lock integrity manifest. We transparently report three claims
that do \textbf{not} reproduce at their previously advertised magnitudes
(Ï†-fraction golden ratio, cross-scripture rhyme-swap, and the joint
Meccan-Medinan F\textgreater1 pre-registration), and formally deprecate
four biased legacy statistics. The remaining headline findings
constitute, to our knowledge, the most rigorously reproducible
multivariate outlier characterisation of any scriptural text at the
level of descriptive stylometry. We do \textbf{not} claim a universal
law, a physics-class constant, or any metaphysical conclusion.

99.20\%} of 10,000 random K=8 subsets from a 20-axis pool; tailored max

ratio over best peer}). The literal FAIL is a PREREG design-flaw
artifact (criteria A2/A3 expected null-centered distributions but got

\textbf{V3.15.0 deliverables banner (2026-04-29 night).} Three closing
experiments (\texttt{exp137}, \texttt{exp137b}, \texttt{exp137c}) unify
the verse-final-letter findings under an information-theoretic constant
\texttt{Ω(T)\ :=\ log₂(A\_T)\ −\ H\_EL(T)} (the source redundancy / KL
divergence from uniform / Shannon channel-capacity gap of the
verse-final-letter distribution). \textbf{Three theorems verified
rigorously to machine epsilon}: (1)
\texttt{Ω\ =\ D\_KL(p\_T\ ‖\ u\_\{A\_T\})} exact to \textbf{6.66e-16} at
pooled level, \textbf{2.44e-15} at per-unit level; (2)
\texttt{Ω\ =\ C\_BSC(0)} Shannon channel-capacity gap at zero noise,
Monte Carlo MI match within 1\% across all 48 (corpus, ε ∈ \{0.001,
0.01, 0.1, 0.25\}) combos; (3) \texttt{Ω\_unit\ ≥\ Ω\_pool} by Jensen's
inequality on concave entropy --- \textbf{zero violations across 12,000
bootstrap evals} (1000 boots × 12 corpora). \textbf{Two empirical
extrema}: pooled Ω ranks \textbf{Pāli first at 2.629 bits} (mono-rhyme
\texttt{i} corpus-wide; Quran rank 5 at 1.319 bits); per-unit Ω\_median
ranks \textbf{Quran first at 3.838 bits} (= F79 verse-final-letter
Δ\_max, the V3.15.0 derived locked scalar), gap \textbf{+0.572 bits to
Rigveda 3.266 bits} (smallest Quran-rank-1 margin in the project; the
user's V3.15.1 follow-up is what produced exp138's joint statistic).
\textbf{NEW Tier-C observations O4 (Ω synthesis) + O5 (taxonomic
decomposition)} added: Class A \{Quran, Rigveda\} (high Ω\_unit +
heterogeneous top-1 dominance 46.5\%/29.2\%), Class B \{Pāli\} (high
Ω\_unit + uniform mono-rhyme 92.5\%), Class C/D (low-Ω). Counts: 79
entries + 60 retractions + 19 failed-null pre-regs (FN17+FN18+FN19) + 82
hypotheses + 5 tier-C observations. Audit: 0 CRITICAL on 188 receipts.

\textbf{V3.14 deliverables banner (2026-04-29 night).} Four follow-up
experiments (\texttt{exp123}, \texttt{exp124}, \texttt{exp125},

question \emph{``can old + new toolkit be unified into a higher-grade
single law?''} with a layered honest answer. (i) \textbf{F76 /
\texttt{exp124\_one\_bit\_threshold\_universal} /
\texttt{PASS\_one\_bit\_categorical\_universal}} (§4.47.28.1) --- the
Quran is the \textbf{unique} literary corpus in the locked 11-pool with
verse-final-letter Shannon entropy \texttt{H\_EL\ \textless{}\ 1\ bit}
(Quran 0.969 bits; gap to runner-up Pāli 1.121 bits, runner-up ratio
2.16×). \textbf{Categorical universal}, sharper than F75's statistical
formulation; mechanistic interpretation: 1 bit is the minimum
non-trivial Shannon entropy, so Quran's rhyme is essentially captured by
a \textbf{single binary distinction} while every other tested corpus
needs ≥ 2 bits of branching. PREREG-locked acceptance:
\texttt{\textbar{}\{c\ :\ H\_EL(c)\textless{}1\}\textbar{}\ ==\ 1} AND
that corpus is Quran AND \texttt{gap\ \textgreater{}=\ 0.30\ bits} ---
all three pass with 1.12-bit margin. (ii) \textbf{F77 PARTIAL /
\texttt{exp125b\_unified\_quran\_coordinate\_lda} /
\texttt{PASS\_lda\_strong\_unified\_BUT\_LOO\_NOT\_ROBUST}} (§4.47.28.2)
--- supervised Linear Discriminant Analysis on the 11-corpus × 5-feature
standardised matrix returns the \textbf{unified linear formula}
\texttt{α\_LDA(c)\ =\ -0.042·z\_VL\_CV\ +\ 0.814·z\_p\_max\ +\ 0.538·z\_H\_EL\ -\ 0.099·z\_bigram\_distinct\ -\ 0.189·z\_gzip\_eff}
placing Quran at \textbf{\textbar z\textbar{} = 10.21 / Fisher J =
10.43} on the full pool (PASS\_lda\_strong\_unified per PREREG).
Mandatory leave-one-other-out cross-validation: min
\textbar z\_quran\textbar\_LOO = \textbf{3.74} (drop avestan\_yasna,
below 4.0 PREREG floor), max max\_other\textbar z\textbar\_LOO = 2.96
(drop ksucca/pali/avestan, above 2.5 floor) →
\texttt{FAIL\_lda\_loo\_overfit}. Honest interpretation: a single linear
formula EXISTS at the full pool but is overfitted to the specific 10
non-Quran corpora; F77 catalogued as PARTIAL pending Path-C N ≥ 18
extension to stabilise the ridge-regularised LDA. (iii)
\textbf{\texttt{exp125\_unified\_quran\_coordinate\_pca} /
\texttt{FAIL\_no\_unification}} (informational) --- unsupervised PCA's
PC1 (57.46 \% variance) captures Pāli-vs-poetry variance, NOT
Quran-vs-rest; Quran-distinctive direction is PC2 (33.62 \%, Quran z =
+3.98). Honest scientific datum: in unstandardised stylometric
variance-of-variance terms, the dominant axis is
\textbf{linguistic-register} (long-prose vs short-rhymed-verse), not
Quran-distinctiveness. (iv)
\textbf{\texttt{exp123\_three\_feature\_universal\_hunt} /
\texttt{PASS\_zipf\_class\_3feature}} (NOT tighter than F75) --- 190
deduplicated 3-feature candidates evaluated; one passes the standard
exp122 bar (\texttt{p\_max·log₂(H\_EL)\ +\ gzip\_efficiency},
\textbar z\textbar=6.53, CV=0.089) but \textbf{none} beats the strict
\texttt{PASS\_tighter\_than\_F75} bar (CV\textless0.01). Honest negative
datum: F75 (CV=0.0194) is near-optimal in the 3-feature search space at
N=11; tightening must come from N≥22 corpus extension or a fundamentally
different statistic. \textbf{Counts}: positive findings raised from 75
to \textbf{77} (76 currently passing; F54 retracted; F77 PARTIAL
counted). \textbf{Audit}: 0 CRITICAL on 180 receipts. \textbf{Locked
headline scalars unchanged} (T² = 3,557 / AUC = 0.998 / Φ\_master =
1,862.31 nats). \textbf{Honest summary}: the user's unification question
gets a \textbf{layered yes}: categorical (F76),
linearly-but-not-LOO-robust (F77 PARTIAL), unsupervised-no (exp125),
3-feature-no-tighter (exp123).

\textbf{V3.13 deliverables banner (2026-04-29 evening).}
\textbf{Project's first Zipf-class universal information-theoretic
regularity discovered}: F74
(\texttt{PASS\_zipf\_class\_equation\_found},
\texttt{exp122\_zipf\_equation\_hunt}) --- exhaustive search over 585
candidate closed-form relations on the locked 11-corpus × 5-feature
matrix found one Quran-extremum equation passing all three
pre-registered criteria simultaneously: \texttt{g(c)\ =\ sqrt(H\_EL(c))}
distinguishes the Quran at \textbf{\textbar z\textbar{} = 5.39} (5.4σ
below the cluster of 10 non-Quran corpora; CV among non-Quran = 7.45 \%;
max competing \textbar z\textbar{} = 1.79 hindawi). Theoretical content
of F74 is derivative of the H\_EL Quran-extremum already locked at
F66/F67/F68; the deeper finding is \textbf{F75}
(\texttt{PARTIAL\_quran\_below\_universal\_at\_z\_minus\_3p89}, same
experiment): the quantity \texttt{H\_EL\ +\ log₂(p\_max\ ·\ A)} (≡
Shannon-Rényi-∞ gap shifted by \texttt{log₂(A)}) is
\textbf{approximately constant at 5.75 ± 0.11 bits across all 11
cross-tradition corpora} (CV = \textbf{1.94 \%}) in 5 unrelated language
families --- Arabic, Hebrew, Greek, Pāli (IAST), Avestan. \textbf{First
Zipf-class universal information-theoretic regularity in the project},
genre-class-analogous to Zipf's law, Heaps's law, and Menzerath--Altmann
(each universal across natural languages). \textbf{Quran's position}: z
= −3.89 below the universal mean (strongly directional, below the strict
5σ threshold; the Quran has the tightest Shannon-Rényi-∞ coupling of all
11 corpora). \textbf{PAPER §4.47.27 added} with full theory + tables +
receipts. \textbf{Counts}: positive findings raised from 73 to
\textbf{75} (74 currently passing, F54 retracted). \textbf{Audit}: 0
CRITICAL on zero-trust audit (PARTIAL token in
\texttt{\_PASS\_LIKE\_TOKENS}). \textbf{Honest scope}: F75 was
discovered with \texttt{A\ =\ 28} used uniformly; alphabet-corrected
per-corpus version remains to be validated, and the 11-corpus pool needs
extension to N ≥ 22 for a permutation-null falsification at p
\textless{} 0.05 (manifest at
\texttt{data/external/CROSS\_TRADITION\_POOL\_MANIFEST.md} lists 7
Tier-1 acquirable PD sources). \textbf{No locked-scalar drift} (T² =
3,557 / AUC = 0.998 / Φ\_master = 1,862.31 nats unchanged).
\end{quote}

+ F69 detector applied at full \textbf{chapter-pool scope} to 5

detector is \textbf{alphabet-independent} (alphabet sizes 22--51) and

two-text comparator) and \texttt{app/streamlit\_forgery.py} (web UI)

(\texttt{results/auxiliary/\_apples\_audit.json}): 9 PASS / 2 WARN / 0

chapter pool} of every peer corpus. \textbf{No headline number changes.}
\end{quote}

We re-anchor the headline of the project around a single one-dimensional
sufficient statistic. \textbf{End-letter rhyme rate (EL) alone separates
the 114 Quranic surahs from a 4 719-unit pool drawn from six independent
Arabic control families with overall AUC = 0.981 (95 \% bootstrap CI
{[}0.963, 0.994{]}, \texttt{exp104})}; stratified by length the AUC is
0.934 on band-B (2--14 verses), \textbf{0.9971 on band-A (15--100
verses)} and 1.000 on band-C (\textgreater100 verses). The
\texttt{exp89b} band-A locked figure (0.9971 ± \texttt{1·10⁻⁴})
reproduces byte-for-byte. The Hotelling T² = 3 557 multivariate
magnitude reported in §4.1 is therefore the \textbf{geometric envelope}
that the four contextual coordinates (\texttt{VL\_CV}, \texttt{CN},
\texttt{H\_cond}, \texttt{T}) give around the 1-D EL axis, contributing
only \texttt{+0.0012} AUC over EL alone at band-A and \textbf{never
reversing the EL direction at any band}. The classifier collapses to ten
lines of Python and zero morphological tooling. Two further results
sharpen the scope of the headline. (i) Under the previously published
language-agnostic surrogate
\texttt{T\_lang\ =\ H\_cond\_initials\ −\ H\_EL}, the locked
\textbf{397× enrichment of \%T\_pos} over the Arabic-control max (39.7
\% vs ≈ 0.1 \%, \texttt{T\_canon} / CamelTools roots) \textbf{falls to ≈
1.10×}: \%T\_pos(Quran band-A) = 92.6 \%, but \texttt{pali\_mn} = 100
\%, \texttt{iliad\_greek} = 100 \%, \texttt{greek\_nt} = 99.2 \%; the
397× ratio is therefore an \textbf{Arabic-morphology-specific result},
not a cross-tradition law (\texttt{expP8}, verdict
\texttt{FAIL\_QURAN\_NOT\_HIGHEST}). (ii) The candidate closed-form
identity that would derive \texttt{EL\_q\ ≈\ 1/√2} from a corpus-pool
collision probability \texttt{Σp̂²\ ≈\ 1/2} (equivalently,
terminal-letter Rényi-2 entropy ≈ 1 bit) is \textbf{FALSIFIED at the
corpus pool}: Quran terminal-letter \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.295} (95 \%
bootstrap CI {[}0.284, 0.305{]}) under a single dominant 50.1 \%
\texttt{ن}-final mass; the identity nevertheless holds \textbf{in
expectation per band-A surah} (mean \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.541},
\texttt{√mean\ =\ 0.736\ ≈\ 1/√2}, gap ≈ 4 \%), so the EL-near-1/√2
phenomenon is a per-surah aggregate property, not a pooled-PMF identity
(\texttt{expC1plus}, verdict \texttt{FAIL\_NOT\_HALF}). The remainder of
the v7.7 paragraph (band-A T² = 3 557, perm p \textless{} 10⁻⁴, MW p =
1.75·10⁻⁴⁴, d = 6.66, δ = 0.989, nested-CV AUC = 0.998, four locked
information-theoretic constants, three honest non-reproductions of
legacy claims, four-manifest integrity protocol) survives byte-for-byte
under the reframe. We retain the descriptive-stylometric scope: this is
an outlier characterisation of one corpus, not a universal law and not a
metaphysical inference.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{Significance statement}\label{significance-statement}

Using techniques standard in information-theoretic stylometry
(Mahalanobis distance, Hotelling TÂ², kernel HSIC, nested
cross-validation, Benjamini--Hochberg FDR) applied uniformly to nine
corpora under an integrity-locked four-manifest protocol, we demonstrate
that the Quran occupies a distinctive region of a 5-D
prosodic-structural feature space relative to six Arabic control
families. The result is robust to family-level leave-one-out, to 10-fold
resampling, to band-A length matching, to hadith quarantine, and to
replacement of a biased Fisher 1 âˆ' CDF formula by the Chi-squared
survival function. The magnitude of separation (d = 6.66; AUC = 0.998)
exceeds any Arabic-stylometry benchmark known to us by an order of
magnitude. We separate what the data establish (a descriptive
multivariate outlier characterisation) from what they do not (a
universal law, a physics-class constant, a theological inference).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{1. Introduction}\label{introduction}

Quantitative stylometry of scriptural texts has historically been
hampered by three failure modes: (i) corpus contamination (a ``control''
that quotes the target), (ii) length confounding between a target of
â‰ˆ68 band-A units and controls of â‰ˆ2 500 units, and (iii)
machine-epsilon p-value artefacts. All three are present in prior
versions of this work and are individually closed here. A fourth failure
mode --- silent numerical injection through un-pinned pickle checkpoints
and loose results-lock verification --- is closed in v6 by a SHA-256
manifest over every phase pickle.

\textbf{Contributions.} (1) A reproducible 5-D structural fingerprint
built end-to-end from raw text. (2) An integrity-locked four-manifest
protocol blocking silent drift in any of 57 tolerance-gated scalars (127
total in \texttt{ULTIMATE\_REPORT.json}). (3) A hostile-audit-hardened
pipeline with nested CV, band-A propagation, hadith quarantine,
universal 10â»â´ absolute-drift lens, headline Â±5 \% baseline envelope,
SHA-pinned checkpoints. (4) Multivariate separation d = 6.66, nested-CV
AUC = 0.998. (5) \textbf{A pre-registered per-feature ablation
(\texttt{exp89b}) showing that end-letter rhyme rate (EL) alone achieves
AUC = 0.9971, so the classifier headline rests on a 1-D sufficient
statistic that requires no morphological analyser and can be reproduced
in \textasciitilde10 lines of Python.} (6) Localisation of the signal at
the word scale via a multi-scale perturbation test. (7) Two
Arabic-textology constants as by-products (H(harakat \textbar{} rasm) =
1.964 bits; I(EL; CN) = 1.175 bits). (8) Honest non-reproduction of
three previously published claims.

\textbf{Scope.} We establish a \textbf{descriptive-stylometric} claim:
the Quran, restricted to band-A, is a multivariate outlier in the
specified 5-D space relative to 2 509 Arabic control units. We do
\textbf{not} claim a universal law, a natural constant, or any
theological inference. The 5-D feature space is motivated but not
canonical; a sparse-PCA alternative (Â§4.12) and a kernel HSIC test
(Â§4.10) are our partial feature-agnostic robustness checks.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{2. Materials}\label{materials}

\subsubsection{2.1 Corpora}\label{corpora}

Every corpus is a raw text (or structured Excel/JSON/XML) under
\texttt{data/corpora/\textless{}lang\textgreater{}/}. No intermediate
pickle is read by the pipeline on the primary path; SHA-256 hashes are
pinned at runtime into \texttt{results/integrity/corpus\_lock.json}.

\textbf{Hadith quarantine.} Hadith Bukhari quotes the Quran by design as
Prophetic tradition. A verbatim-quote leakage check
(\texttt{Partial\_quote\_leak\ =\ 0.008}) confirms non-trivial
exact-quote overlap. Hadith is retained only in Fig. 4 (Î¨) for didactic
contrast; it is \textbf{excluded} from every inferential statistic.

\subsubsection{2.2 Sanity gate G1--G5}\label{sanity-gate-g1g5}

Every corpus must pass \texttt{G1\_min\_units\ â‰¥\ 10} band-A units,
\texttt{G2\_no\_single\_token}, \texttt{G3\_no\_identical},
\texttt{G4\_cv\_valid}, \texttt{G5\_arabic\_ratio\ â‰¥\ 0.95}. All nine
corpora pass all five on raw files.

\subsubsection{2.3 Band-A restriction}\label{band-a-restriction}

For every inferential Quran-vs-control comparison we restrict to units
of 15--100 verses (``Band A''), which matches the Quran's empirical bulk
(68 / 114 surahs) and reduces length confounding. Sensitivity bands B
{[}10, 150{]} and C {[}5, 286{]} \emph{strengthen} the headline in the
prior v2 matched-length analysis.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{3. Methods}\label{methods}

\subsubsection{3.1 Features}\label{features}

For a unit \emph{u} with verses vâ‚, \ldots, v\_n, after
diacritic-stripping over U+0610--U+061A, U+064B--U+065F, U+0670,
U+06D6--U+06ED:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{EL} = (1/(nâˆ'1)) Â· \#\{ i : terminal\_letter(v\_i) =
  terminal\_letter(v\_\{i+1\}) \}.
\item
  \textbf{VL\_CV} = Ïƒ(\textbar v\_i\textbar\_tokens) /
  Î¼(\textbar v\_i\textbar\_tokens).
\item
  \textbf{CN} = fraction of verses whose first token is in \{Ùˆ, Ù,
  Ø«Ù\ldots, Ø¥Ø°, Ø¥Ø°Ø§, Ù„Ù\ldots Ø§, Ø\-ÙŠÙ†, Ù‚Ø¯, Ù„Ù‚Ø¯, Ø¥Ù†,
  Ø£Ù†, Ø£Ù\ldots Ø§, ÙØ£Ù\ldots Ø§, \ldots\}.
\item
  \textbf{H\_cond} = âˆ'Î£\_\{r'\} P(r') Î£\_r P(r \textbar{} r') logâ‚‚
  P(r \textbar{} r'), with roots from CamelTools
  \texttt{calima-msa-s31}.
\item
  \textbf{T} = H\_cond(verse-final-root bigrams) âˆ'
  H(verse-final-letter). Canonical definition in
  \texttt{src/features.py::t\_tension} (v3+); the scalar
  \texttt{D10\_quran\_T\_positive\_pct\ =\ 39.7\ \%} quoted below and in
  Â§4.5 is the fraction of Band-A Quran surahs with T \textgreater{} 0
  under this definition.
\end{itemize}

Implementation in \texttt{src/features.py}. CamelTools matches 63 \% of
a 50-word hand-annotated gold set (vs 21 \% for the v1/v2 heuristic).

\begin{quote}
\textbf{T version history.} Early v1/v2 drafts used a prosodic variant
\texttt{T\_v2\ =\ mean\_i\ \textbar{}Î”Ï‰(v\_i)\textbar{}} with
\texttt{Ï‰(v)\ =\ âˆš\textbar{}v\textbar{}\_tokens\ âˆ’\ Î¼(token\_length(v))}
that gave \texttt{\%T\textgreater{}0\ â‰ˆ\ 24.3\ \%} on
contaminated-pickle data. The v3 clean-data rebuild adopted the
information-theoretic form \texttt{T\ =\ H\_cond\ âˆ’\ H\_el} codified
in \texttt{src/features.py::t\_tension} (ref:
\texttt{QSF\_PAPER\_DRAFT\_v2\ Â§2.6}, fix F-11); under this definition
\%T\textgreater0 = \textbf{30.3 \%} on the heuristic root extractor and
\textbf{39.7 \%} on CamelTools. All v5+ locked scalars (\texttt{D10},
\texttt{T10} in \texttt{results\_lock.json}) refer to the v3
CamelTools-based form and 39.7 \% is the authoritative value. Readers
comparing to \texttt{docs/old/} manuscripts or pre-v3 JSONs should use
the version-history key above before citing.
\end{quote}

\subsubsection{3.2 Mahalanobis
fingerprint}\label{mahalanobis-fingerprint}

Let Î¼, Î£ be the mean/covariance of 5-D vectors over the band-A Arabic
control pool \emph{excluding the Quran}. Î£ is regularised by a
1Â·10â»â¶ Â· I ridge (unified across Hotelling/HSIC code paths in v5).
Î¦\_M(u) = âˆš((x\_u âˆ' Î¼)áµ€ Î£â»Â¹ (x\_u âˆ' Î¼)).

\subsubsection{3.3 Hotelling TÂ² and permutation
null}\label{hotelling-tuxe2uxb2-and-permutation-null}

Primary band-A statistic: pooled Hotelling TÂ² of \{Quran band-A\} vs
\{Arabic controls band-A\}, nâ‚ = 68, nâ‚‚ = 2 509. Permutation null
N\_PERM = 200 (FAST\_MODE) / 10 000 (full); perm p = (1 + \#\{TÂ²\_perm
â‰¥ TÂ²\_obs\}) / (N\_PERM + 1). Replaces the legacy biased Cohen's d.

\subsubsection{3.4 Nested 5-fold
classifier}\label{nested-5-fold-classifier}

Stratified outer 5-fold (\texttt{random\_state\ =\ 42}); within each
outer fold, features are scaled on inner-train indices only. Logistic
regression (\texttt{class\_weight\ =\ "balanced"}). Reported AUC is mean
across five held-out outer folds. The in-sample AUC in Cell 62 is
explicitly flagged ``DIAGNOSTIC, not blessed''.

\subsubsection{3.5 Pre-registered tests (v10.18 frozen
2026-04-18)}\label{pre-registered-tests-v10.18-frozen-2026-04-18}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Test A} (leave-one-Arabic-family-out Î¦\_M d â‰¥ 1.5): 6 / 6
  splits pass; min d = 5.26. \textbf{PASS}.
\item
  \textbf{Test B} (F\_Meccan \textgreater{} 1.0 AND F\_Medinan
  \textgreater{} 1.0): F\_M = 0.797, F\_D â‰ˆ 0.84. \textbf{FALSIFIED at
  the joint threshold}.
\item
  \textbf{Test C} (â‰¥ 95 \% of 1 000 bootstraps give Î© \textgreater{}
  2.0): 100 \%, median 10.0. \textbf{PASS STRONGER}.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{3.6 FDR correction}\label{fdr-correction}

Benjamini--Hochberg over the permutation-p family gives 7 / 13 survivors
at q â‰¤ 0.05. Full coverage audit:
\texttt{results/integrity/fdr\_coverage\_audit.json}.

\subsubsection{3.7 Integrity locks}\label{integrity-locks}

Five manifests verified at every phase and at paper-build time:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{corpus\_lock.json} --- combined SHA of nine raw corpora.
\item
  \texttt{code\_lock.json} --- combined SHA of 136 notebook code cells.
\item
  \texttt{results\_lock.json} --- combined SHA of 59 locked-scalar
  signatures (57 original + 2 v7.6 6-D Hotelling).
\item
  \texttt{names\_registry.json} --- every \texttt{ULTIMATE\_SCORECARD}
  ID registered ex-ante.
\item
  \texttt{checkpoints/\_manifest.json} (v6) --- per-pickle SHA;
  refuse-to-deserialise on drift.
\end{itemize}

A \texttt{HallucinationError} is raised at Phase 21 if any of the
tolerance-gated scalars in \texttt{results\_lock.json} drifts beyond
per-scalar tolerance, beyond the universal 1Â·10â»â´ absolute lens (v6),
or beyond the Â±5 \% headline baseline envelope (v6).

\subsubsection{3.8 Deprecations}\label{deprecations}

\texttt{D02} / \texttt{S1} / \texttt{D28} (biased Cohen's d) â†'
\textbf{replaced by \texttt{Phi\_M\_hotelling\_T2} +
\texttt{Phi\_M\_perm\_p\_value}}. \texttt{D27} (non-directional Abbasi
discrimination) â†' \textbf{replaced by \texttt{D27\_directional}} (6 /
8 directional beats in favour of the Quran).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{4. Results}\label{results}

\subsubsection{4.1 Multivariate separation
(headline)}\label{multivariate-separation-headline}

Band-A, Quran (nâ‚ = 68) vs pooled Arabic controls (nâ‚‚ = 2 509) across
six non-hadith families:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}

\subsubsection{4.6 Cross-scripture Î¨}\label{cross-scripture-uxee}

The Quran's Î¨ = 3.76 is â‰ˆ 3.1Ã--- the next-ranked Arabic corpus
(poetry\_abbasi Î¨ = 1.23) and â‰ˆ 76Ã--- the hadith (quarantined
reference, Î¨ = 0.05) --- Fig. 4.

\textbf{Scale-sensitivity disclosure.} Raw Î¨ is a composite of terms
with mixed dimensions (Mahalanobis Ïƒ Ã--- probability Ã--- entropy Ã---
CV), and its ranking is not scale-invariant. Under the z-scored
sensitivity variant Î¨\_z (Cell 109,
\texttt{notebooks/ultimate/QSF\_ULTIMATE.ipynb}), which applies a
monotone transform to each input channel before aggregation, the top
rank shifts from Quran to \texttt{ksucca}. We retain raw Î¨ as the
primary descriptive composite because it is the quantity pre-registered
in \texttt{preregistration.json} and because the Mahalanobis-native
Î¦\_M headline (Â§4.1) and the classifier AUC (Â§3.4, Â§4.1) do not
depend on Î¨. The Î¨\_z inversion is a scale artefact of the composite,
not a reversal of the Î¦\_M-based headline; it is reported here for
transparency.

\subsubsection{4.7 Cross-language infeasibility (v6
correction)}\label{cross-language-infeasibility-v6-correction}

The v3--v5 pipeline reported a cross-language Î¨ that depended on a
silent fallback: if the band-A filter returned zero units for Iliad /
Greek-NT / Hebrew-Tanakh, the full corpus was substituted. This fallback
was removed in v6; under the corrected gate all three non-Arabic
scriptures return zero band-A units and are skipped as INFEASIBLE. The
cross-language claim is \textbf{deferred} pending a proper
band-A-matched Greek/Hebrew corpus; it is not supported by the present
run and should not be cited.

\subsubsection{4.8 Information-theoretic
constants}\label{information-theoretic-constants}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{H(harakat \textbar{} rasm) = 1.964 bits} (tol 0.15, PROVED).
  Channel capacity of full vocalisation given the consonantal rasm,
  across the vocalised Quran. Any Arabic NLP system recovering harakat
  from rasm is bounded below by this number.
\item
  \textbf{I(EL; CN) corpus-level = 1.175 bits} (tol 0.10, PROVED).
  Unit-level counterpart \texttt{D05} = 0.100 bits is tight-replicated
  but falsified as a per-unit claim; corpus-level survives.
\end{itemize}

Both are Arabic-textology constants, not Quran-unique, but numerically
stable.

\subsubsection{4.9 Dependency structure (G2 /
HSIC)}\label{dependency-structure-g2-hsic}

Max normalised pairwise MI \texttt{G2\ =\ 0.318} (tol 0.05, PROVED).
Kernel HSIC 5-channel max pair perm p = 0.005 (FDR-surviving). The five
channels are \textbf{jointly informative}, not claimed independent.

\subsubsection{4.10 Long-memory}\label{long-memory}

\texttt{Supp\_A\_Hurst} (R/S) = 0.738, RÂ² = 0.991.
\texttt{Hurst\_DFA\_quran} = 0.901, RÂ² = 0.990. Multi-level Hurst:
letter-seq 0.537 vs EL-seq 0.738 --- long memory at the prosodic-level
scale, not at the letter level.

\subsubsection{4.11 Sparse-PCA
alternative}\label{sparse-pca-alternative}

As a feature-rotation robustness check: sparse-PCA PC1 Cohen's d =
\textbf{4.81}, perm p = \textbf{0.005} (FDR-surviving). The direction of
separation is not dictated by the five-feature axis choice.

\subsubsection{4.12 Adiyat blind test
(updated)}\label{adiyat-blind-test-updated}

The seven-metric blind Adiyat-case test
(\texttt{src/adversarial\_tests.py}) reports the canonical reading
``Ø§Ù„Ø¹Ø§Ø¯ÙŠØ§Øª Ø¶Ø¨Ø\-Ø§Ù‹'' winning 4 of 7 independent metrics
(\texttt{Adiyat\_blind\ =\ 0.5714}, perm p = \textbf{0.070}). This is a
\textbf{weakening} relative to the prior 5/7 claim; the micro-case does
not cross p \textless{} 0.05 at N\_PERM = 200. The underlying
macro-claim it supported (simultaneous maximisation of root diversity
and end-letter rhyme, Â§4.5) is \textbf{stronger} under the current run
(RD Ã--- EL = 0.632 vs 0.179 next-best, 3.5Ã--- margin). Detailed
discussion in \texttt{docs/ADIYAT\_ANALYSIS\_AR.md}. The Î¦\_M
``single-letter ceiling â‰ˆ 2--3 \%'' reported here applies to the
aggregate surah-level Î¦\_M statistic and is \textbf{superseded as a
system-level ceiling} in Â§4.14 (R2 sub-surah amplification).

\textbf{Single-letter Monte-Carlo enumeration (supplementary,
2026-04-20).} To preempt the ``cherry-picked three alternatives''
framing risk, we enumerated \textbf{all 864} single-letter substitutions
of Adiyat verse 1 (32 consonant positions Ã--- 27 alternative Arabic
consonants) and recomputed Î¦\_M for each variant (source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp23\_adiyat\_MC/exp23\_adiyat\_MC.json}).
The defensible reading of this enumeration is: among the subset of
variants that \textbf{actually engage the 5-D channels}, the canonical
is the strict maximum.

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  **Canonical Î¦\_M = 10.286.**
\item
  \textbf{864 total variants}; however, \textbf{836 are
  feature-invariant} (the letter change falls outside the 5-D channels'
  sensitivity window --- verse-final rhyme and connective-first tokens
  are unaffected by mid-verse edits; this is the expected behaviour per
  Â§7 of \texttt{docs/ADIYAT\_ANALYSIS\_AR.md}, and is a known
  limitation of surah-level features, not a property of this specific
  verse).
\item
  \textbf{28 variants are feature-active} (engage EL or H\_cond via
  edits to the verse-first or verse-final word).
\item
  **Of the 28 feature-active variants, 0 exceed the canonical Î¦\_M**;
  the variant minimum is 9.198 (a drop of \textasciitilde11 \% below
  canonical).
\end{itemize}

The weakest defensible statement is: ``no single-letter edit of verse 1
that registers on any 5-D channel increases the Quran-detector score
above the canonical.'' The stronger framing ``canonical at 100th
percentile of 864'' is numerically correct but 97 \% of those 864 are
feature-invariant ties and should not be counted as independent
supporting evidence.

Caveat (v0): the enumeration does not gate for linguistic validity, so
many of the 28 active variants are non-words; a v1 run with a
CamelTools-roots whitelist is scaffolded in
\texttt{experiments/exp23\_adiyat\_MC/notes.md}. The v0 result is
reported descriptively as a direct answer to the three-alternatives
critique, not as a formal edit-detection test.

(appendix)}\label{topological-data-analysis-appendix}

Vietoris-Rips H1 persistent homology on the z-scored band-A 5-D cloud: 0
long-lived loops at 0.25 Ïƒ; bootstrap marginal-shuffle null p = 1.0.
The multivariate outlier claim does \textbf{not} rest on a topological

\subsubsection{4.14 Ultimate-2 edit-detection layer (11 channels,
v7)}\label{ultimate-2-edit-detection-layer-11-channels-v7}

Ultimate-1 is a corpus-level outlier test: given a text, is it in the
Quran cluster? Ultimate-2 is an edit-detection layer: given a canonical
Quranic text and a candidate edit, did an edit occur? The layer consists
of 11 independent channels R1--R11, each with a pre-registered target
and a calibrated rate after two hostile-audit rounds. Primary output:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp20\_MASTER\_composite/ULTIMATE2\_REPORT.json}.

\textbf{Main-body claim.} Of the 11 channels, only two --- \textbf{R2
(sub-surah sliding-window amplification)} and \textbf{R3
(cross-scripture z-test)} --- clear their pre-registered targets
unambiguously. These two channels alone carry the paper's edit-detection
claim. R11 is a near-pass vs classical Arabic poetry only; R1 and R8 are
PARTIAL; R4, R5, R7, R10 FAIL their targets; R9 is REVERSED. The full
11-row table below is retained for audit transparency --- it documents
the calibration discipline of the layer, not the paper's claim strength.

\textbf{Composite upper bound}:
\texttt{P\_detect\_upper\ =\ 1\ âˆ’\ Î~\_i\ (1\ âˆ’\ rate\_i)\ =\ 0.981}
\textbf{is dominated by R2 alone} and is reported here only as an upper
bound under a (deliberately optimistic) channel-independence assumption.
With R2 excluded the composite collapses to R3's \texttt{0.960}; with
both R2 and R3 excluded, the remaining nine channels give a composite
well below 0.50. The paper's edit-detection claim therefore rests on the
two channels that pass independently, \textbf{not} on the 0.981
composite. The layer does not replace the Ultimate-1 Î¦\_M headline; it
\textbf{complements} it by providing per-edit sensitivity at the R2 and
R3 levels.

Architectural invariants (enforced at every cell): (i) no write-access
to \texttt{results\_lock.json} or any Ultimate-1 artefact; (ii)
\texttt{self\_check\_begin()} / \texttt{self\_check\_end()} wraps every
cell with SHA-256 receipts stored in
\texttt{results/integrity/self\_checks/}; (iii) any divergence raises
\texttt{IntegrityError} and halts the notebook. Two audit rounds closed
13 + 5 FATAL and 21 + 8 WARN items before bless (logs archived under
\texttt{archive/audits/}).

\subsubsection{4.16 R3 cross-scripture --- rebuilt from raw corpora,
v7.2}\label{r3-cross-scripture-rebuilt-from-raw-corpora-v7.2}

\textbf{What changed from v7.1.} The v7.1 Â§4.16 table quoted
\texttt{z\_Quran\ =\ âˆ’8.74,\ z\_GreekNT\ =\ âˆ’4.97,\ z\_Tanakh\ =\ âˆ’5.02}
inherited from the v10.3c \texttt{qsf\_breakthrough\_tests.py}
breakthrough pipeline. During the zero-trust audit we discovered that
(a) the source script is \textbf{absent from the current repo} (deleted
during the v3â†'v5â†'v7 cleanup); (b)
\texttt{integrity/corpus\_lock.json} had Hebrew Tanakh and Greek NT
marked \texttt{exists\ =\ false} at never-moved paths
(\texttt{data/corpora/he/tanakh.txt},
\texttt{data/corpora/el/greek\_nt.txt}); (c) the actual corpora are on
disk at different paths --- \texttt{data/corpora/he/tanakh\_wlc.txt}
(Westminster Leningrad Codex, 5.76 MB, SHA-256 \texttt{f317b359…}) and
\texttt{data/corpora/el/opengnt\_v3\_3.csv} (Open Greek NT v3.3, 46.4
MB, SHA-256 \texttt{d2853da4…}). The v7.1 numbers were therefore
\textbf{unreproducible} at the time of v7.1 release. We supersede them
here.

\textbf{Protocol (exp35\_R3\_cross\_scripture\_redo).} Per scripture:
compute the 5-D language-agnostic feature vector (EL, VL\_CV, CN,
H\_cond\_initials, T\_lang) per unit (chapter/surah/book) via
\texttt{raw\_loader.load\_all(include\_cross\_lang\ =\ True)}; z-score
the 5-D matrix within scripture (scale-invariance across alphabets);
compute the Euclidean sum-of-adjacent-distances path cost in the
canonical unit order; null is the empirical distribution of path cost
under N\_PERM = 5 000 random permutations of the unit sequence (SEED =
42). Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp35\_R3\_cross\_scripture\_redo/exp35\_R3\_cross\_scripture\_redo.json}.

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter

BH-pooled \texttt{min\_p\_adj\ =\ 3Â·10â»â´}. Three of four scriptures
survive; the Iliad correctly falls in the null, serving as a
same-alphabet negative control for the Greek NT result.

\textbf{Key reframing (PLEASE READ).} In raw z-magnitude the Quran is
\textbf{not} the strongest optimiser; the \textbf{Hebrew Tanakh is} (z =
âˆ'15.29 vs Quran âˆ'8.92 vs Greek NT âˆ'12.06). The v10.3c Â«Quran
â‰ˆ76 \% stronger than the next scriptureÂ» claim is \textbf{FALSIFIED}
at the new measurement. Under a sample-size correction
\texttt{z\ /\ âˆšn} the ordering flips --- Quran = âˆ'0.84, Greek NT =
âˆ'0.75, Tanakh = âˆ'0.50 --- so on a \textbf{per-unit} basis the Quran
is the most efficient path-minimiser among tested scriptures. This
rescaling is a \textbf{post-hoc} diagnostic and is not pre-registered;
the \textbf{raw z} is the authoritative test statistic.

\textbf{What we claim in v7.2.} All three major Abrahamic scriptures
exhibit statistically significant canonical-order path minimisation
(BH-pooled min\_p\_adj = 0.0003 = 3e-4, well below alpha = 0.001),
falsifying any interpretation that treats path minimality as
Quran-unique. The \textbf{amount} of minimisation, however, differs: raw
z favours Tanakh; per-unit \texttt{z\ /\ âˆšn} favours Quran. A
narrative stylometric text (Iliad) shows no optimisation.
Cross-scripture path minimality is therefore a \textbf{shared
Abrahamic-scripture property}, not a Quran-specific one, contra the
pre-v7.2 framing. This is a genuine weakening of the paper's
cross-scripture rhetoric and is reported as such in Â§5.

\subsubsection{4.17 F6 --- adjacent-verse length coherence (new, d =
+0.877, p =
1.4Â·10â»Â¹Â¹)}\label{f6-adjacent-verse-length-coherence-new-d-0.877-p-1.4uxe210uxe2uxe2uxb9uxe2uxb9}

During the Ultimate-2 Adiyat-audit track, a single new Cohen's-d â‰¥ 0.8
effect was discovered that is not represented in any existing channel:
the Spearman rank-correlation between \texttt{\textbar{}v\_i\textbar{}}
and \texttt{\textbar{}v\_\{i+1\}\textbar{}} (token counts of adjacent
verses within a unit) is systematically higher in the Quran than in the
Arabic-control pool. Cohen's d (Band-A, hadith quarantined) =
\textbf{+0.877}, Mann--Whitney p = \textbf{1.4Â·10â»Â¹Â¹}.
Interpretation: Quranic verses are locally rhythmic in length, even
under the well-known Quran-wide high VL\_CV (i.e., global length
variance is preserved while local step-to-step variance is compressed).
This is a candidate sixth Î¦\_M feature pending two-team external
replication, tracked in
\texttt{archive/audits/ADIYAT\_BREAKTHROUGH\_AUDIT\_2026-04-20.md}.
Until replicated externally, it is reported here but not added to
\texttt{results\_lock.json}.

\textbf{Lag-k extension (supplementary, 2026-04-20, Band-A {[}15, 100{]}
with canonical gate).} F6 was extended to lag-k autocorrelations
(\texttt{results/experiments/exp24\_F6\_autocorr/exp24\_F6\_autocorr.json}):
lag-1 d = \textbf{+0.832} (Mann--Whitney p = 1.7Â·10â»Â¹Â²), lag-2 d =
\textbf{+0.281} (p = 5.8Â·10â»Â³), lag-3 d = +0.182 (p = 5.4Â·10â»Â²,
marginal), lag-4 d = +0.026 (null), lag-5 d = +0.265 (p = 2.2Â·10â»Â²).
The lag-1 value (d = +0.832) aligns within sampling noise with the
audit-reported pipeline T32 value (d = +0.827,
\texttt{archive/audits/ADIYAT\_BREAKTHROUGH\_AUDIT\_2026-04-20.md:41})
and is 0.05 below the audit's headline F6 value (d = +0.877); the
audit's headline uses a slightly different pooling of the control family
and this supplementary run is a Band-A-canonical independent probe.
Reading: F6 is \textbf{primarily a lag-1 phenomenon}; lag-2 carries weak
but significant residual coherence, lag-3 is borderline, lag-4 is null,
and the lag-5 rebound may reflect verse-group periodicity but is not
claimed. The multi-step unification with T12 (Markov-2 bigram
sufficiency) is \textbf{not supported} at the d â‰¥ 0.5 threshold; F6
stands as a one-step length-coherence law.

\subsubsection{4.18 Parsimonious (T, EL) classifier --- matches full-5D
for
detection}\label{parsimonious-t-el-classifier-matches-full-5d-for-detection}

The locked 5-D nested-CV classifier (Â§3.4, D09) reaches AUC = 0.998.
External review (2026-04-20) asked whether the same AUC is achievable
with the two features that depend least on external linguistic
resources: \textbf{T} (an information-theoretic rhyme-tension scalar)
and \textbf{EL} (an end-letter rhyme rate). Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp22\_TxEL\_classifier/exp22\_TxEL\_classifier.json}.

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Protocol}: byte-exact parity with \texttt{\_build.py} Cell 71
  (the locked D09 protocol): outer
  \texttt{StratifiedKFold(5,\ random\_state=SEED)}, inner
  \texttt{StratifiedKFold(3,\ random\_state=SEED+1)} for hyperparameter
  selection, \texttt{StandardScaler} fit inside each inner-train fold
  (no leakage), \texttt{LogisticRegression} C tuned over \{0.01, 0.1,
  1.0, 10.0\}, best-C refit on full outer-train with a fresh scaler and
  evaluated on outer-test.
\item
  Features: \texttt{(T,\ EL)} only --- no VL\_CV, no CN, no H\_cond, no
  CamelTools root analyser, no ARABIC\_CONN stopword list.
\item
  Observed: \textbf{AUC = 0.9979 Â± 0.0018} nested-CV across 5 outer
  folds; N\_quran = 68, N\_ctrl = 2 509 (Band A {[}15, 100{]}, canonical
  gate matching \texttt{\_build.py:1129}).
\item
  Per-fold best C = {[}1.0, 0.01, 0.01, 0.1, 0.1{]} --- moderate
  regularisation preferred.
\item
  Locked 5-D nested-CV baseline: 0.998.
\item
  \textbf{Parsimony gap: \textless{} 0.001 AUC} (below the 0.002
  nested-CV standard deviation).
\end{itemize}

This is a strong Zipf-style parsimony result under identical protocol.
The full 5-D Mahalanobis composite remains the pre-registered headline
and is retained for magnitude estimation (Hotelling TÂ², Cohen d) and
for the Adiyat Monte-Carlo and edit-detection channels that reference
individual features. But the \textbf{detection headline} --- ``can a
held-out surah be classified Quran vs classical-Arabic control'' ---
collapses cleanly to two scalars. A consequence is that the Farasa
root-analyser sensitivity concern flagged in
\texttt{experiments/exp25\_farasa\_sensitivity/notes.md} applies
\textbf{only} to the H\_cond-dependent magnitude claims (H\_cond, T =
H\_cond âˆ' H\_el, and Î¦\_M), \textbf{not} to the classifier headline:
EL uses no root analyser and T's H\_cond dependence is absorbed by the
log-odds boundary the LogReg fits on the (T, EL) plane.

\subsubsection{4.19 Scale-invariant Markov-1 law --- audited across four
scales (partial pass,
v7.1)}\label{scale-invariant-markov-1-law-audited-across-four-scales-partial-pass-v7.1}

External review (2026-04-20) proposed a \textbf{Zipf-class universal
law} in which the Quran exhibits bigram sufficiency at every scale
simultaneously --- character-within-word, verse-boundary root,
verse-length, and surah-order path. We tested this hypothesis directly
by (i) adding a character-scale H\_char\_3/H\_char\_2 test
(\texttt{exp27\_hchar\_bigram}, mirrors T11 protocol at the character
layer) and (ii) assembling all four scales plus the locked
root-Markov-order ratio (T28 H2/H1) into a single 5-row verdict table
(\texttt{exp28\_scale\_invariant\_law},
\texttt{results/experiments/exp28\_scale\_invariant\_law/exp28\_scale\_invariant\_law.json}).
The law requires the Quran to be extremal in the predicted direction at
every scale.

\textbf{Verdict}: \texttt{PARTIAL\_LAW\_HOLDS\_AT\_MAJORITY\_SCALES} (3
/ 5). The uniform universal-law framing is \textbf{not supported}: the
character-scale ratio actively fails, and the root-Markov-order ratio is
in the opposite of the predicted direction. Three scales ---
root-bigram-sufficiency, verse-length coherence, and surah-order path
minimality --- remain Quran-extremal as independently reportable
findings.

As a secondary analysis we computed a \textbf{char-root gap} per corpus
(\texttt{gap\ =\ H\_char\_3/H\_char\_2\ âˆ’\ root\_H3/H2}, both pooled)
to test whether the \emph{ratio} of Markov-1 sufficiency across scales
is itself Quran-specific. The Quran ranks \textbf{4 / 7} on this gap
(\texttt{poetry\_islami} 0.545 \textgreater{} \texttt{poetry\_jahili}
0.541 \textgreater{} \texttt{poetry\_abbasi} 0.514 \textgreater{}
\texttt{quran} 0.492 \textgreater{} \texttt{hindawi} 0.442
\textgreater{} \texttt{ksucca} 0.049 \textgreater{}
\texttt{arabic\_bible} âˆ'0.073). No new fingerprint candidate is
supported from this angle.

Cross-scripture reference: pooled Greek Iliad character-scale
H\_char\_3/H\_char\_2 = \textbf{0.866} (highest of all measured
corpora). The Arabic family therefore uniformly occupies a lower-ratio
regime than Greek; within that regime, the Quran is not extremal.

\subsubsection{4.20 Cascade product-code ceiling --- empirically
falsified for internal-letter edits
(v7.1)}\label{cascade-product-code-ceiling-empirically-falsified-for-internal-letter-edits-v7.1}

External review also proposed a four-channel \textbf{cascade product
code} for single-letter internal substitutions:

\begin{verbatim}
P_composite = 1 âˆ’ Î _k (1 âˆ’ p_k)
\end{verbatim}

with estimated per-channel hit-rates \texttt{p\_L0\ â‰ˆ\ 0.55–0.70},
\texttt{p\_L1\ â‰ˆ\ 0.20}, \texttt{p\_L2\ â‰ˆ\ 0.50},
\texttt{p\_L3\ â‰ˆ\ 0.03} â†' estimated composite \textbf{0.82--0.90}.
We empirically measured all four rates
(\texttt{exp29\_cascade\_product\_code},
\texttt{results/experiments/exp29\_cascade\_product\_code/exp29\_cascade\_product\_code.json}).

Protocol. Generate 1 360 perturbations (68 Band-A Quran surahs Ã--- 20
each) and 4 000 paired ctrl perturbations (200 Band-A Arabic-ctrl units
Ã--- 20 each). Each perturbation replaces a \textbf{non-initial,
non-terminal letter in a non-boundary word of a non-terminal verse} with
a random distinct Arabic consonant from the 28-letter set. Channel
statistics are computed as:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{L0}: \textbar Î''H\_char\textbar{} on the 3-verse window
  containing the edit.
\item
  \textbf{L1}: max
  \texttt{\textbar{}\textbar{}Î”(EL,\ VL\_CV,\ CN,\ H\_cond,\ T)\textbar{}\textbar{}\_M}
  across the 10-verse sliding windows that contain the edit (Mahalanobis
  norm, Arabic-ctrl covariance).
\item
  \textbf{L2}:
  \texttt{\textbar{}\textbar{}Î”f\_surah\textbar{}\textbar{}\_M} on the
  surah-level 5-D feature vector.
\item
  \textbf{L3}:
  \texttt{\textbar{}\textbar{}pert\_f\ âˆ’\ q\_centroid\textbar{}\textbar{}\_M}
  under the canonical Quran centroid.
\end{itemize}

Thresholds come from two nulls: (a) 95th-percentile of natural variation
among unperturbed windows/surahs (conservative) and (b) 95th-percentile
of the \emph{ctrl perturbation} distribution (Quran-specificity).
Results under the ctrl-perturbation null:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\centering

L0 H\_char 3-verse & 0.948 & 0.137 & \textbf{4.9Â·10â»Â³} \\
L1 Î¦\_M 10-verse window & \textbf{0.000} & 0.000 & 1.0 \\
L2 Î¦\_M surah & \textbf{0.000} & 0.000 & 1.0 \\

}

~ L3 p\_any\_move = 1.0 is a definitional artefact (L3 reports a scalar
distance from the centroid, which is non-zero for any canonical surah),
not a detection.

\textbf{Empirical composite} \texttt{P\_composite\_ctrl\ â‰ˆ\ 0.137} vs
feedback estimate \textbf{0.82--0.90}. The product-code framing is
empirically falsified for single-letter internal substitutions.

\textbf{Root cause --- structural blindness.} A direct diagnostic (100
Quran-surah Ã--- 20 perturbations = 2 000 tests in a separate probe, and
68 Ã--- 20 = 1 360 in the main exp29 run) shows that
\texttt{features\_5d} returns a \textbf{byte-exact identical} vector for
every one of these internal perturbations. This is not a measurement
precision issue; it is a mathematical property of the features. EL reads
verse-terminal letters only, CN reads verse-opening words only, VL\_CV
counts words only, and H\_cond uses CamelTools on the verse-final word
only. An internal letter of an internal word of an internal verse falls
outside every one of these sensitivity windows by construction. Even a
\emph{verse-swap} perturbation --- which does change the terminal letter
of one verse --- moves the Mahalanobis norm of the feature delta by only
â‰ˆ 0.18 on average, vs a natural-variation 95th-percentile threshold of
â‰ˆ 9.1 (â‰ˆ 50Ã--- below signal).

\textbf{Consequence for the paper.} The 5-D fingerprint is a
\textbf{corpus-level multivariate-outlier statistic}, as Â§4.1 already
claims; it is \textbf{not} a per-edit error-detector. Any narrative that
implied the locked 5-D pipeline provides statistical redundancy against
internal-letter edits is hereby explicitly retracted (see Â§5). The L0
H\_char signal alone is too weak to sustain the cascade claim (Quran vs
ctrl medians 0.0184 vs 0.0177 per 3-verse window; MW p = 4.9Â·10â»Â³ but
effect size negligible). The Quran's \emph{actual} error-correcting
mechanism is recitation, memorisation and tajweed; these are
oral-transmission properties, not structural-statistical properties, and
were never captured by the 5-D system.

\textbf{What survives.} Corpus-level separation (Â§4.1, Î¦\_M d = 6.66,
AUC = 0.998) is unaffected. R2 sliding-window amplification (Â§4.14)
retains its pre-registered rate of 0.981 \emph{for the class of
perturbations it was calibrated on} (synthetic word-scale edits in
\texttt{exp10\_R2\_sliding\_window}), but that calibration does
\textbf{not} transfer to single-letter internal edits --- the
Adiyat-style Ø¹â†'Øº variant is among the edits the 5-D-based channels
cannot see.

\textbf{R1 9-channel empirical extension (exp30, added v7.1).} To close
the question of whether R1's three \emph{non}-5-D channels (A\_spectral
34Ã---34 letter-transition SVD, C\_bigram\_dist letter-bigram L2, E\_ncd
gzip compression distance) retain sensitivity to the specific
``non-initial / non-terminal letter in non-boundary word of non-terminal
verse'' class, we ran R1's \texttt{nine\_channel\_features} on the exp29
perturbation design (680 Quran + 1 000 ctrl perturbations; source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp30\_cascade\_R1\_9ch/exp30\_cascade\_R1\_9ch.json}).

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lcc@{}}

\textbf{P\_composite across 9 R1 channels = 0.417} (vs 0.137 for Î¦\_M
5-D at Â§4.20's main table; vs 0.82--0.90 feedback estimate). Fire rate
at the R1 decision criterion (â‰¥ 3 channels with \textbar z\textbar{}
\textgreater{} 2): Quran 5.6\%, ctrl 2.4\% --- barely above the 5\% FPR
floor. Every Mann-Whitney
\texttt{p(Q\textbar{}Î”\textbar{}\ \textgreater{}\ ctrl\textbar{}Î”\textbar{})}
is â‰¥ 0.58, meaning \textbf{none of the 9 R1 channels fire more in the
Quran than in the controls under internal perturbations} --- the channel
\emph{is} sensitive to the edit class (non-zero \texttt{p\_ctrl}) but
not Quran-\emph{specific}. R1's locked 0.494 rate from
\texttt{exp09\_R1\_variant\_forensics\_9ch} was calibrated on
any-position swaps including word boundaries; it does not transfer to
the internal-only class.

\textbf{R1 on the Adiyat variants directly.} For the three Adiyat
variants injected into Al-Adiyat verse 1 (exp30 sub-test), channels
firing at \textbar z\textbar{} \textgreater{} 2 vs the exp30 ctrl-null
distribution:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Variant A (Ø¹â†'Øº, internal)}: \textbf{1 / 9} channels ---
  only \texttt{E\_ncd} (gzip). Below the ``â‰¥ 3 fired'' threshold that
  \texttt{docs/ADIYAT\_ANALYSIS\_AR.md} Â§6 row 9 assumes.
\item
  \textbf{Variant B (Ø¶â†'Øµ, terminal)}: \textbf{2 / 9} ---
  \texttt{E\_ncd} + \texttt{G\_root\_trigram}.
\item
  \textbf{Variant C (both)}: \textbf{3 / 9} --- \texttt{E\_ncd} +
  \texttt{G\_root\_trigram} + \texttt{C\_bigram\_dist}.
\end{itemize}

Across all three variants, \texttt{E\_ncd} (gzip normalised compression
distance) is the single channel that consistently fires, suggesting a
Kolmogorov-complexity-class signal that is out-of-model for the
information-theoretic 5-D system. That is a candidate \textbf{R12}
channel; pre-registration and calibration would be a v7.2 item. The
finding does not rescue the cascade composite to the feedback's
0.82--0.90 range --- even R1's 9-channel composite is 0.417, and it is
not Quran-\emph{specific} under internal perturbations (MW all â‰¥
0.58).

An implicit reviewer objection to any 68-unit multivariate-outlier claim
is ``your sample is small; the result is dominated by a handful of

Band-A surahs and asking how far the Hotelling TÂ² degrades. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp31\_subset\_centroid\_stationarity/exp31\_subset\_centroid\_stationarity.json}.

\subsubsection{4.22 5-D topology --- a dense cluster on a continuum, not
a topological island
(v7.2)}\label{d-topology-a-dense-cluster-on-a-continuum-not-a-topological-island-v7.2}

Â§4.1 reports an aggregate Mahalanobis separation (TÂ² = 3 557, d =
6.66). A natural question is whether that separation manifests as a
\textbf{topological island} --- a region of 5-D space that no control
unit enters --- or as a \textbf{dense cluster on a continuum} where
individual control units can sit as close to individual Quran units as
other Quran units do. We test this directly. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp33\_island\_isolation/exp33\_island\_isolation.json}.

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter

  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\centering
Value
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Interpretation
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
max(NND within Quran) & 4.56 & Largest neighbour gap inside the Quran

The strict single-linkage ``island'' hypothesis is \textbf{falsified}.
Aggregated separation (TÂ², d) and local clustering (silhouette, NNR)

neighbour is a control unit are Q:046, Q:022, Q:014, Q:049, Q:034 ---
and in four of the top five the nearest neighbour is a narrative book of
the \textbf{Arabic Bible} (Nehemiah, Joshua, Chronicles), with Q:049
nearest to Abbasid poetry. Interpretation: the Quran's nearest
stylometric neighbours under the 5-D feature space are narrative
Medinan-length texts of similar structural character; the Quran is a
dense cluster in a neighbourhood shared with Bible-narrative and poetry,
not a disconnected manifold.

must operate at the sub-surah scale --- which is exactly what exp29 /
exp30 / R2-sliding-window / E\_ncd address, at mixed success rates.

\subsubsection{4.24 (T, EL) classifier meta-CI across 5 random seeds

Â§4.18 reports AUC = 0.9979 Â± 0.0018 at SEED = 42 (exp22). The Â±0.0018

\texttt{results/experiments/exp36\_TxEL\_seed\_metaCI/exp36\_TxEL\_seed\_metaCI.json}.

\subsubsection{4.25 R12 gzip NCD --- letter-level edit-detection channel
(v7.3,
length-audited)}\label{r12-gzip-ncd-letter-level-edit-detection-channel-v7.3-length-audited}

The v7.1 Ultimate-2 channel bank (Â§4.14) had two edit-detection
channels passing their pre-registered targets (R2, R3) and nine channels
failing, null, or reversed. v7.1 Â§4.20 observed that gzip NCD (the
E\_ncd channel of R1) was the single channel that fired on all three
Adiyat variants despite R1's population-level null (MW p = 1.00 for
E\_ncd on raw-text inputs). v7.3 formalises a \textbf{new}
pre-registered operationalisation of gzip NCD on the 28-letter
consonantal rasm and verifies its length-controlled structural
significance.

\textbf{Protocol (exp41\_gzip\_formalised, v7.3, 2026-04-20 post-hoc
code-state lock).} For each Band-A Quran surah (n=68) and 200
matched-length Band-A Arabic-ctrl units, apply the exp29 internal-edit
policy (non-initial/non-terminal letter in non-boundary word of
non-terminal verse) N\_PERT=20 times per unit (1,360 Quran + 4,000 ctrl
edits total). For each canonical/edited pair compute
\texttt{NCD(canon\_28letter\_stream,\ edited\_28letter\_stream)} via
\texttt{gzip.compress(...,\ compresslevel=9)} and a 3-verse window-scale
analogue. Source: \texttt{results/experiments/exp41\_gzip\_formalised/}.

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lccc@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Measure & Quran & Ctrl & Verdict \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Doc-scale NCD median & 0.0426 & 0.0414 & \\
Doc-scale Cohen d & --- & --- & \textbf{+0.534} (raw) \\
Doc-scale MW p\_greater & --- & --- & \textbf{6.6Â·10â»Â³â¹} \\
Window-scale Cohen d & --- & --- & +0.329 \\
Window-scale MW p\_greater & --- & --- & 4.4Â·10â»Â¹Â³ \\
\end{longtable}
}

\textbf{Critical length audit.} NCD(canon, canon+1edit) is mechanically
dominated by \texttt{const\ /\ Z(canon)}, so shorter documents inflate
the signal. Spearman Ï(NCD, n\_letters) = âˆ'0.52 pooled (p â‰ˆ
10â»Â²Â²â´). The log-linear regression
\texttt{log\ NCD\ =\ Î±\ +\ Î²Â·log(n\_letters)\ +\ Î³Â·I(Quran)} gives:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Length slope Î² = âˆ'0.0719 (SE 0.0019)
\item
  \textbf{Quran indicator Î³ = +0.0716 (95 \% CI {[}+0.066, +0.078{]}, p
  â‰ˆ 0)}
\end{itemize}

The \textbf{paper-grade headline is the empirical edit-detection
residual Î³ = +0.0716} (the regression coefficient with its 95 \% CI;
reported as a reproducible empirical scalar, not a Kolmogorov-theoretic
quantity --- a formal derivation connecting Î³ to compressibility lower
bounds remains open, see Â§8.4 U03); this corresponds to approximately
\textbf{7.4 \% higher NCD per edit at fixed document length} on the
linear scale, which is the form most useful for reader intuition but is
a rounded derivative, not the authoritative scalar. All downstream
citations (DEEPSCAN, RANKED\_FINDINGS, COMPLETE\_REFERENCE) use Î³ =
+0.0716 as the canonical number; the rounded ``â‰ˆ 7.4 \%'' figure is
reserved for prose context. The raw d = +0.534 is the length-confounded
population statistic and must NOT be reported without the length
control. Decile-stratified inspection shows Quran NCD \textgreater{}
ctrl NCD in 9 of 10 letter-count deciles; deciles 6 and 10 are null or
reversed. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp41\_gzip\_formalised/length\_audit.json},
verdict \texttt{GENUINE\_STRUCTURAL\_SIGNAL\_AFTER\_LENGTH\_CONTROL}.

\textbf{R12 is distinct from the locked E\_ncd channel (v7.1 Â§4.20).}
E\_ncd in \texttt{exp09\_R1\_variant\_forensics\_9ch} consumes the raw
diacritic-preserving text, giving the null MW p = 1.00 on internal
edits. R12 consumes the 28-letter consonantal rasm (diacritics stripped,
hamza variants folded, whitespace removed). Both results stand; they
measure different statistics on different inputs. Any citation of R12
must name the input form explicitly.

\textbf{Adiyat direct test.} The three hand-picked Adiyat variants
(Ø¹â†'Øº, Ø¶â†'Øµ, both) all fire R12 at the ctrl-null 95th-percentile
threshold: - Variant A: NCD = 0.0653, z\_ctrl = \textbf{+5.58} - Variant
B: NCD = 0.0653, z\_ctrl = \textbf{+5.58} - Variant C: NCD = 0.0804,
z\_ctrl = \textbf{+9.14}

Important framing: R12 fires on 99.1 \% of all Quran internal
single-letter edits at this threshold. The A/B/C firings are
in-distribution instances of the Quran edit population, NOT
Adiyat-specific detections. The defence against the ``cherry-picked
three'' critique is that all three happen to fire, none is exceptional
--- R12 is a \textbf{population-level Quran-edit detector}, not an
Adiyat-specialised detector.

\textbf{Two structural modulators (v7.8 cross-references, 2026-04-22).}
Two downstream experiments refine the flat-threshold R12 framing without
disturbing the Î³ = +0.0716 headline:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Phonetic-distance modulation} ---
  \texttt{experiments/exp54\_phonetic\_law\_full} (overall\_verdict
  \texttt{LAW\_CONFIRMED}) fits per-emphatic-class detection rate as a
  linear function of the articulatory-Hamming distance between
  substituted consonants:
  \texttt{detection\_rate\ =\ 0.007265\ Â·\ d\_hamming\ âˆ’\ 0.002388},
  Pearson r = 0.929, p = 0.0025, n = 7 classes Ã--- 10 461 edits. The 8
  of 864 Adiyat variants that \emph{fail} to fire R12 at the flat
  ctrl-p95 threshold are predicted by this law to cluster at the
  low-\texttt{d\_hamming} end (emphatic â†'' plain dentals). The
  follow-up \texttt{experiments/exp95\_phonetic\_modulation} executed
  the preregistered stratum-calibrated threshold test and returned
  \textbf{\texttt{FAIL\_ctrl\_stratum\_overfpr}}: it did \textbf{not}
  safely close the residual because the control-stratum false-positive
  requirement failed. Source:
  \texttt{results/experiments/exp54\_phonetic\_law\_full/exp54\_phonetic\_law\_full.json};
  \texttt{results/experiments/exp95\_phonetic\_modulation/exp95\_phonetic\_modulation.json}.
\item
  \textbf{VL\_CV structural floor (Boolean gate)} ---
  \texttt{experiments/exp98\_vlcv\_floor} (overall\_verdict
  \texttt{PASS\_floor\_revised}) tested whether every Band-A Quran surah
  satisfies \texttt{VL\_CV\ â‰¥\ 0.1962} and whether a non-trivial
  fraction of matched-length Arabic controls violate it. Measured:
  \textbf{min(VL\_CV \textbar{} Quran Band-A, n=68) = 0.2683} (the
  addendum-quoted 0.1962 was a loose lower bound; the true empirical
  floor is higher), bootstrap 95 \% CI {[}0.268, 0.298{]} (width 0.030),
  100 \% of Q vs 43.1 \% of 2 509 ctrl surah-equivalents pass the 0.1962
  floor, and Cohen d(Q vs ctrl pool) = \textbf{+1.67}. The 0.1962 gate
  is therefore a \textbf{lossless} Boolean filter on the Quran Band-A +
  an asymmetric 56.9 \% filter on the Arabic-ctrl pool. It adds
  orthogonal information to the 5-D Î¦\_M (which only uses VL\_CV as a
  continuous coordinate, not a floor). Source:
  \texttt{results/experiments/exp98\_vlcv\_floor/exp98\_vlcv\_floor.json}.
\end{itemize}

Both modulators preserve the Â§4.25 Î³ = +0.0716 claim verbatim --- they
refine \emph{thresholds} and add a \emph{Boolean sanity gate}, not the
underlying compression-residual measurement.

\textbf{Compressor-family honesty caveat (exp103, 2026-04-22).}
\texttt{experiments/exp103\_cross\_compressor\_gamma} re-runs the
length-controlled Î³ regression on the identical 5 360-edit perturbation
plan with four universal lossless compressors. All four produce
\textbf{statistically significant} Quran-vs-ctrl separation (each 95 \%
CI excludes zero), but with \textbf{directionally different signs and
compressor-specific magnitudes}:

The cross-compressor coefficient-of-variation is
\texttt{CV(Î³)\ =\ 2.95}, far above the pre-registered ``universal law''
gate of 0.10. \textbf{Î³ = +0.0716 is therefore a gzip-calibrated
edit-detection parameter, not a candidate information-theoretic
constant.} Any claim of the form ``Î³ âˆ K-complexity difference'' is
falsified. The retained claim is the weaker but still substantive:
\emph{``The Quran's 28-letter rasm is structurally distinguishable from
matched-length Arabic controls under every compressor tested (all four p
\textless{} 0.01 at n = 5 360 edits), with the sign of the detection
residual determined by whether the compressor models medium-window
copy-repetition (Î³ \textgreater{} 0: gzip, brotli) or global
statistical structure (Î³ \textless{} 0: zstd-ultra, bzip2).''} This
rebuts the ``Î³ is a Kolmogorov constant'' reading cleanly, closes
\texttt{docs/reference/prereg/PREREG\_GAMMA\_KOLMOGOROV.md} Â§3.1
Theorem 1 as empirically falsified under the pre-registered decision
matrix, and strengthens rather than weakens the honesty posture of the
paper. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp103\_cross\_compressor\_gamma/exp103\_cross\_compressor\_gamma.json},
verdict \texttt{FAIL\_not\_universal}.

\subsubsection{4.26 Adiyat 864-variant compound test

enumerates all 864 single-letter substitutions of Surah 100 verse 1 and
reports detection rates against five detectors. The thresholds for D2/D3

D5 fires on any edit by construction and is reported informationally.

canonical on the 5-D headline statistic.

\textbf{The cleanest statement of the Adiyat compound result:} 99.1 \%
of 864 single-letter variants fire either NCD doc or NCD window at the
exp41 ctrl-p95 threshold (a 5 \% false-positive rate calibrated on 4,000
independent ctrl perturbations). Canonical vs canonical is zero on NCD
by construction and Î¦\_M = canonical by identity, so canonical is the
single configuration that trivially fails to fire any detection. The
honest non-trivial content is that R12 discriminates at pre-registered 5
\% FPR with 99.1 \% sensitivity on internal single-letter edits.

A fuller discussion of what this does and does not solve is at
\texttt{docs/reference/adiyat/ADIYAT\_CASE\_SUMMARY.md}.
