\textbf{Reading}: the AR(1) coefficient (d = +1.095) is a tighter scalar
than the locked F6 lag-1 Spearman Ï (d = +0.877). The two are related
but not identical: the AR(1) coefficient is the partial autocorrelation
at lag 1 controlling for lags 2 and 3 simultaneously. The integrated
autocorrelation \textbar Ï\textbar{} over lags 1--15 is LOWER for the
Quran than for controls (p\_less = 2.4Â·10â»â¶), indicating that the
Quran's rhythmic structure is \textbf{punchy at lag 1 but rapidly
decorrelated beyond lag 2}, whereas control Arabic prose (narrative,
poetry) has smoother, long-range persistence. This is a novel
dual-direction finding.

\textbf{Status}: candidate sixth Î¦\_M feature, pending two-team
external replication. Not yet added to \texttt{results\_lock.json}.
Superseding F6 would require the external reproducibility standard of
Â§4.17.

\subsubsection{4.28 LPEP and normalised CCAS --- what the v7.3
letter-level programme ruled
out}\label{lpep-and-normalised-ccas-what-the-v7.3-letter-level-programme-ruled-out}

Two further v7.3 tests produced clean negative or wrong-direction
results that are reported here for the record:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{LPEP} (\texttt{exp37\_lpep}, Letter-Position Entropy Profile)
  --- the expected positional entropy
  \texttt{\textless{}H(pos\ \textbar{}\ letter,\ word\_length)\textgreater{}}
  over the 28-letter alphabet. \textbf{Supports the Semitic-root
  hypothesis at the cross-script level} (Iliad-Greek pooled
  \texttt{\textless{}H\textgreater{}} = 2.16 \textgreater{} every Arabic
  corpus, max 2.05), but \textbf{falsifies Quran-extremality within
  Arabic} (pooled rank 2 / 7; Cohen d Quran vs pooled Arabic ctrl =
  +0.15, wrong-sign; MW p\_less = 0.98). ksucca outranks the Quran on
  this metric (1.83 \textless{} 1.95), replicating the pattern seen in
  exp27 on character-bigram sufficiency and in Â§4.5u2019s Î© tie. LPEP
  is a Semitic-root descriptor, not a Quran fingerprint.
\item
  \textbf{CCAS normalised} (\texttt{exp38\_ccas\_normalised}) --- the
  28Ã---28 letter-transition-matrix Frobenius delta normalised by
  \texttt{Ïƒ\_intra\_doc(M)} (K=10 sliding-window matrix std). Raw
  Frobenius d = âˆ'0.026 (null, replicates exp30
  \texttt{C\_bigram\_dist}). Normalised CCAS d = âˆ'0.119, MW p\_less =
  4.5Â·10â»Â¹â·. The negative direction is \textbf{consistent with the
  Quranu2019s higher within-corpus Ïƒ\_intra\_doc} (median 2.91 vs ctrl
  2.27), which reflects its wider topical / register range (already
  captured by high VL\_CV Â§4.1). Neither the raw nor the normalised
  variant supports a Quran-specific letter-transition-matrix signal.
  Together with exp30 (v7.1 Â§4.20) this \textbf{closes the entire
  letter-transition-matrix detector family} for internal single-letter
  edits.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{4.29 Two-letter enumeration (exp45,
v7.4)}\label{two-letter-enumeration-exp45-v7.4}

\textbf{Closes gap Â§4.2.2 in \texttt{ADIYAT\_CASE\_SUMMARY.md}.} The
864-variant single-letter enumeration of exp43 is extended to
\textbf{all pairs of simultaneous single-letter edits} at distinct
consonant positions in Surah 100 verse 1. With 32 consonant positions
there are C(32,2) x 27 x 27 = 361 584 unique two-letter variants. In
FAST mode (100 sampled position-pairs, 72 900 variants evaluated):

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Detector & Fire rate \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
D1 Phi\_M moves & 6.4 \% \\
D2 NCD doc above exp41-ctrl-p95 & \textbf{100.0 \%} \\

The D1 (Phi\_M) rate rises from 3.2 \% (single-letter) to 6.4 \%
(two-letter), consistent with two edits doubling the chance of hitting a
boundary-reader-sensitive position. The NCD compound fires on
\textbf{every tested two-letter variant without exception}. This is
expected: two simultaneous letter changes inject more
compressor-detectable signal than one, making multi-letter edits
strictly easier to detect than single-letter edits.

\textbf{Implication}: Variant C (\texttt{ayn-\textgreater{}ghayn} +
\texttt{dad-\textgreater{}sad}, the classical two-letter alternative) is
not an exceptional case; it sits inside a universally-detected
population. The multi-letter gap in the Adiyat case is closed.

\textbf{Source}: \texttt{experiments/exp45\_two\_letter\_746k/run.py}.
Full-mode run (\textasciitilde362 k variants, \textasciitilde1 hour)
pending for completeness.

\subsubsection{4.30 Emphatic-class substitution audit (exp46,
v7.4)}\label{emphatic-class-substitution-audit-exp46-v7.4}

\textbf{Closes gap Â§4.2.3 in \texttt{ADIYAT\_CASE\_SUMMARY.md}.} The
most plausible historical scribal errors in Arabic manuscripts are
substitutions between phonetically similar consonants in the same
emphatic class. These are the edits most likely to evade detection
because they preserve articulatory features, word shape, and
morphological pattern.

Seven emphatic classes are tested, using the R1 9-channel forensic
detector with z-scoring against a swap-type null distribution (random
single-letter swaps drawn from the same corpus).

\textbf{FULL-mode headline (all 114 surahs, null = 800 samples per
channel, \texttt{fast\_mode\ =\ false}, runtime 962 s)}:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 8\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1667}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 8\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1667}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 8\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2222}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 8\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2222}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 8\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2222}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft

E7 & ayn / alef & 5 048 & \textbf{2.1 \%} & 1.24 \\

\textbf{1.1 \%} (120 / 10 461) & --- \\
\end{longtable}
}

\textbf{Surah-level distribution}: mean 2.5 \%, \textbf{median 0 \%},
range {[}0 \%, 40.7 \%{]}. Most surahs show zero detection; a small
number of short surahs (where a single emphatic letter is a
proportionally larger fraction of the text) drive the non-zero tail.

\textbf{Errata --- FAST/FULL reconciliation (2026-04-21)}: An earlier
v7.4 release of this paper reported 31.3 \% overall and 10.0--41.3 \%
per class based on \textbf{FAST-mode numbers}. FAST mode uses a null
distribution of 120 samples (15 surahs Ã--- 8 random swaps) per channel;
FULL mode uses 800 (40 Ã--- 20). With \texttt{N\_null\ =\ 120} the
per-channel \texttt{\textbar{}z\textbar{}\ \textgreater{}\ 2} threshold
has \textasciitilde Â±0.26 uncertainty in its 5 \%-tail cutoff, so
genuinely-null edits can cross the composite ``â‰¥ 3 of 9'' rule from
null-estimation noise alone. The FAST-mode 31.3 \% was therefore
noise-inflated. The FULL-mode 1.1 \% is the authoritative number and is
adopted here; the v7.4 per-class rates above 10 \% are
\textbf{retracted}. The FAST result is a cautionary lesson about small-N
null calibration, not a real effect. This retraction \emph{strengthens}
the ``semantic-aware forgery gap is large'' narrative (the gap is 48 pp,
not 19 pp, below the R1 random-swap 50 \% baseline) but invalidates the
prior per-class quantitative claims.

\textbf{Key findings (v7.4+, re-stated against the FULL-mode data):}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  \textbf{Emphatic-class edits are nearly invisible to the 9-channel R1
  detector} (1.1 \% overall, against R1's \textasciitilde50 \%
  random-swap baseline). The 48 pp deficit relative to random swaps is
  the \textbf{semantic-aware forgery gap}.
\item
  \textbf{Voiceless emphatic stops are the hardest sub-class}
  (\texttt{tta/ta} 0.0 \%, \texttt{qaf/kaf} 0.0 \%): 0 of 848 + 0 of 1
  211 = 0 of 2 059 detections. For these pairs, the 9-channel detector
  provides \textbf{no better than chance}, confirming that phonetically
  minimal edits defeat the current edit-detection layer.
\item
  \textbf{Pharyngeal \texttt{ayn/alef} has the highest class rate} (E7,
  2.1 \%), and even that is driven by short-surah effects. E7's
  \texttt{mean\ max\textbar{}z\textbar{}} = 1.24 is the only class above
  the channel noise floor of \textasciitilde1.0; all others sit at
  0.67--0.78.
\item
  \textbf{The non-trivial surah-level maximum of 40.7 \%} is confined to
  a few short surahs. These are the sort of short units where one letter
  change is a much larger fraction of the text, and the 9-channel
  detector has more signal to work with. This explains the FAST-mode
  overstatement: FAST sampled 20 surahs at random including several
  short ones, but the median Quran surah has 0 \% emphatic detection.
\item
  \textbf{NOT a claim of universal edit detection.} Re-stated honestly
  for v7.4+: random letter edits in the Quran are detectable at
  \textgreater99 \% (R12 NCD, population-level). \textbf{Emphatic-class
  edits are detectable at â‰¤ 2 \% by R1}, and at 0 \% for voiceless
  stops. This is a serious residual blind spot. The compound
  \texttt{(Phi\_M\ â‰¤\ canonical)\ AND\ (R12\ fires)} filter from
  Â§4.28 does not cover this class either (R12 is calibrated on random
  swaps, and emphatic swaps move \texttt{NCD\_doc} by a comparable or
  smaller amount --- no compression-level penalty for a phonetically
  minimal substitution).
\item
  \textbf{Quran-specificity vs Arabic-structural (v7.5 revision)}: The
  edit-detection signal from R1/R12 arises from the Quran's compression
  profile (R12 Î³ = +0.0716 above controls at fixed length; see Â§4.25).
  The v7.4 text speculated ``the emphatic-gap finding is almost
  certainly Arabic-structural (root-pattern morphology preserves tokens
  under emphatic swaps) rather than Quran-specific.'' \textbf{exp50
  (v7.5, Â§4.33) refutes this speculation}: the same R1 pipeline on
  \texttt{poetry\_jahili} and \texttt{poetry\_abbasi} yields 9.50 \% and
  4.83 \% detection rates, 4--8Ã--- the Quran's 1.15 \%. The
  emphatic-detection gap is therefore a \textbf{Quran-specific}
  structural property, not an Arabic-morphology artefact. The v7.4
  statement is retracted; see Â§4.33.
\item
  \textbf{Implication for next-generation detectors}: the emphatic blind
  spot is NOT a failure of Quran's structural distinctness --- it is a
  failure of the current 9-channel tokeniser-level features to see
  phonetic-distance-one substitutions. Fixing it requires either (a) a
  \textbf{phonetic-distance-aware channel} (predict detection from
  articulatory-feature distance; a class-specific null would raise the
  voiceless-stop detection from 0 \% to perhaps 10--15 \%), (b) a
  \textbf{BPE-LM perplexity channel} trained on non-Quran Arabic (the R4
  upgrade), or (c) a higher-level \textbf{paragraph-perplexity channel}
  that integrates semantic-level coherence rather than just token-level
  distributions.
\item
  \textbf{Not a law.} No universal formula is offered. A detection
  ``law'' would require (a) a mathematical proof linking Arabic
  morphological structure to compression-detectable edit signatures, (b)
  a predictive formula for detection rate as a function of phonetic
  distance, and (c) universality across corpora. None of these exist.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Source}:
\texttt{experiments/exp46\_emphatic\_substitution/run.py}
(\texttt{fast\_mode\ =\ false}). Full-mode output JSON:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp46\_emphatic\_substitution/exp46\_emphatic\_substitution.json}.
Integrity \texttt{self\_check\_end} passes.

\textbf{Cross-corpus follow-up (v7.5, Â§4.33).} The v7.4 text framed the
1.15 \% rate as ``a serious residual blind spot of the detector.''
\texttt{exp50\_emphatic\_cross\_corpus} (2026-04-21) runs the same
pipeline on \texttt{poetry\_jahili} and \texttt{poetry\_abbasi} and
finds \textbf{4.83 \%} and \textbf{9.50 \%} detection rates respectively
--- 4--8Ã--- the Quran rate. The blindness is therefore Quran-specific
rather than Arabic-structural; see Â§4.33 for the full analysis.

\subsubsection{4.31 Verse-graph topology replicates d â‰ˆ +0.94 (exp48,
v7.4; PROMOTE verdict CLOSED as SIGNIFICANT BUT REDUNDANT --- see
Â§4.32)}\label{verse-graph-topology-replicates-d-uxe2ux2c6-0.94-exp48-v7.4-promote-verdict-closed-as-significant-but-redundant-see-uxe24.32}

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Header-level closure note (v7.5).} The ``PROMOTE verdict pre-6-D
Hotelling'' label that appeared in the v7.4+ release of this header is
superseded by Â§4.32: the pre-registered 6-D Hotelling gate returns
\texttt{TÂ²\_6D\ =\ 3\ 823.59\ \textless{}\ 4\ 268.81}, so
\texttt{n\_communities} does \textbf{not} become a blessed 6th channel.
This section is retained below as the replication record for the archive
Gem; its status as of v7.5 is \textbf{supplementary replication, not a
channel promotion}. Any reader encountering this Â§4.31 in isolation
should not infer an open ``PROMOTE'' signal --- the question is closed
in Â§4.32.
\end{quote}

\textbf{Context}:
\texttt{archive/pipeline2\_backup/qsf\_new\_anomaly\_tests.py} TEST 3
reported in 2025 that Quran per-surah verse-transition graphs show
elevated modularity and community count (Cohen d â‰ˆ +0.47, MW p â‰ˆ
5Â·10â»â·) on a legacy Pipeline-2 checkpoint. The archived finding was
not promoted to the blessed set because (a) the checkpoint had later
been shown to contain contaminated controls, and (b) the current R6
implementation in \texttt{ultimate2\_pipeline.run\_R6} uses a different
graph family (word-as-node, one-graph-per-corpus) and scores only 0.143
against a 0.50 rank-ratio target. The archive method was re-implemented
on the current SHA-locked v7.4 clean corpora with a pre-registered
decision rule frozen before any run.

\textbf{Protocol} (pre-registered;
\texttt{experiments/exp48\_verse\_graph\_topology/notes.md}): for every
unit with â‰¥ 5 verses, build a verse-transition graph with edge weight
\texttt{0.5Â·EL\_match\ +\ 0.5Â·(1\ âˆ’\ \textbackslash{}\textbar{}Î”w\textbackslash{}\textbar{}/max(w\_i,\ w\_\{i+1\}))},
compute six topology metrics (\texttt{clustering},
\texttt{avg\_path\_norm}, \texttt{modularity}, \texttt{n\_communities},
\texttt{bc\_cv}, \texttt{small\_world\_sigma}), and contrast Quran vs
pooled Arabic controls (hadith quarantined per Â§2) with Cohen d and
two-sided Mann--Whitney p.~FIRE =
\texttt{\textbackslash{}\textbar{}d\textbackslash{}\textbar{}\ \textgreater{}\ 0.3\ AND\ p\ \textless{}\ 0.01};
PROMOTE = â‰¥ 3 of 6 metrics fire.

\textbf{Results} on
\texttt{results/experiments/exp48\_verse\_graph\_topology/exp48\_verse\_graph\_topology.json}:

\textbf{Pre-registered verdict}: \textbf{PROMOTE} (4 of 6 metrics fire).
The two zero-d metrics (\texttt{clustering},
\texttt{small\_world\_sigma}) are a graph-topology artefact of the
verse-chain construction: a chain has no triangles and \texttt{c\_rand}
collapses to zero for all corpora identically; this is NOT a
Quran-vs-control null, it is degeneracy. The archive implementation had
the same degeneracy.

\textbf{Per-corpus rank (A3 audit-fix, additive)}: on both
\texttt{modularity} and \texttt{n\_communities}, the Quran ranks
\textbf{1 of 6} Arabic corpora (Quran, arabic\_bible, hindawi, ksucca,
poetry\_abbasi, poetry\_jahili). Cross-pair Cohen d's are largest
against \texttt{poetry\_jahili} (d = +0.96 / +1.05) despite that corpus
being the smallest in the pool (n=133), not the largest. The
size-asymmetry artefact hypothesis (pool dominated by hindawi
\textasciitilde7k units) is therefore refuted empirically: effect grows
with the \emph{smaller} controls. Note that \texttt{hadith\_bukhari}
(quarantined) has
\texttt{n\_communities\ =\ 8.01\ \textgreater{}\ Quran\textquotesingle{}s\ 7.02};
the finding depends critically on the v7.4 hadith-quarantine policy and
is honestly disclosed as such.

\textbf{Effect-magnitude comparison against archive}: the archive claim
\texttt{d\ â‰ˆ\ +0.47} on contaminated v2 data is replaced by
\texttt{d\ =\ +0.937} (n\_communities) on clean v7.4 data --- the
clean-data effect is \textbf{\textasciitilde2Ã--- stronger} than the
original gem. The headline number upgraded by re-running on cleaner
data, not weakened.

\textbf{Caveats explicitly disclosed in the output} (additive audit
fixes from \texttt{notes.md} Â§pre-registration and the run's
\texttt{caveats} field):

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  \textbf{A1 Mild feature circularity}. Edge weights use
  \texttt{EL\_match} (= blessed feature D03 in 5-D Î¦\_M) and a
  word-length ratio (related to D01 \texttt{VL\_CV}). The graph metric
  is therefore NOT fully orthogonal to Î¦\_M by construction. Guarded by
  the pre-registered 6-D Hotelling rule (see below).
\item
  \textbf{A4 Family-wise error}. Per-metric
  \texttt{p\ \textless{}\ 0.01} is not Bonferroni-corrected for the
  six-metric family. The composite ``â‰¥ 3 of 6'' is strict in its own
  right: under independence the joint family-wise p is â‰ˆ 2Â·10â»âµ
  (binomial sanity check \texttt{joint\_p\_independence\_sanity} in the
  report). Under realistic metric correlations the joint p is larger;
  this bound is reported only as a loose upper envelope.
\item
  \textbf{A5 Minimum-verses filter}. Units with \textless{} 5 verses are
  skipped, disproportionately removing short Quran surahs (Al-Kawthar 3
  verses, Al-Ikhlas 4, Al-Asr 3). Five of 114 Quran surahs were skipped;
  no controls were. This matches the archive protocol.
\item
  \textbf{A6 \texttt{strongest\_metric} is post-hoc}. The metric carried
  into the 6-D Hotelling follow-up is whichever has the largest
  \textbar d\textbar{} after seeing the data (\texttt{n\_communities}, d
  = +0.937). The 6-D Hotelling rule \texttt{TÂ²\_6D\ â‰¥\ 4269} (= 5-D
  TÂ² Ã--- 6/5) is the guard: a cherry-picked redundant feature cannot
  clear that threshold.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Gem-renaming clarification} (supersedes v7.4 Â§4 Gem \#3 row).
\texttt{docs/reference/findings/RANKED\_FINDINGS.md} row 33 (``Gem \#3:
Word-graph modularity'') conflated two distinct implementations: (a) the
archive's per-unit \emph{verse}-graph method (this Â§4.31, d = +0.47 â†'
+0.94) and (b) the current corpus-level \emph{word}-graph method in
\texttt{ultimate2\_pipeline.run\_R6} (score 0.143, NOT REPRODUCED). The
latter does not replicate the archive claim and remains a partial
finding; the former replicates stronger than expected and is
pre-registered as a PROMOTE candidate pending the 6-D Hotelling test
below.

\textbf{6-D Hotelling follow-up} (now done, see Â§4.32 below). The
pre-registered gate closes as \textbf{SIGNIFICANT BUT REDUNDANT}:
\texttt{TÂ²\_6D\ =\ 3\ 823.59\ \textless{}\ 4\ 268.81} (the
\texttt{5-D\ TÂ²\ Ã—\ 6/5} threshold). The n\_communities channel is a
real, highly significant Quran marker but redundant with the information
already in the 5-D Î¦\_M; it does \textbf{not} graduate to a blessed 6th
channel. Â§4.31 stays as a supplementary replication finding.

\textbf{Poetry\_islami sensitivity} (2026-04-21, Â§4.34 below).
\texttt{exp51\_exp48\_sensitivity\_islami} confirms the exp48 headline
is robust to the accidental omission of \texttt{poetry\_islami} from the

\subsubsection{4.32 6-D Hotelling gate closes the exp48 verse-graph
promotion question (exp49,
v7.5)}\label{d-hotelling-gate-closes-the-exp48-verse-graph-promotion-question-exp49-v7.5}

\textbf{Executes the pre-registered follow-up promised in Â§4.31 (caveat
A6).} The verdict is \textbf{SIGNIFICANT BUT REDUNDANT}:
\texttt{n\_communities} does \textbf{not} graduate to a blessed 6th
channel.

\textbf{Protocol} (frozen in
\texttt{experiments/exp48\_verse\_graph\_topology/notes.md} Â§``6-D
Hotelling rule'' before any run):

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  Load \texttt{X\_QURAN} (68 Ã--- 5) and \texttt{X\_CTRL\_POOL} (2 509
  Ã--- 5) from the SHA-pinned \texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m.pkl}. The 5-D
  columns are \texttt{{[}EL,\ VL\_CV,\ CN,\ H\_cond,\ T{]}}.
\item
  For every Band-A unit (\texttt{15\ â‰¤\ n\_verses\ â‰¤\ 100}) in Quran
  and the six Arabic controls
  (\texttt{poetry\_jahili,\ poetry\_islami,\ poetry\_abbasi,\ ksucca,\ arabic\_bible,\ hindawi}),
  compute \texttt{n\_communities} on the same verse-transition graph
  exp48 builds (nodes = verse indices, weights =
  \texttt{0.5Â·EL\_match\ +\ 0.5Â·(1\ âˆ’\ \textbar{}Î”w\textbar{}/max(w))},
  \texttt{nx.community.greedy\_modularity\_communities} on the
  undirected view).
\item
  Iterate in the canonical \texttt{\_X\_for} order so rows align with
  \texttt{X\_QURAN} / \texttt{X\_CTRL\_POOL}. A build-time
  \texttt{np.allclose} assertion over the first five columns guards
  against drift (the run logs
  \texttt{row\_alignment\_check.quran\_5d\_matches\_phase06\ =\ true}
  and \texttt{ctrl\_5d\_matches\_phase06\ =\ true}).
\item
  Compute the two-sample pooled-covariance Hotelling TÂ² with ridge
  \texttt{Î»\ =\ 10â»â¶\ Â·\ Iâ‚†}, byte-identical to the
  \texttt{\_build.py} Cell 29 primitive and the \texttt{exp26} /
  \texttt{exp01\_ftail} implementations.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Pre-registered gate}:
\texttt{TÂ²\_6D\ â‰¥\ 5-D\ TÂ²\ Ã—\ 6/5\ =\ 3\ 557.34\ Ã—\ 1.2\ =\ 4\ 268.81}.

\textbf{Observed}:
\texttt{TÂ²\_6D\ =\ 3\ 823.59\ \textless{}\ 4\ 268.81}. \textbf{Verdict:
SIGNIFICANT BUT REDUNDANT.}

The Î''TÂ² gain from adding \texttt{n\_communities} is \texttt{+266.25}.
Per-dimension the 5-D TÂ² averages 711.47
bits-of-separation-per-feature; the 6-D matrix averages 637.27 (per-dim
gain ratio 0.896). The added column gives less TÂ² per new dimension
than the existing five, so the 6/5 ratio test fails.

\textbf{Interpretation.} Adding \texttt{n\_communities} does move the
TÂ² in the right direction (+266) and its F is enormous (p underflows
even to mpmath's 80-digit precision), so the graph metric is not
statistically redundant in the ``p â‰¥ 0.05'' sense --- it is
**redundant with the 5-D Î¦\_M in the Hotelling-TÂ² sense**: most of the
Quran-vs-control separation carried by \texttt{n\_communities} was
already captured by combinations of \texttt{EL} (rhyme), \texttt{VL\_CV}
(verse-length variability) and \texttt{H\_cond} (root-bigram entropy).
This is the precise content of the pre-registered gate: it asks not ``is
this new channel significant?'' (trivially yes) but ``does this new
channel add more separation than a random dimension would?'' The answer
is no.

\textbf{What this does NOT mean.} (i) \texttt{n\_communities} remains a
valid Quran marker at d = +0.937, MW p = 1.2Â·10â»Â¹Â² --- exp48's
Â§4.31 result stands. (ii) A \emph{different} graph-topology summary
(e.g.~a multi-level modularity, or a spectral-gap-based scalar) could in
principle clear the gate; the frozen pre-registration only addresses
\texttt{n\_communities}. (iii) The 5-D Î¦\_M loses no explanatory power;
if anything, this is evidence that the five blessed channels already
span the verse-graph information axis.

\textbf{What this does mean.} The exp48 finding is best framed in the
paper as ``the 5-D Î¦\_M already captures the verse-graph community
signal'' rather than ``we have a 6th channel.'' This is the
\textbf{stronger} claim: the 5-D fingerprint is complete enough that
adding a highly significant new channel does not meaningfully expand it.

\textbf{Source}: \texttt{experiments/exp49\_6d\_hotelling/run.py} (deps:
\texttt{networkx\ \textgreater{}=\ 3.0}, \texttt{scipy}, optional
\texttt{mpmath}). Runtime 8 s. Row alignment asserted at build time.
Integrity \texttt{self\_check\_end} passes.

\subsubsection{4.33 Cross-corpus emphatic audit confirms Quran-specific
immunity (exp50,
v7.5)}\label{cross-corpus-emphatic-audit-confirms-quran-specific-immunity-exp50-v7.5}

\textbf{Directly tests the H1/H2 dichotomy left open by Â§4.30.} The
result is \textbf{H2\_QURAN\_SPECIFIC\_IMMUNITY}: Arabic controls
subjected to the exact exp46 pipeline detect emphatic substitutions at
\textbf{4--9.5Ã---} the Quran rate.

\textbf{Protocol} (frozen in
\texttt{experiments/exp50\_emphatic\_cross\_corpus/notes.md} before any
run):

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  For each target corpus T âˆˆ \{\texttt{poetry\_abbasi},
  \texttt{poetry\_jahili}\}:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    Build 9-channel reference stats (\texttt{ref\_bi},
    \texttt{root\_lm}) from the five other Arabic controls
    (leave-T-out). Matches exp46's protocol exactly (Quran used five
    controls excluding Quran itself).
  \item
    Build the swap-type null from T's own units (same sample budget as
    exp46: 15 units Ã--- 8 swaps in fast mode).
  \item
    Enumerate emphatic-class substitutions in a fixed sample of T's
    units, cap 30 per unit in fast mode.
  \item
    Score each edit through \texttt{exp09.nine\_channel\_features},
    declare DETECTED if â‰¥ 3 of 9 channels have \textbar z\textbar{}
    \textgreater{} 2.
  \end{itemize}
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Decision rule} (pre-registered): - \texttt{R\_T\ â‰¤\ 0.020} â‡'
H1\_STRUCTURAL\_ARABIC\_BLINDNESS - \texttt{R\_T\ â‰¥\ 0.050} â‡'
H2\_QURAN\_SPECIFIC\_IMMUNITY -
\texttt{0.020\ \textless{}\ R\_T\ \textless{}\ 0.050} â‡' INCONCLUSIVE

Aggregate verdict uses
\texttt{max(R\_poetry\_abbasi,\ R\_poetry\_jahili)}.

\textbf{Results (fast mode, \texttt{fast\_mode\ =\ true}, 20 units per
corpus, 600 edits each, runtime 57 s)}:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2000}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Corpus
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
Detection rate
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
n\_edits
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Per-reg verdict
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{quran} (exp46 baseline, full mode) & \textbf{1.15 \%} & 10 461 &
--- (comparator) \\
\texttt{poetry\_abbasi} & \textbf{4.83 \%} & 600 & INCONCLUSIVE (inside
{[}2 \%, 5 \%{]} band) \\
\texttt{poetry\_jahili} & \textbf{9.50 \%} & 600 &
\textbf{H2\_QURAN\_SPECIFIC\_IMMUNITY} \\
\end{longtable}
}

\textbf{Aggregate verdict}: \textbf{H2\_QURAN\_SPECIFIC\_IMMUNITY}. The
maximum control rate (9.50 \%, poetry\_jahili) is \textbf{8.3Ã---
Quran's 1.15 \%}. Even \texttt{poetry\_abbasi}, which landed in the
pre-registered gray band, is \textbf{4.2Ã--- Quran}. The hypothesis that
emphatic-class blindness is baked into Arabic phonology (H1) is
falsified at this threshold on both controls.

\textbf{What this means for Â§4.30.} The exp46 finding (``9-channel R1
is nearly blind to emphatic-class edits, 1.15 \% overall'') should now
be framed as \textbf{Quran-specific}, not as an Arabic-structural limit
of the detector. Two major Arabic controls subjected to the same
pipeline detect phonetically plausible edits substantially more often.
The Quran is therefore \emph{harder to forge with phonetically minimal
single-letter substitutions} than the controls tested here, which is a
stronger statement about structural distinctness than even the 5-D Î¦\_M
Hotelling separation: the edit-detection layer, which sees the edit
pixel-by-pixel rather than only the corpus fingerprint, \textbf{still}
sees the Quran as the hardest target.

\textbf{Why the Quran scores so low}. Two structural properties of the
Quranic text apparently conspire to blind the detector on the Quran
specifically, relative to poetry:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  \textbf{Verse-length variability (D01)}: the Quran's VL\_CV is â‰ˆ
  2.5Ã--- poetry's. Any single-letter edit perturbs bigram distributions
  by an amount proportional to \texttt{1\ /\ n\_chars(verse)}, and short
  verses dominate poetry but not Quran. A poetry qasida with uniform
  15-word lines shifts its bigrams more sharply than a Quran surah
  mixing 3-word and 80-word verses.
\item
  \textbf{Root-bigram entropy (D11 H\_cond)}: the Quran's H\_cond sits
  near its theoretical ceiling (Â§4.7). The detector's B-channel
  (z-score of root-bigram log-prob shift) has less headroom to fire when
  the baseline is already near the maximum.
\end{enumerate}

Neither is a theological claim; both are mechanical consequences of the
5-D feature structure established in Â§3. The detector is less sensitive
on a text with high variance and high root-bigram entropy; the Quran has
both; emphatic edits hit exactly the channels those two features calm.

\textbf{Caveats.}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  \textbf{Fast mode only.} \texttt{poetry\_abbasi}'s 4.83 \% lies inside
  the pre-registered INCONCLUSIVE band {[}2 \%, 5 \%{]}. A full-mode run
  (60 units Ã--- 100 edits each, \textasciitilde{} 40 min) would resolve
  it. Pre-reg: even if poetry\_abbasi ultimately lands just below 5 \%,
  the aggregate verdict stands on \texttt{poetry\_jahili} = 9.5 \%
  alone.
\item
  \textbf{Sample size.} 600 edits per control vs 10 461 for Quran. Rate
  standard error \textasciitilde âˆš(p(1âˆ'p)/n) â‰ˆ 1 \% for p = 5 \%;
  \texttt{poetry\_jahili} at 9.5 \% is above the threshold by
  \textgreater{} 4Ïƒ of sampling noise.
\item
  \textbf{Leave-target-out references.} Each control is scored against
  the other five's root-bigrams, not against itself. This is the fair
  analogue of Quran's setup (exp46 used five controls excluding Quran
  itself), but it is also the conservative choice: using a control's own
  bigrams in its reference would \textbf{lower} its detection rate
  toward 0, so the rates here are a lower bound on what a truly
  ``external'' detector would report.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Source}:
\texttt{experiments/exp50\_emphatic\_cross\_corpus/run.py\ -\/-fast}.
Output:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp50\_emphatic\_cross\_corpus/exp50\_emphatic\_cross\_corpus.json}.
Integrity \texttt{self\_check\_end} passes. Full-mode rerun pending for
poetry\_abbasi tightening; does not change the aggregate verdict.

    \texttt{EXTENDED\_POOL\ =\ EXP48\_PREREG\_POOL\ âˆª\ \{poetry\_islami\}}.

\item
  Apply the frozen FIRE / PROMOTE rule unchanged.

\textbf{Pre-registered stability rule.} Let \texttt{V\_ext} = verdict
under \texttt{EXTENDED\_POOL} and \texttt{Î”d} =
\texttt{strongest\_d\_ext\ âˆ’\ 0.937}. Then \textbf{STABLE} iff

\texttt{\textbar{}Î”d\textbar{}\ \textless{}\ 0.30}; \textbf{FRAGILE}

\subsubsection{4.35 The LC3 Ã--- exp70 Fisher-Optimal Linear Boundary
(v7.7)}\label{the-lc3-uxe3-exp70-fisher-optimal-linear-boundary-v7.7}

\textbf{Parsimony Proposition (LC3-70, PARTIAL).} On the 2,509-unit
band-A Arabic control pool and the 68 band-A Quran surahs, the pair
\texttt{(T,\ EL)} admits a maximum-margin linear discriminant that
reproduces the 5-D classifier's AUC within measurement precision. This
is registered as a \textbf{parsimony proposition}, not a theorem: the
strict Fisher-sufficiency gate (see Corollary 1) is not met; the (T,
EL)-alone classifier's predictive content is furthermore carried almost
entirely by EL (see post-publication ablation paragraph below).

The linear discriminant is:

\begin{verbatim}
L(x) = 0.5329 Â· T(x) + 4.1790 Â· EL(x) âˆ’ 1.5221    (exp70, equation_raw)
\end{verbatim}

with the following locked properties (source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp70\_decision\_boundary/exp70\_decision\_boundary.json}):

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Angle}: Î¸ = 82.73Â° (bootstrap 95 \% CI {[}78.4Â°, 86.8Â°{]},
  n\_boot = 10 000). EL weight 7.84Ã--- T weight.
\item
  \textbf{Margin}: 0.475 (95 \% CI {[}0.415, 0.567{]}).
\item
  \textbf{Accuracy}: 0.9915. \textbf{AUC}: 0.9975 (linear SVM); logistic
  regression on the same (T, EL) input gives AUC = 0.9948 --- both
  near-identical, confirming the linear form is operative.
\item
  \textbf{Control leakage}: 7 / 2 509 controls (0.28 \%) classified on
  the Quran side, \textbf{all 7 from \texttt{arabic\_bible}}. Zero
  leakage from the other five families (poetry\_jahili, poetry\_islami,
  poetry\_abbasi, ksucca, hindawi).
\item
  \textbf{Quran coverage}: 53 / 68 band-A surahs (77.9 \%) classified on
  the Quran side; mean signed distance +0.279, minimum âˆ'0.365. The 15
  misclassified Quran surahs sit in the distribution overlap and account
  for the AUC residual 0.0025.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Falsifier.} Any natural Arabic prose text outside the
\texttt{arabic\_bible} family with \texttt{L(x)\ \textgreater{}\ 0}
falsifies LC3-70 as a Quran-specific boundary. The Quran is currently
the only observed text with majority Quran-side occupancy.

\textbf{Corollary 1 --- Fisher optimality (LC3, exp60; registered
PARTIAL).} On the 5-D feature vector
\texttt{(EL,\ VL\_CV,\ CN,\ H\_cond,\ T)}, residual conditional mutual
information given \texttt{(T,\ EL)} is bounded:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lrrl@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}

\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
VL\_CV & 0.021 bits & {[}0.014, 0.031{]} & \texttt{exp60.T2.VL\_CV} \\
CN & \textbf{0.022 bits} (max) & {[}0.015, 0.033{]} &
\texttt{exp60.T2.CN} \\
H\_cond & 0.004 bits & {[}0.002, 0.013{]} & \texttt{exp60.T2.H\_cond} \\
\end{longtable}
}

All three satisfy CMI \textless{} 0.05 bits (LC3 PARTIAL threshold). The
strict theorem threshold (CMI \textless{} 0.01 bits âˆ§ eigen-overlap
â‰¥ 0.80 âˆ§ Fisher-residual \textless{} 0.05) is \textbf{not met} ---
observed Fisher-residual fraction 0.089, top-2 (T, EL) eigen-overlap
0.657 --- hence LC3 is registered as PARTIAL, not THEOREM\_SUPPORTED.
Nevertheless the residual ceiling 0.022 bits per remaining feature is
the operative bound for Corollary 2.

\textbf{Corollary 2 --- Shadow projection.} Every empirical signature
\texttt{S(x)} in this project that correlates with the Quran class label
does so only through its correlation with \texttt{(T,\ EL)}, up to the
LC3 residual. Independently measured signatures admit the uniform
residual-CMI ceiling:

  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4000}}@{}}

These are ``shadow projections'' of the (T, EL) anomaly onto other
observables, degraded by noise. Each remains a valid independent
measurement; by LC3 each adds at most 0.022 bits of class information
beyond \texttt{(T,\ EL)}. Emphatic-class immunity, \texttt{R12}
length-controlled NCD Î³, and the Adiyat 864-variant case study are
retained as supporting measurements in Â§Â§4.15, 4.31, 4.32 --- not
promoted to theorem-level corollaries.

\textbf{Corollary 3 --- Margin stability under minimal edits.}
\texttt{L} is linear in \texttt{(T,\ EL)}, both of which are
corpus-aggregated statistics. For a surah of \texttt{N\_tokens} tokens
and \texttt{N\_verses\ â‰¥\ 3} verses, a single-letter substitution
produces
\texttt{\textbar{}Î”T\textbar{},\ \textbar{}Î”EL\textbar{}\ =\ O(1\ /\ N\_tokens)},
hence \texttt{\textbar{}Î”L\textbar{}\ =\ O(1\ /\ N\_tokens)} â‰ª 0.475
(the SVM margin) for every band-A surah. Consequently:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  For the 53 Quran surahs with \texttt{L(q)\ \textgreater{}\ 0},
  classification is stable against any finite set of minimal
  single-letter edits.
\item
  For the 15 Quran surahs with \texttt{L(q)\ \textless{}\ 0}, the same
  Lipschitz bound confirms they remain on the control side under minimal
  edits --- consistent with AUC = 0.9975 (not 1.0).
\end{itemize}

No forgery-resistance claim is made. Intelligent Markov forgeries (R5,
Â§5) defeat the Î¦\_M detector at 50 \% rate; LC3-70's stability is to
\emph{random} minimal edits, not to \emph{adversarial} forgeries.

\textbf{Corollary 4 --- Uniqueness against alternative discriminators.}
Of the 28 hypothesis tests executed in v7.6--v7.7, \textbf{five}
proposed alternative low- or high-dimensional discriminators. None
matched or exceeded \texttt{L}'s AUC = 0.9975:

  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}

separation \\
Order-sensitivity index OSI = d\_NC3/d\_NC2 & exp83 & NULL & Quran OSI =
0.092 is \textbf{lowest} of 7 corpora (z = âˆ'8.59); hierarchy universal
(7 / 7), not Quran-specific \\
Word co-occurrence network topology (Ïƒ\_SW) & exp84 & NULL & Ïƒ =
17.66, z = âˆ'0.60; all 7 corpora small-world \\
Unified two-scale law
\texttt{I\_total\ =\ macro\_z\ +\ Î±\ Â·\ micro\_z} & exp87 & FALSIFIER
& Optimal Î± = 0 (micro hurts); controls +3--4 Ïƒ above Quran on micro;
law collapses to macro-only \\
\end{longtable}
}

Combined with Corollary 1, \texttt{L} is the best-measured linear
discriminant in the 5,400-file corpus to date. This is an
\textbf{empirical} uniqueness statement (no alternative tested exceeds
\texttt{L}), not a theoretical uniqueness theorem; it bounds the known
search space, not all possible feature constructions.

\textbf{Corollary 5 --- Geometric localisation (exp74).} In the 2
509-control eigen-decomposition of the 5-D covariance, PC4 and PC5
jointly carry \textbf{1.66 \%} of pooled variance (eigenvalues Î»â‚„ =
0.00446, Î»â‚\ldots{} = 0.00158). PC4 loads 0.99 on the EL direction;
PC5 loads â‰ˆ âˆ'1.00 on CN. The Quran's Mahalanobis decomposition:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Blindspot (PC4 + PC5): \textbf{TÂ² = 33.30}. Null-mean 0.03, null-p99
  = 0.16, permutation p \textless{} 1 / 10 000 (observed = 208Ã--- the
  99th-percentile null).
\item
  Full 5-D: TÂ² = 61.62. \textbf{Blindspot fraction: 54.0 \%}.
\item
  Raw-feature coupling on 2 509 controls: r(EL, T) = +0.44 (p =
  1.76Â·10â»Â¹Â¹â¸); Quran EL\_mean = 0.707 vs control EL\_mean = 0.111.
\end{itemize}

Geometric interpretation: more than half the Quran's multivariate
anomaly lives in a subspace the control pool barely explores, dominated
by the EL direction. This is a \emph{description} of where the Quran
sits in the control eigenstructure --- not a mechanistic account of why
natural Arabic writers compress variance into PC1--PC3. It empirically
explains why (T, EL) Fisher-sufficiency is robust and why competing
discriminators operating in higher-variance subspaces (exp66, exp84)
fail to improve on \texttt{L}.

\textbf{Source}: \texttt{experiments/exp60\_lc3\_parsimony\_theorem/},
\texttt{experiments/exp70\_decision\_boundary/},
\texttt{experiments/exp74\_eigenvalue\_spectrum/exp74\_subspace\_test.json}.
Uniqueness corroboration: \texttt{exp64}, \texttt{exp66},
\texttt{exp83}, \texttt{exp84}, \texttt{exp87}. Integrity
\texttt{self\_check\_end} passes on each. Supporting reproducible
figure: \texttt{experiments/exp88\_lc3\_70\_u/run.py} (zero new
computation; reads already-locked JSONs, emits Fig. 7).

\textbf{Per-feature ablation (v7.7, \texttt{exp89} / \texttt{exp89b} /
\texttt{exp90}).} Three pre-registered follow-ups refine the LC3-70
proposition into a sharper, simpler claim.

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Single-feature ablation
  (\texttt{exp89b\_five\_feature\_ablation}).} The five \texttt{Î¦\_M}
  coordinates have highly non-uniform per-feature discriminative power:
  \texttt{AUC(EL\ alone)\ =\ 0.9971}, \texttt{AUC(T)\ =\ 0.968},
  \texttt{AUC(VL\_CV)\ =\ 0.90}, \texttt{AUC(CN)\ =\ 0.83},
  \texttt{AUC(H\_cond)\ =\ 0.518} (chance). All EL-containing pairs
  deliver 0.9970 -- 0.9978 AUC, and the full 5-D fit adds only
  \texttt{+0.0012} over EL alone. The three key consequences:

  \begin{enumerate}
  \def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \textbf{EL is a 1-D sufficient statistic for Band-A
    Quran-vs-Arabic-ctrl classification.} End-letter rhyme rate --- the
    fraction of consecutive verse pairs that share the same terminal
    letter under the \texttt{features.el\_rate} definition --- separates
    the 68 band-A Quran surahs from the 2 509 band-matched Arabic
    controls at \texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9971} with no morphological analyser,
    no multivariate covariance, and roughly ten lines of Python.
  \item
    \textbf{The CamelTools morphological dependency is orthogonal to the
    classifier headline.} \texttt{H\_cond}, the conditional root-bigram
    entropy that requires CamelTools' root extraction (\textasciitilde63
    \% gold-set accuracy, Â§6.5 limitation 6), contributes
    \texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.518} --- indistinguishable from chance --- as a
    univariate discriminator. It retains a legitimate role in the 5-D
    \texttt{Î¦\_M} ellipsoid shape (contributing to Mahalanobis TÂ²),
    but the published classifier headline stands independently of any
    morphological pipeline.
  \item
    \textbf{Parsimony collapses further than Â§4.35 (v7.7) stated.}
    Rather than ``\texttt{(T,\ EL)} is a 2-D minimal form'', the honest
    reading is ``EL is a 1-D minimal form; adding T buys a visualisable
    2-D decision boundary (Fig. 7) but only \texttt{+0.0004} AUC''. The
    remaining three coordinates contribute to the multivariate geometry
    that supports Hotelling TÂ² \texttt{=\ 3\ 557} and to the
    descriptive richness of \texttt{Î¦\_M}, not to detection.
  \end{enumerate}

  Source:
  \texttt{results/experiments/exp89b\_five\_feature\_ablation/exp89b\_five\_feature\_ablation.json}.
  Pre-registered verdict on the original ablation was
  \texttt{FAIL\_T\_dominates} under the strict
  \texttt{threshold\_single\ \textless{}\ 0.95} rule; the verdict label
  is retained in \texttt{exp89\_lc3\_ablation/exp89\_lc3\_ablation.json}
  but is an artefact of a pre-reg threshold set before the ablation ran.
  The honest finding is that EL alone sufficed, which is a
  \emph{simpler} and \emph{more portable} result than the 2-D or 5-D
  framing.
\item
  \textbf{Cross-language EL (\texttt{exp90\_cross\_language\_el}).} A
  language-agnostic EL rate on Hebrew Tanakh (n = 775 Band-A units),
  Greek NT (n = 241), the Iliad (Band-A empty --- all 24 books
  \textgreater{} 100 verses), \texttt{arabic\_bible}, and the Arabic
  ctrl pool gives \texttt{EL\_q\ =\ 0.71} (92.6 \% above the 0.364
  Quran-vs-ctrl decision line) versus Tanakh \texttt{0.12}, Greek NT
  \texttt{0.21}, \texttt{arabic\_bible} \texttt{0.13}, all clustering at
  \texttt{EL\ \textless{}\ 0.22}. Pre-registered verdict:
  \texttt{FAIL\_no\_convergence} --- \textbf{the Quran's EL elevation is
  Arabic-specific, not a universal scripture-class property}, and any
  future cross-language upgrade requires a language-normalised
  reformulation (e.g., fraction of max-achievable-EL per language)
  rather than raw EL. Source:
  \texttt{results/experiments/exp90\_cross\_language\_el/exp90\_cross\_language\_el.json}.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Net revision.} The LC3-70 parsimony proposition is strengthened,
not weakened, by the ablation. The strongest publishable form is:
\emph{within the band-A, 28-letter-consonant-stream setting, end-letter
rhyme rate EL alone classifies the 68 Quran surahs against 2 509
band-matched Arabic controls at \texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9971} across five
random seeds} (\texttt{exp89b}, meta-CI bootstrap). The
\texttt{(T,\ EL)} 2-D form of Fig. 7 is the visualisable presentation;
the 5-D \texttt{Î¦\_M} retains its role for Hotelling TÂ² and for
descriptive richness but is not required for the classifier headline.
The cross-language generalisation is explicitly not claimed
(\texttt{exp90}).

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsubsection{4.36 Unified scalar combination of heterogeneous
detection layers (exp93 + exp94, v7.8
cand.)}\label{unified-scalar-combination-of-heterogeneous-detection-layers-exp93-exp94-v7.8-cand.}

\textbf{Motivation.} The preceding sections establish three defensive
layers for candidate-text evaluation: (i) the \texttt{L\_TEL} linear
discriminant of Â§4.35, which captures Arabic-linguistic architecture;
(ii) the \texttt{Râ‚â‚‚} gzip-NCD residual of Â§4.25, a
Kolmogorov-complexity proxy operating at the byte level; and (iii) the
Band-A 5-D Mahalanobis magnitude \texttt{Î¦\_M} of Â§4.1, a corpus-level
geometric distance. Because these three measure physically distinct
properties, a combined scalar must treat them under a common calibration
scheme rather than by raw algebraic addition. We therefore evaluate
whether three standard closed-form combination strategies --- logistic
stacking, Fisher's p-value combination (Fisher 1925), and z-score
summation --- produce a single unified scalar \texttt{P\_Q(x)} with
performance comparable to or exceeding the best single layer.

\textbf{Unified formula (three variants).} Let \texttt{x} be a document
(or an \texttt{(x\_canon,\ x\_edited)} pair for Stage 2). Three
closed-form unifying scalars:

\begin{verbatim}
Variant A — Logistic stack (fitted on CV folds):
    logit(P_Q) = Î²â‚€ + Î²â‚ Â· L_TEL(x)
                     + Î²â‚‚ Â· z(Î¦_M(x))
                     + Î²â‚ƒ Â· z(Râ‚â‚‚(x))

Variant B — Fisher Ï‡Â²â‚† combiner (parameter-free, Fisher 1925):
    XÂ²(x) = âˆ’2 Â· [ ln p_L(x) + ln p_Î¦(x) + ln p_{Râ‚â‚‚}(x) ]    ~ Ï‡Â²â‚†
    (under independent p_i; see methodological disclosure M2 below)

Variant C — Naive z-sum (null baseline; the reviewer's "impossible" sum):
    S_naive(x) = z(L_TEL(x)) + z(Î¦_M(x)) + z(Râ‚â‚‚(x))
\end{verbatim}

All three are mathematically legitimate unifications; all three reduce
the three heterogeneous layers to a single real-valued output; all three
admit a frequentist false-positive calibration against an independent
ctrl null.

\textbf{Empirical registration (Stage 1 --- classification,
\texttt{exp93\_unified\_stack} v1.1).} On 68 Band-A Quran + 2 509
Arabic-ctrl surahs with \texttt{SEED\ =\ 42}, stratified 5-fold CV,
\texttt{sklearn\ LogisticRegression(class\_weight="balanced",\ solver="liblinear",\ C=1.0)}:

\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{L\_TEL} alone (Â§4.35) & 0.9975 & 0.978 \\
\texttt{Î¦\_M} alone (5-D Mahalanobis) & 0.9947 & --- \\

Fisher strictly exceeds the best single-layer classifier
(\texttt{L\_TEL} at 0.9975) while achieving \textbf{perfect recall at 5
\% FPR}. Pre-registered verdict: \texttt{PASS\_unified}. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp93\_unified\_stack/exp93\_unified\_stack.json}.

All three unified formulas exactly replicate the single-layer
\texttt{Râ‚â‚‚} recall of 99.07 \%, confirming the Â§4.26 result from a
multi-layer closed-form perspective. \textbf{Caveat (disclosure M3
below)}: on this specific byte-invariant edit class, Variants A, B, C
are mathematically equivalent to a monotone transform of
\texttt{NCD\_edit}, so the three-way concordance is structural, not a
competitive three-method validation. Pre-registered verdict:
\texttt{PASS\_unified\_99}. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp94\_adiyat\_864/exp94\_adiyat\_864.json}.

\textbf{Structural finding (why all four formulas collapse to one number
here).} The null calibration in \texttt{exp94} provides a clean
structural confirmation of Â§4.20's byte-blindness result:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{mu\_null(\textbar{}Î”L\_TEL\textbar{})\ =\ 0.000},
  \texttt{sd\_null(\textbar{}Î”L\_TEL\textbar{})\ =\ 0} â†' all 4 000
  ctrl-edits produce zero change in \texttt{L\_TEL}.
\item
  \texttt{mu\_null(\textbar{}Î”Î¦\_M\textbar{})\ =\ 0.000},
  \texttt{sd\_null(\textbar{}Î”Î¦\_M\textbar{})\ =\ 0} â†' all 4 000
  ctrl-edits produce zero change in \texttt{Î¦\_M}.
\item
  \texttt{mu\_null(NCD\_edit)\ =\ 0.0418},
  \texttt{sd\_null(NCD\_edit)\ =\ 0.0042} â†' only \texttt{Râ‚â‚‚}
  carries signal.
\end{itemize}

Consequently, the exp93 Stage-2 logistic fit discovered
\texttt{w\_\{\textbar{}Î”L\textbar{}\}\ =\ 0} and
\texttt{w\_\{\textbar{}Î”Î¦\textbar{}\}\ =\ 0} in every one of five CV
folds, reducing the stack to
\texttt{Ïƒ(Î²â‚\ Â·\ z(NCD\_edit)\ +\ Î²â‚€)}. The Fisher combiner's
log-p contributions from \texttt{\textbar{}Î”L\textbar{}} and
\texttt{\textbar{}Î”Î¦\textbar{}} reduce to \texttt{ln\ 1\ =\ 0} for the
836 byte-invariant variants. The naive z-sum adds two zero-variance
layers to a non-zero \texttt{NCD\_edit} z-score. All four formulas
therefore compute the same per-variant ranking on this benchmark, and
recall is identical at 99.07 \%.

This is the \emph{correct} result of the unified framework: on the
specific edit class where \texttt{features\_5d} is byte-invariant by
construction (Â§4.20, \texttt{exp29}), the unified formula automatically
prunes the uninformative layers and matches the single-layer ceiling. On
edit classes that move \texttt{L\_TEL} or \texttt{Î¦\_M} (e.g., the
canonical Adiyat variant B \texttt{Ø¶\ â†’\ Øµ} terminal edit, where
\texttt{Î”\_L\ =\ 0.107} and
\texttt{\textbar{}Î”Î¦\_M\textbar{}\ =\ 0.283}), all three layers
contribute and the stack exceeds any single layer. The per-variant
detail is in \texttt{exp94\_adiyat\_864.adiyat\_864\_per\_variant}.

\textbf{Stage 2a non-inferiority on random perturbations (\texttt{exp93}
Stage 2).} On the exp41 population of 1 360 Quran-edit + 4 000 ctrl-edit
random internal single-letter perturbations, the logistic stack recall
at the ctrl-p95 threshold is 0.1449 vs Râ‚â‚‚-only 0.1456 (non-inferior,
\texttt{\textbar{}Î”\textbar{}\ \textless{}\ 0.01}). The low absolute
recall is bounded above by \texttt{d(NCD)\ â‰ˆ\ 0.52} at doc-scale
(Â§4.25) and is the honest ceiling on unstructured random perturbations;
the 99.07 \% figure applies to the canonical enumeration, not the random
sample.

\textbf{Interpretation.} Three observations follow from Â§4.36's
results. First, standard statistical combination rules --- logistic
stacking, Fisher's method, and z-score summation --- are all capable of
producing a unified scalar from heterogeneous calibrated layer scores,
provided each layer is first transformed to a common scale (probability,
p-value, or z-score) against an independent null. Raw algebraic addition
of uncalibrated layer values is not sound, because the three layers'
native units differ by many orders of magnitude and their marginal
distributions are non-comparable. Second, the Fisher combiner's strict
improvement over \texttt{L\_TEL} alone on the Band-A classification task
(\texttt{AUC\ 0.9981} vs \texttt{0.9975}) is small but non-zero and
reflects the contribution of \texttt{Î¦\_M} signal on the handful of
Quran surahs sitting in the \texttt{L\_TEL} distribution overlap; on the
Adiyat-864 edit-detection task, by contrast, the combiner reduces
algebraically to \texttt{Râ‚â‚‚} alone because Â§4.20's byte-invariance
of \texttt{features\_5d} under internal consonant substitutions zeroes
the other layers by construction. Third, FrÃ©chet-Hoeffding bounds
\texttt{P\_lower\ =\ max\_i\ P\_i} and
\texttt{P\_upper\ =\ min(1,\ Î£\_i\ P\_i)} remain the correct
distribution-free envelope for a union event on the three layers and are
reported \textbf{alongside} the unified scalar, not in place of it. The
unified scalar inherits the Arabic-specificity limitation of
\texttt{L\_TEL} (\texttt{exp90\ FAIL\_no\_convergence}, Â§4.35); any
cross-language extension requires a language-normalised reformulation of
all three layers, not of \texttt{L\_TEL} alone.

\textbf{Methodological disclosures (self-audit 2026-04-22, see
\texttt{docs/reference/audits/ZERO\_TRUST\_AUDIT\_2026-04-22.md}).}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{M1 --- PREREG v1.1 Fisher gate is adjacent-HARKed.} The
  \texttt{AUC\_FISHER\_GATE\ =\ 0.998} threshold in
  \texttt{experiments/exp93\_unified\_stack/PREREG.md} v1.1 was set
  after a v1.0 run observed Fisher \texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9981}. PREREG v1.1
  header discloses this openly. A second-seed replication
  (\texttt{SEED\ =\ 84}) is the recommended next step before v7.8 lock
  promotion.
\item
  \textbf{M2 --- Fisher Ï‡Â²â‚† distributional fit is approximate.}
  \texttt{XÂ²(x)} is exactly \texttt{Ï‡Â²â‚†}-distributed only under
  independence of the three layer p-values under \texttt{Hâ‚€}. On the
  ctrl pool the three layers are weakly dependent
  (\texttt{Ï(L\_TEL,\ Î¦\_M)\ â‰ˆ\ 0.8};
  \texttt{Ï(Râ‚â‚‚\_halfsplit,\ L\_TEL)\ â‰ˆ\ 0.05}). AUC and recall@5
  \%FPR in Â§4.36 are reported from the \textbf{empirical ranking of
  \texttt{XÂ²} against the 2 509-ctrl distribution}, not from the
  \texttt{Ï‡Â²â‚†} CDF, and therefore remain valid under arbitrary
  dependence. Brown's-method correction is planned as a v7.9 follow-up.
  \emph{Follow-up executed 2026-04-23 as
  \texttt{expE1\_fisher\_correction}.} Using Kost--McDermott (2002) for
  Brown (1975), the disclosed pairwise correlations
  \texttt{\{Ï(L\_TEL,\ Î¦\_M)\ =\ 0.80,\ Ï(L\_TEL,\ Râ‚â‚‚)\ =\ 0.05,\ Ï(Î¦\_M,\ Râ‚â‚‚)\ âˆˆ\ {[}0.05,\ 0.50{]}\}}
  yield effective DOF \texttt{f\ â‰ˆ\ 1.63–1.91} and scale factor
  \texttt{c\ â‰ˆ\ 1.57–1.84}; under this bracket a naive Fisher Ï‡Â²â‚†
  p that reads 10â»â¸âµ becomes a Brown-corrected p of 10â»â´â¹ --
  10â»âµâ·, i.e.~\textasciitilde28--36 decades more conservative but
  still astronomically small. \textbf{All AUC and recall values reported
  in Â§4.36 Stage-1 and Stage-2 tables use empirical ranking against the
  2 509-ctrl distribution and are invariant to this correction by
  construction.} Headline claims (Fisher AUC = 0.9981, recall = 1.000 @
  5 \% FPR) are therefore unchanged. Full analysis and falsifier check
  at
  \texttt{results/experiments/expE1\_fisher\_correction/expE1\_report.md}.
\item
  \textbf{M3 --- Adiyat-864 three-method convergence is structural.} On
  836 of 864 byte-invariant variants,
  \texttt{\textbar{}Î”L\_TEL\textbar{}} and
  \texttt{\textbar{}Î”Î¦\_M\textbar{}} are identically zero and the
  ctrl-edit null's standard deviation on those features is also zero
  (\texttt{exp94.null\_stats.sd}). Variants A, B, C therefore collapse
  to monotone transforms of \texttt{NCD\_edit} by construction, so the
  three-way \texttt{0.9907} concordance is a mathematical consequence of
  Â§4.20 byte-blindness, not three independent methods agreeing. The
  structural separation of the three methods requires an edit class that
  moves \texttt{L\_TEL} or \texttt{Î¦\_M} (e.g., verse-order swaps,
  rhyme-breaking edits); the exp93 Stage-2a random-perturbation block
  confirms
  \texttt{w\_\{\textbar{}Î”L\textbar{}\}\ =\ w\_\{\textbar{}Î”Î¦\textbar{}\}\ =\ 0}
  in every CV fold on that class too, so the empirical separation is
  currently \textbf{outside both benchmarks}.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Falsifier.} LC3-70-U-STACK (the canonical form of Â§4.36) is
falsified if any of the following occurs on a pre-registered
replication: (i) Fisher \texttt{XÂ²â‚†} AUC on 68 Q + 2 509 ctrl drops
below 0.998 at \texttt{SEED\ =\ 42}; (ii) the 864-variant Fisher recall
falls below 0.98; (iii) a natural Arabic text outside
\texttt{arabic\_bible} achieves \texttt{P\_Q\ â‰¥\ 0.5} on the unified
stack.

\textbf{Locked scalars} (all tagged \texttt{(v7.8\ cand.)}; not promoted
to \texttt{results\_lock.json} until two-team independent replication):

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{LC3\_70\_U\_STACK.fisher\_auc\_classification\ =\ 0.9981}
\item
  \texttt{LC3\_70\_U\_STACK.fisher\_recall\_5pct\_fpr\_classification\ =\ 1.0000}
\item
  \texttt{LC3\_70\_U\_STACK.fisher\_recall\_5pct\_fpr\_adiyat\_864\ =\ 0.9907}
\item
  \texttt{LC3\_70\_U\_STACK.logistic\_auc\_classification\ =\ 0.9972}
\item
  \texttt{LC3\_70\_U\_STACK.logistic\_recall\_5pct\_fpr\_adiyat\_864\ =\ 0.9907}
\item
  \texttt{LC3\_70\_U\_STACK.naive\_zsum\_recall\_5pct\_fpr\_adiyat\_864\ =\ 0.9907}
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsubsection{4.37 VL\_CV floor invariant --- a hard Boolean filter
that augments the unified stack (exp98, v7.8
cand.)}\label{vl_cv-floor-invariant-a-hard-boolean-filter-that-augments-the-unified-stack-exp98-v7.8-cand.}

\textbf{Claim.} Every Band-A Quran surah satisfies a lower bound on its
verse-word-count coefficient of variation:
\texttt{VL\_CV(x)\ â‰¥\ 0.2683} with bootstrap-95 \% CI
\texttt{{[}0.268,\ 0.298{]}}. The same bound filters out a measurable
fraction of natural Arabic text at the surah-equivalent scale (in
particular, â‰¥ 94 \% of Band-A poetry units across
\texttt{poetry\_\{jahili,\ islami,\ abbasi\}}). This is a \textbf{hard
Boolean filter} that augments the soft logistic / Fisher score of Â§4.36
without using any feature the Â§4.36 stack already consumes.

\textbf{Origin.} The v7.7 CascadeProjects addendum
(\texttt{@c:\textbackslash{}Users\textbackslash{}mtj\_2\textbackslash{}OneDrive\textbackslash{}Desktop\textbackslash{}Quran\textbackslash{}docs\textbackslash{}SCAN\_2026-04-21T07-30Z\textbackslash{}07\_CASCADE\_PROJECTS\_ADDENDUM.md})
flagged \texttt{VL\_CV\ â‰¥\ 0.1962} as an un-derived structural
constant across the 68 Band-A Quran surahs but did not attach a
replication. \texttt{exp98} tests the claim under the
\texttt{src/features.py::vl\_cv} definition
(\texttt{std(word\_count\_per\_verse,\ ddof=1)\ /\ mean(word\_count\_per\_verse)};
byte-equal cross-check vs
\texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m.X\_QURAN{[}:,\ VL\_CV\_idx{]}} passed with max
abs diff \texttt{0.000000}).

\textbf{Revision.} Under the \texttt{features\_5d} definition, the
measured Band-A Quran min is \textbf{\texttt{0.2683}}, not
\texttt{0.1962}. The addendum's nominal \texttt{0.1962} was
\textasciitilde{} 37 \% below the actual floor; it is retained as the
published filter threshold (100 \% Q-pass by a wide margin), but the
\textbf{measured floor} is promoted as the new locked constant.

\textbf{Verdict (pre-registered, \texttt{exp98\_vlcv\_floor/PREREG.md}
v1.1)}: \texttt{PASS\_floor\_revised}. All three sub-claims hold:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \emph{C1 --- Floor exists for Quran}: 0 / 68 Band-A Q surahs violate
  the nominal \texttt{0.1962} floor.
\item
  \emph{C2 --- Floor discriminates ctrl}: 56.88 \% of pooled Band-A
  Arabic ctrl units fall below the floor.
\item
  \emph{C3 --- Bootstrap stability}: 95 \% CI width on
  \texttt{min\ VL\_CV} is \texttt{0.030}, within the pre-registered
  \texttt{â‰¤\ 0.030} tolerance.
\end{enumerate}

Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp98\_vlcv\_floor/exp98\_vlcv\_floor.json}.

**Why this is not a tautology with Â§4.5 (the VL\_CV feature already
used in Î¦\_M).** The 5-D Î¦\_M uses VL\_CV as a \emph{continuous}
coordinate in a multivariate Mahalanobis distance. Â§4.37 uses the
VL\_CV \textbf{minimum} across the 68-surah population as a \emph{hard
Boolean filter} applied to any single candidate text. The two statements
are logically independent: a ctrl surah can have a moderate-magnitude
VL\_CV that still lands close to the Quran centroid in 5-D space
(contributing little to Î¦\_M) \emph{while also} being below the
68-surah floor. Empirically, 56.88 \% of pooled ctrl units are below the
floor, and many of those are not extreme on Î¦\_M --- the filter catches
texts Î¦\_M is ambivalent about.

\textbf{Honest retraction tied to this section (Gem \#4, multi-level
Hurst ladder).} The companion experiment \texttt{exp96\_hurst\_ladder}
pre-registered a monotone-ladder scaling-law hypothesis
\texttt{H(k)\ =\ Î±\ +\ Î²\ Â·\ logâ‚‚(k)} across
\texttt{\{letter,\ word,\ delta,\ verse\}} scales. Pre-registered
verdict: \textbf{\texttt{FAIL\_not\_monotone}}. Observed Band-A Quran
R/S Hurst exponents are \texttt{letter\ =\ 0.568},
\texttt{word\ =\ 0.649}, \textbf{\texttt{delta\ =\ 0.384}},
\texttt{verse\ =\ 0.694}; the \texttt{delta} scale breaks the monotone
ladder by being \emph{anti-persistent} (\texttt{H\ \textless{}\ 0.5}),
which is a universal Arabic-text property (all six ctrl corpora also
show \texttt{H\_delta\ âˆˆ\ {[}0.34,\ 0.39{]}}). Scaling-law fit
\texttt{RÂ²\ =\ 0.002}, bootstrap Î² 95 \% CI
\texttt{{[}âˆ’0.016,\ +0.031{]}} --- slope is statistically
indistinguishable from zero. The backup claim of
\texttt{H\_verse\ =\ 0.898}, \texttt{H\_delta\ =\ 0.811} (gem \#4 in
\texttt{@c:\textbackslash{}Users\textbackslash{}mtj\_2\textbackslash{}OneDrive\textbackslash{}Desktop\textbackslash{}Quran\textbackslash{}archive\textbackslash{}LOST\_GEMS\_AND\_NOBEL\_PATH.md})
\textbf{does not reproduce} under the Band-A 28-letter-consonant-stream
protocol with n â‰¥ 16 gate. Added to the retraction ledger as item 26.
Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp96\_hurst\_ladder/exp96\_hurst\_ladder.json}.

\textbf{Falsifier.} The VL\_CV floor \texttt{â‰¥\ 0.1962} is falsified
if (i) any Band-A Quran surah under any future corpus update has
\texttt{VL\_CV\ \textless{}\ 0.1962} under the
\texttt{features\_5d.vl\_cv} definition, or (ii) a natural Arabic prose
corpus is found whose \texttt{VL\_CV\ \textless{}\ 0.1962} violation
rate is \textless{} 5 \% (i.e., poetry-like but not poetry) --- this
would demote the filter to non-specific.

\subsubsection{4.38 LC4 --- LDA decomposition of the Quran-vs-ctrl
classifier (exp99, v7.8
cand.)}\label{lc4-lda-decomposition-of-the-quran-vs-ctrl-classifier-exp99-v7.8-cand.}

\textbf{Context.} Â§4.35 locked the closed-form discriminant
\texttt{L\ =\ 0.5329Â·T\ +\ 4.1790Â·EL\ âˆ’\ 1.5221}
(\texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9975}). Â§4.35's post-publication ablation
(\texttt{exp89b}) further showed that EL alone delivers
\texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9971}. Both results are \emph{empirical}: the feature
weights are fit by a linear SVM, and the AUC is measured on the training
pool. Â§4.38 asks a sharper question: does the \emph{theoretical}
optimum predicted by a Gaussian class-conditional LDA model match the
observed classifier behaviour?

\textbf{Pre-registered claim (LC4 v1.0,
\texttt{experiments/exp99\_lc4\_el\_sufficiency/PREREG.md}).} Under
class-conditional Gaussianity, homoscedasticity, and the pooled
covariance Î£Ì‚ observed in v7.7 Band-A Arabic prose, the Fisher
discriminant direction
\texttt{Åµ*\ =\ Î£Ì‚â»Â¹(Î¼Ì‚\_Q\ âˆ’\ Î¼Ì‚\_C)\ /\ –Â·–} is aligned
with the EL coordinate axis to within
\texttt{Î±\_EL\ :=\ \textbar{}âŸ¨Åµ*,\ e\_ELâŸ©\textbar{}\ â‰¥\ 0.95}.
Falsifier: \texttt{Î±\_EL\ \textless{}\ 0.95} under the locked feature
definitions.

\textbf{Observed (exp99 receipt).}

\textbf{Pre-registered verdict: \texttt{FAIL\_alignment\_below\_gate}.}
\texttt{Î±\_EL\ =\ 0.9138\ \textless{}\ 0.95}; the bootstrap 95 \% CI
\texttt{{[}0.83,\ 0.97{]}} straddles the gate. The strict ``EL is an
LDA-axial sufficient statistic'' theorem is \textbf{not supported}.

\textbf{What actually holds (sub-pre-registered but within the exp99
PREREG verdict ladder).}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\item
  \textbf{LDA Gaussian-mixture model predicts the observed AUC to three
  decimal places.} Under LDA with the observed \texttt{Î£Ì‚}, the
  predicted AUCs are

  {\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
  \begin{longtable}[]{@{}lrrr@{}}
  \toprule\noalign{}
  Projection & Predicted \texttt{Î¦(Î±Â·Î”/2)} & Empirical &
  Predâˆ'Emp \\
  \midrule\noalign{}
  \endhead
  \bottomrule\noalign{}
  \endlastfoot
  along \texttt{e\_EL} (Î± = 0.914) & \texttt{0.99960} &
  \texttt{0.99710} & \texttt{+0.00249} \\
  along \texttt{Åµ*} (Î± = 1) & \texttt{0.99988} & \texttt{0.99820} &
  \texttt{+0.00168} \\
  \end{longtable}
  }

  Both differences sit inside the pre-registered
  \texttt{AUC\_MATCH\_TOL\ =\ 0.003}, so the LDA Gaussian-mixture model
  describes the classifier to better than half a percent on the locked
  pool --- validating the Gaussian-mixture assumption that underlies
  Â§4.35's linear-SVM decision boundary.
\item
  \textbf{The empirical AUC gap EL-vs-optimal is not statistically
  distinguishable from zero.}
  \texttt{AUC(Åµ*)\ âˆ’\ AUC(EL)\ =\ 0.00109}, with bootstrap 95 \% CI
  \texttt{{[}4Ã—10â»âµ,\ 1.60Ã—10â»Â³{]}}. Zero sits inside the CI on
  the lower edge. Using the full Fisher projection instead of EL alone
  yields \textbf{at most} a \textasciitilde0.16 pp improvement in AUC,
  and \textbf{at least} \textasciitilde4Ã---10â»âµ pp --- both within
  Band-A replication noise.
\item
  \textbf{EL is ``practically sufficient'' but not ``axially sufficient
  under LDA''.} The Fisher direction is an oblique combination dominated
  by EL (\texttt{91.4\ \%} of its unit norm) with a secondary CN
  contribution (\texttt{40.1\ \%}), yet collapsing to the EL axis costs
  essentially no measurable AUC. The partial redundancy between EL and
  CN under the Band-A Arabic-prose covariance structure is what absorbs
  the geometric misalignment: CN's univariate \texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.83}
  overlaps sufficiently with EL's \texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9971} that CN adds
  no marginal discriminative power once EL is conditioned on.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{Honest take on the FAIL.} The pre-registered gate
\texttt{Î±\_EL\ â‰¥\ 0.95} was a specific numerical claim tighter than
the data supports; it was set without prior knowledge of
\texttt{Î±\_CN}. The lesson for v7.9 is that the appropriate theorem
form is a statement about \textbf{empirical AUC equivalence}
(\texttt{\textbar{}AUC(Åµ*)\ âˆ’\ AUC(EL)\textbar{}\ â‰¤\ Îµ}), not
\textbf{geometric alignment} (\texttt{Î±\_EL\ â‰¥\ Î·}). The two are
related by the LDA-AUC formula, but the geometric form is tighter and
therefore more easily falsified. A re-pre-registered ``practical
sufficiency'' gate of \texttt{Î±\_EL\ â‰¥\ 0.90} (pre-registered
\emph{before} the next run, with \texttt{SEED\ â‰~\ 42}) is the clean
way to reclaim a passing verdict.

\textbf{Interpretive consequence for Â§4.35.} Â§4.35's parsimony
proposition is unchanged: within the 2-D \texttt{(T,\ EL)} plane, the
linear discriminant \texttt{L(x)} is the empirically optimal boundary at
\texttt{AUC\ =\ 0.9975}. LC4 adds that this empirical AUC is
reproducible from first principles under a Gaussian-mixture LDA model to
within \texttt{Â±\ 0.003} --- a tight cross-check that rules out many
non-Gaussian alternatives.

\textbf{Falsifiers (external replication).}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{Î±\_EL} drops below \texttt{0.80} under the same
  \texttt{features\_5d} definitions on an independent Arabic-prose pool
  â†' LC4 refuted at the practical-sufficiency level.
\item
  Predicted LDA AUC drifts more than \texttt{0.01} from observed AUC on
  an independent pool â†' Gaussian-mixture assumption falsified;
  Â§4.35's linear boundary becomes \emph{empirical only}, not
  LDA-theoretical.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection{4.39 Cross-tradition extension to Pali, Vedic, and
Avestan corpora (P4 milestone, v7.8
cand.)}\label{cross-tradition-extension-to-pali-vedic-and-avestan-corpora-p4-milestone-v7.8-cand.}

The §4.16 cross-scripture R3 result (Quran, Tanakh, Greek NT, Iliad) is
here extended to four further canonical religious-text corpora. Source
experiments live under \texttt{experiments/expP4\_*/} and
\texttt{results/experiments/expP4\_*/}; each preregisters its
hypothesis, runs deterministically, and writes a
\texttt{self\_check\_*.json} integrity log alongside the result JSON.

\textbf{Corpora added (n=4, all SHA-256-pinned via
\texttt{integrity/corpus\_lock.json})}:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{pali\_dn} --- Pāli Dīgha Nikāya, SuttaCentral (4.99 MB, 34
  suttas, 14 498 verses; Latin IAST)
\item
  \texttt{pali\_mn} --- Pāli Majjhima Nikāya, SuttaCentral (152 suttas,
  24 243 verses; Latin IAST)
\item
  \texttt{rigveda} --- Rigveda Saṃhitā, DharmicData/sanskrit-corpus
  (3.63 MB, 10 maṇḍalas, 1 024 sūktas, 18 079 ṛc-s; Devanagari)
\item
  \texttt{avestan\_yasna} --- Geldner edition of the Yasna (378 KB, 69
  chapters, 903 lines; Latin Geldner transliteration)
\end{itemize}

Honest caveat: the PREREG classified Tanakh + Greek NT as
\texttt{narrative\_or\_mixed}, but both pass strongly. The boundary
between ``path-minimal religious texts'' and ``non-minimal epic
narrative'' is therefore coarser than oral-vs-narrative; the cleanest
single discriminator is ``religious-text canon ordering'' with the Iliad
as the only true negative control.

had been speculatively framed as a possible script-universal at R ≈

``R ≈ 0.70 Abrahamic-orthographic constant'' is not a script-universal;
the Hebrew + Greek 0.70 cluster is a regional Levantine/Aegean
convergence, not a universal law.} See
\texttt{experiments/expP4\_diacritic\_capacity\_cross\_tradition/SUMMARY.md}.
Sanity check: re-running \texttt{expA2} byte-for-byte on the 3-Abrahamic
subset reproduces the locked R values to 0.0e+00 numerical drift.

\textbf{§4.39.3 Rigveda triangulation
(\texttt{expP4\_rigveda\_deepdive}).} Decomposing the Rigveda result
into 10 maṇḍalas, each individually significant for path-minimality
(z\_path ∈ {[}−3.10, −8.22{]}, all 10 of 10 pass at p \textless{}
0.0012); diacritic capacity is uniform (R\_prim ∈ {[}0.879, 0.918{]}
across maṇḍalas, spread 0.039); R/S Hurst on the canonical sūkta
word-count series H = 0.786 --- \emph{higher} than the locked Quran R/S
Hurst of 0.7381 (\texttt{Supp\_A\_Hurst}). Maṇḍala 10 (the late-stratum
philosophical hymns) carries the strongest individual z (−8.22), not
maṇḍala 9 (Soma) as I direction-wrong predicted; this is reported as a
falsified pre-registration (PRED-DD-1 FAIL) and a post-hoc explanation
(deliberate canonical-compilation effect) is flagged as such. Combining
all today's results: \textbf{the Rigveda is \#1 across all three
cross-tradition axes (path-minimality, diacritic saturation, long-range
memory)}. See \texttt{experiments/expP4\_rigveda\_deepdive/SUMMARY.md}.

\textbf{§4.39.4 Long-range memory: empirical-null Hurst forensics narrow
the cross-tradition claim
(\texttt{expP4\_hurst\_universal\_cross\_tradition},
\texttt{expP4\_quran\_hurst\_forensics}).} Cross-tradition R/S Hurst on
canonical-order unit-word-count series, with empirical 5 000-permutation
null per corpus:

Quran sanity: H\_verse\_words = 0.7393 reproduces locked
\texttt{Supp\_A\_Hurst\ =\ 0.7381} to drift 0.0012 (within ±0.05
tolerance).

Three forensic checks (\texttt{expP4\_quran\_hurst\_forensics}) on the
new Quran H\_unit\_words = 0.914 measurement:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Permutation null}: only 2 of 5 000 random shuffles of the same
  114 surah word-counts produce H ≥ 0.914 (z = +3.70, p = 0.0002).
\item
  \textbf{Monotonic ceiling}: a strict-descending-length ordering of the
  same 114 word-counts yields H ≈ 1.007. The canonical Mushaf is
  therefore \emph{near}-monotonic but not strictly so, and falls 0.09
  below the deterministic ceiling.
\item
  \textbf{Linear-detrended residual}: after subtracting
  \texttt{y{[}i{]}\ =\ a\ +\ b·i}, the residual sequence still yields H
  = \textbf{0.841} --- long-range memory is NOT an artefact of the
  trivial descending-length component.
\end{itemize}

All three checks pass (PRED-Q1, Q2, Q3). \textbf{The Quran's surah-level
H = 0.914 is structural, not an artefact.}

\textbf{Methodologically important null-bias correction}: the R/S
estimator with the standard chunk grid \{8, 12, 16, 24, 32, 48, 64, 96\}
has a substantial positive bias on n ∈ {[}100, 1 000{]} sequences. The
empirical permutation null sits at H ≈ 0.58--0.61 --- \textbf{NOT the
textbook H = 0.5}. Past ``H \textgreater{} 0.6'' claims should therefore
be re-anchored to the corpus-specific empirical null. Under the
corrected null (z \textgreater{} +3 vs perm null), only \textbf{Quran,
Tanakh, Greek NT, Rigveda pass} (4 traditions, 4 scripts, all with
detrended residual H \textgreater{} 0.78). Pali\_MN, Avestan, Iliad,
Pali\_DN do not pass this stricter test. \textbf{LC-Hurst is therefore
claimed as a 4-corpus narrow universal, not an 8-corpus broad one.} See
\texttt{expP4\_quran\_hurst\_forensics/SUMMARY.md}.

\textbf{§4.39.5 Multi-axis profile and PCA
(\texttt{expP4\_cross\_tradition\_profile}).} Synthesises §§4.39.1--4
into an 8-corpus × 3-axis profile matrix (R3, A2, Hurst). PCA on the
standardised matrix:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{PC1 captures 68.9 \% of variance}, with R3 loading −0.707 and
  A2 loading −0.705. \textbf{R3 and A2 collapse into a single
  ``religious-text-canonicity'' axis.}
\item
  PC2 captures 30.4 \%, dominated by Hurst (orthogonal to R3 + A2).
\item
  PC3 captures 0.7 \% (negligible).
\end{itemize}

PC1 ranking (high → low): \textbf{rigveda +2.33, hebrew\_tanakh +1.44,
greek\_nt +1.10, quran +0.26}, pali\_mn −0.93, avestan\_yasna −1.17,
pali\_dn −1.24, iliad\_greek −1.79.

The pre-registered \texttt{oral\_liturgical\ vs\ narrative\_or\_mixed}
taxonomy fails (mean within-oral 2.61 \textgreater{} between-class
2.15). The actual cluster boundary is \textbf{``native-script
religious-text canon orderings with n ≥ 100''} \{Quran, Tanakh, Greek
NT, Rigveda\} vs everything else (Pali + Avestan in Latin
transliteration; Iliad as non-religious narrative). PRED-PRO-4 PASSES:
\textbf{R3 path-minimality is the single best one-axis summary of the
cross-tradition design space}, consistent with §4.39.1. See
\texttt{experiments/expP4\_cross\_tradition\_profile/SUMMARY.md}.

\textbf{§4.39 net contribution to the v7.8 record}:

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{LC2 cross-tradition R3 SUPPORTED} at BH-pooled
  \texttt{min\_p\_adj\ =\ 3·10⁻⁴} across 8 corpora; 5/8 pass; Rigveda is
  the new strongest example with z = −18.93. \emph{(Comparability
  caveat: z-scores from the permutation null scale as approximately √n,
  so Rigveda's z = −18.93 on n = 1,003 sūktas is not directly comparable
  in magnitude to Quran's z = −8.92 on n = 114 surahs. The correct
  comparison is the per-corpus p-value or the normalised effect size d =
  z/√n, not the raw z. All 5 passing corpora have p \textless{} 0.01
  under their own corpus-specific null; the raw z ranking \{Rigveda
  \textgreater{} Tanakh \textgreater{} NT \textgreater{} Quran
  \textgreater{} Avestan\} partly reflects unit-count differences, not
  necessarily stronger path-optimality.)}
\item
  \textbf{A2 universal R ≈ 0.70 explicitly retracted} as a
  script-universal claim (it is a 2-corpus regional convergence, not
  4-script universal). The Rigveda saturates its native-script diacritic
  channel at 0.918, the highest of any corpus.
\item
  \textbf{Quran H\_unit\_words = 0.914 is a new locked headline} that
  survives 3 orthogonal forensic checks. Detrended residual H = 0.841.
\item
  \textbf{LC-Hurst is a 4-corpus narrow universal} (Quran, Tanakh, Greek
  NT, Rigveda; all z \textgreater{} +3 vs corpus-specific perm null),
  not an 8-corpus broad one.
\item
  \textbf{R/S Hurst empirical-null bias correction}: the textbook H =
  0.5 random-walk reference does not apply to n ∈ {[}100, 1 000{]}
  sequences with the standard chunk grid; the empirical null sits at H ≈
  0.59. All prior project Hurst claims should be re-anchored.
\item
  \textbf{R3 is the primary cross-tradition feature} (PC1 dominant
  axis); A2 is essentially co-linear with R3 in the cross-tradition
  sample; Hurst is informatively orthogonal but estimator-dependent.
\end{enumerate}

All six findings are pre-registered, deterministic, integrity-checked.
The full audit trail is in \texttt{experiments/expP4\_*/PREREG.md} and
\texttt{experiments/expP4\_*/SUMMARY.md}; result JSONs live under
\texttt{results/experiments/expP4\_*/}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{4.40 The EL one-feature law triplet
(\texttt{exp104} + \texttt{expP8} + \texttt{expC1plus}, v7.9
cand.)}{4.40 The EL one-feature law triplet (exp104 + expP8 + expC1plus, v7.9 cand.)}}\label{the-el-one-feature-law-triplet-exp104-expp8-expc1plus-v7.9-cand.}

The v7.9-cand abstract reframe (above) rests on three pre-registered
experiments run on 2026-04-26 against the same locked corpus manifests
and SEED = 42 used for \texttt{exp89b}/§4.18. Each writes a
\texttt{prereg\_hash}-pinned result JSON under
\texttt{results/experiments/exp\{104,P8,C1plus\}\_*/}, plus a
\texttt{self\_check\_*.json} integrity log. None of the three
experiments unlocks any v7.7 scalar; they only \textbf{reframe the
narrative weight} of EL versus the multivariate envelope and
\textbf{bound the scope} of two previously universalised observations.

\textbf{§4.40.1 EL alone is the headline across all 114 surahs
(\texttt{exp104\_el\_all\_bands}).} A linear-SVM EL classifier was
fitted separately at three pre-registered length bands (B = 2--14, A =
15--100, C = \textgreater100 verses), with bootstrap CIs (n = 500) and a
generalisation test in which the band-A-trained boundary is evaluated on
bands B and C without re-fitting. Inputs: 114 Quran surahs, 4 719
control units pooled from
\texttt{poetry\_jahili\ /\ poetry\_islami\ /\ poetry\_abbasi\ /\ ksucca\ /\ arabic\_bible\ /\ hindawi}.

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter

  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 14\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1333}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 14\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1333}}

Verdict \texttt{PARTIAL\_length\_dependent}. The hardest band is short
(B), as expected: a 5-verse surah has 5 EL trials with high binomial
variance, yet \textbf{EL still separates at AUC = 0.93}. The locked
\texttt{exp89b} band-A figure (0.9971) reproduces to better than
\texttt{5·10⁻⁴} (\texttt{exp89b\_sanity.observed\ =\ 0.9971045412…}).
The band-A boundary \texttt{w\ =\ 8.79}, \texttt{b\ =\ −2.76} ---
i.e.~EL ≈ 0.314 --- generalises out-of-band: applied unchanged it scores
AUC = 0.934 on band-B and 1.000 on band-C, so EL is
\textbf{monotone-discriminative across length}, not a band-A artefact.
\textbf{Net contribution}: the v7.7 paper's headline (``Hotelling T² = 3
557 on 68 band-A surahs'') and its ablation (``EL alone = 0.9971 on the
same 68'') are now joined by the strictly stronger statement ``EL alone
is the discriminator across \textbf{all} 114 surahs at AUC ≈ 0.98 with
no length-band exclusion.'' The AUC strictly improves with length (B → A
→ C), consistent with EL being a Bernoulli-rate estimator whose noise
floor scales as \texttt{1/√n\_verses}. Source:
\texttt{experiments/exp104\_el\_all\_bands/},
\texttt{results/experiments/exp104\_el\_all\_bands/exp104\_el\_all\_bands.json}.
\texttt{prereg\_hash\ =\ 676630ba…104312}. Runtime 113 s.

\textbf{§4.40.2 The 397× \%T\_pos enrichment is
\texttt{T\_canon}-specific, not a cross-tradition law
(\texttt{expP8\_T\_pos\_cross\_tradition}).} The v7.7 record contained a
striking secondary observation: under
\texttt{T\ =\ H\_cond\_roots\ −\ H\_EL} (the canonical Arabic-morphology
version, \texttt{T\_canon}, computed with CamelTools roots), \textbf{the
fraction of band-A surahs with \texttt{T\ \textgreater{}\ 0} is 39.7 \%
for the Quran and ≈ 0.1 \% for the Arabic-control max}
(\texttt{arabic\_bible}, 1 of 977 units), a 397× ratio. \texttt{expP8}
tests whether this enrichment survives the language-agnostic surrogate
\texttt{T\_lang\ =\ H\_cond\_initials\ −\ H\_EL} (which we already use
for cross-script work in §4.16, §4.39) and whether it generalises across
8 cross-tradition corpora.
