Verdict \texttt{FAIL\_QURAN\_NOT\_HIGHEST}. Under \texttt{T\_lang}, the
Quran band-A figure (92.6 \%) sits \textbf{below} \texttt{pali\_mn} (100
\%), \texttt{iliad\_greek} (100 \%, all-unit), and \texttt{greek\_nt}
(99.2 \%). The 397× ratio over the Arabic-control max is therefore
\textbf{not preserved} when the same statistic is applied
cross-tradition with a language-agnostic surrogate; under
\texttt{T\_lang}, the Quran-vs-Arabic-control-max ratio drops to
\textbf{1.10×} (\texttt{ksucca} band-A = 84.2 \%). The 397× number is a
\textbf{\texttt{T\_canon}-specific result} --- a property of
CamelTools-resolved Arabic root-bigram conditional entropy minus EL, not
of structural tension as such. Two honest implications follow: (a) the
Quran-band-A 39.7 \% \texttt{T\_canon} figure remains a \textbf{valid
Arabic-prose anomaly} (within Arabic, the next-best corpus is
\texttt{arabic\_bible} at 0.10 \%, ratio 397×), and (b) any
\textbf{cross-tradition} generalisation of the ``T\_pos enrichment''
claim must be retracted; the Pali, Greek, and Iliad numbers under
\texttt{T\_lang} show that the ``many surahs have positive T'' pattern
is not Quran-specific outside Arabic. Source:
\texttt{experiments/expP8\_T\_pos\_cross\_tradition/},
\texttt{results/experiments/expP8\_T\_pos\_cross\_tradition/expP8\_T\_pos\_cross\_tradition.json}.
\texttt{prereg\_hash\ =\ 953ffa54…204f}. Runtime 44 s. Sanity: locked
\texttt{T\_canon\_pct\_quran\_band\_a\ =\ 0.397} reproduces (observed
0.39706, within ±0.05 tol).

\textbf{§4.40.3 The closed-form Rényi-2 derivation
\texttt{EL\_q\ ≈\ 1/√2\ ⇐\ Σp̂²\ =\ 1/2} is FALSIFIED at the corpus pool
but holds in expectation per band-A surah
(\texttt{expC1plus\_renyi2\_closed\_form}).} A long-standing project
speculation (predating v7.7) was that the empirical near-coincidence
\texttt{EL\_q\ ≈\ 1/√2} (locked: \texttt{EL\_q\ =\ 0.7271…}) might
follow from a closed-form information-theoretic statement: under iid
sampling from the verse-final-letter PMF
\texttt{p̂\ =\ (p̂\_1,\ …,\ p̂\_28)}, the EL rate is the corpus-pool
collision probability \texttt{Σp̂²}, and \texttt{1/√2} is exactly the
square root of \texttt{1/2}. The hypothesis was therefore
\textbf{\texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.500\ ±\ 0.005}} (equivalently Rényi-2 entropy
≈ 1 bit). \texttt{expC1plus} tests this against (i) the corpus-pool PMF
over all 6 236 Quran verses, with a 100 000-bootstrap CI, and (ii)
cross-corpus comparison against 13 other corpora.

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1154}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1538}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1538}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1538}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1538}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1538}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 12\tabcolsep) * \real{0.1154}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}

\end{longtable}
}

Verdict \texttt{FAIL\_NOT\_HALF}. The Quran corpus-pool
\texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.295} is far from \texttt{0.500} and the 100
000-bootstrap two-sided p-value against the strict band {[}0.495,
0.505{]} is \textbf{0.000} (\texttt{p\_left\_lt\_half\ =\ 1.0}). The
Rényi-2 entropy is \texttt{1.763\ bits}, not \texttt{1\ bit}. The cause
is mechanical: 50.1 \% of Quranic verse-finals are \texttt{ن}, which
alone contributes \texttt{0.501²\ =\ 0.251} to \texttt{Σp̂²}.
\textbf{Therefore the closed-form derivation \texttt{EL\_q²\ =\ 1/2} is
wrong as stated.} However, the \textbf{per-band-A-surah} behaviour
preserves the qualitative match: across the 68 band-A surahs,
\textbf{mean \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.541}, median \texttt{0.456},
\texttt{√mean\ =\ 0.7356}}, vs \texttt{1/√2\ =\ 0.7071} --- a residual
gap of only 4 \%. So the EL-near-\texttt{1/√2} phenomenon is an
\textbf{average-over-surahs property} (each surah is locally
rhyme-saturated on a small alphabet of dominant finals), \textbf{not a
pooled-PMF property}. Within Arabic the pooled-PMF result is still
distinguishing: the Quran's \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.295} is \textbf{3.2× the
median Arabic-control corpus-pool value} (0.078--0.085) and \textbf{2×
even the highest-rhyming Arabic control} (\texttt{pali\_mn} and
\texttt{pali\_dn} are not Arabic; the highest Arabic control
\texttt{Σp̂²} is 0.085). Source:
\texttt{experiments/expC1plus\_renyi2\_closed\_form/},
\texttt{results/experiments/expC1plus\_renyi2\_closed\_form/expC1plus\_renyi2\_closed\_form.json}.
\texttt{prereg\_hash\ =\ 321b00e2…8a9c56}. Runtime 26 s.

\textbf{§4.40 net contribution to the v7.9-cand record:}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{EL one-feature law promoted from band-A ablation (§4.18, AUC =
  0.9971 on 68 surahs) to a length-stratified law across all 114 surahs
  (\texttt{exp104}, AUC = 0.9813 overall; ≥ 0.93 at every band)}, with
  the band-A boundary \texttt{w\ ≈\ 8.79}, \texttt{b\ ≈\ −2.76}
  generalising out-of-band without re-fitting. The Hotelling T² = 3 557
  figure is preserved unchanged but is reframed as the \textbf{geometric
  envelope} around the EL axis.
\item
  \textbf{The 397× \%T\_pos enrichment is now bounded as
  Arabic-morphology-specific (\texttt{T\_canon} / CamelTools)}. Under
  \texttt{T\_lang}, the Quran is not the highest, and the
  cross-tradition extension of the T-pos claim is RETRACTED
  (\texttt{expP8}). The \textbf{within-Arabic} 397× anomaly stands.
\item
  \textbf{The closed-form Rényi-2 derivation
  \texttt{EL\_q²\ =\ 1/2\ ⇒\ EL\_q\ =\ 1/√2} is FALSIFIED at the corpus
  pool (\texttt{expC1plus}, \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.295})}. The
  phenomenological coincidence \texttt{EL\_q\ ≈\ 1/√2} is preserved as
  an \textbf{average-over-band-A-surahs identity}
  (\texttt{√⟨Σp̂²⟩\_surah\ ≈\ 0.74}). The §4.8 information-theoretic
  constants (\texttt{H(harakat\ \textbar{}\ rasm)\ =\ 1.964\ bits},
  \texttt{I(EL;\ CN)\ =\ 1.175\ bits}) are unaffected.
\end{enumerate}

All three experiments are pre-registered, deterministic, and
integrity-checked. \texttt{results\_lock.json} was updated 2026-04-26 PM
to pin \texttt{Phi\_M\_hotelling\_T2\ =\ 3557.34\ ±\ 5.0} and
\texttt{Phi\_M\_perm\_p\_value\ =\ 0.004975\ ±\ 0.001} (previously
unprotected at \texttt{expected:\ 0.0,\ tol:\ Infinity}). The new
v7.9-cand experiments themselves remain
integrity-locked-but-not-results-locked until two-team replication.
Audit trail: \texttt{experiments/exp\{104,P8,C1plus\}\_*/PREREG.md} and
the per-experiment JSON + \texttt{self\_check\_*.json}.

\subsubsection{4.40.4 The EL Simplicity Law as a falsifiable proposition
(v7.9
cand.)}\label{the-el-simplicity-law-as-a-falsifiable-proposition-v7.9-cand.}

The empirical observations of \texttt{exp89b} (band-A AUC = 0.9971) and
\texttt{exp104} (length-stratified AUC ≥ 0.93 at every band, ≥ 0.98
overall) admit the following formal proposition.

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Proposition (EL Simplicity Law, v7.9-cand).} Let \texttt{C} be a
corpus of vocalised Arabic prose with verse boundaries, let
\texttt{EL:\ surah\ →\ {[}0,1{]}} denote the verse-final-letter rhyme
rate (the fraction of verses ending in the most-frequent verse-final
letter of that surah), and let
\texttt{Φ\_EL(surah)\ =\ 𝟙\{EL(surah)\ ≥\ θ*\}} with
\texttt{θ*\ =\ 0.314} (the locked \texttt{exp104} band-A linear-SVM
boundary, \texttt{w\ =\ 8.79}, \texttt{b\ =\ −2.76}). For any 6-corpus
Arabic-prose sample drawn from
\texttt{\{poetry\_jahili,\ poetry\_islami,\ poetry\_abbasi,\ ksucca,\ arabic\_bible,\ hindawi\}}
of total size \texttt{n\_C\ ≥\ 4\ 719}, the per-band AUC of
\texttt{Φ\_EL} discriminating Quran from the pooled controls satisfies

\begin{verbatim}
AUC(B = 2-14 verses)   ≥ 0.93
AUC(A = 15-100 verses) ≥ 0.99
AUC(C > 100 verses)    = 1.00
AUC(all 114 surahs)    ≥ 0.98
\end{verbatim}

with the band-A-trained boundary generalising to bands B and C without
re-fitting.

\textbf{Falsification condition.} Any single Arabic-prose corpus of
\texttt{≥\ 100} band-A units producing
\texttt{AUC(Φ\_EL,\ vs\ Quran\ band-A)\ \textless{}\ 0.95} falsifies the
proposition.
\end{quote}

This converts the v7.7 / v7.9-cand empirical observations into a
\emph{replicable} statement that any external team can test on a fresh
Arabic-prose corpus. The proposition is intentionally narrower than the
cross-tradition extension, which \texttt{expP9.N1} shows fails for Pali
sutta literature in IAST transliteration (§4.41.1 below).

\subsubsection{4.40.5 Out-of-band generalisation as a separate
robustness result (v7.9
cand.)}\label{out-of-band-generalisation-as-a-separate-robustness-result-v7.9-cand.}

The v7.7 paper reports the 5-D Φ\_M classifier as a band-A object. We
here promote the \textbf{out-of-band generalisation} of the EL boundary
to a stand-alone robustness statement. Fitting a linear-SVM on EL using
band-A only (68 Quran surahs vs 2 509 band-A controls), the resulting
decision boundary \texttt{EL\ =\ 0.314} is then evaluated unchanged on
the 28 band-B short surahs (vs 2 068 short controls) and the 18 band-C
long surahs (vs 142 long controls). Out-of-band AUCs are \textbf{0.934
(band-B)} and \textbf{1.000 (band-C)}, with no per-band re-fitting. The
corresponding 5-D out-of-band test (\texttt{expP7}) is even tighter: the
band-A 5-D boundary gives \textbf{AUC = 0.979 on band-B and AUC = 0.993
on band-C}, vs the in-band 5-D AUCs of 0.985 (B) and 1.000 (C).
Out-of-band 5-D AUC is therefore within \texttt{0.006} of in-band 5-D
AUC at every band --- a quantitative refutation of the null hypothesis
that the classifier overfits to medium-length surahs.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{4.41 Whole-Quran 5-D extension and
v7.9-cand quartet (\texttt{expP7} + \texttt{expP9} batch,
2026-04-26)}{4.41 Whole-Quran 5-D extension and v7.9-cand quartet (expP7 + expP9 batch, 2026-04-26)}}\label{whole-quran-5-d-extension-and-v7.9-cand-quartet-expp7-expp9-batch-2026-04-26}

The v7.9-cand reframe (§4.40) anchors the headline on EL alone but
explicitly preserves the multivariate envelope. Two follow-up batches
run on 2026-04-26 close the band-A gap on the 5-D side and add four new
diagnostic results.

\textbf{§4.41.0 Full-Quran 5-D classifier
(\texttt{expP7\_phi\_m\_full\_quran}).} The 5-D Hotelling T² and 5-D
linear-SVM classifier of §4.1 are re-run on \textbf{all 114 Quran surahs
vs the full 4 719-unit Arabic-prose pool} (no length gate). Results:

Band-A locked sanity passes: observed T² = 3 557.79 vs locked 3 557.34 ±

corpus (95 chapters) loaded for the first time in this project. AUCs

Verdict \texttt{PASS\_arabic\_only}. Within Arabic incl.~the new hadith
corpus, EL discriminates the Quran at AUC ≥ 0.972 against every control;
\textbf{EL distinguishes the Quran from the directly comparable Sahih
Bukhari hadith corpus at AUC = 0.972} despite both being formal
classical-Arabic religious prose. Cross-tradition, EL discriminates
against the \textbf{5 of 7} non-Arabic religious-text corpora that lack
transliteration-marker artefacts at AUC ≥ 0.926 (Hebrew Tanakh 0.982,
Greek NT 0.962, Iliad 0.978, Rigveda 0.968, Avestan 0.926); but it drops
to 0.87--0.90 against the \textbf{2 Pali corpora in IAST Latin
transliteration}. Forensic check (§4.41.2 below): the Pali AUC drop is
driven by the IAST full-stop sentence marker dominating the Pali
verse-final character distribution at 56--60 \%, not by genuinely high
natural-letter rhyme --- Pali natural-letter EL is comparable to
Arabic-control EL.

\textbf{Audit-patch disclosure (2026-04-26 evening,
\texttt{audit\_patch.json})}: the original v7.9-cand-patch-B
\texttt{run\_supplement.py} set \texttt{include\_cross\_lang=False} and
therefore did NOT load Hebrew Tanakh or Greek NT despite their being
listed in the PREREG.md \texttt{NON\_ARABIC} set. The audit patch loaded
them and obtained AUC = 0.982 / 0.962 respectively --- both pass the
0.95 threshold. The \texttt{PASS\_arabic\_only} verdict is unchanged
because Pali\_MN AUC = 0.865 remains the binding constraint. \textbf{The
hadith\_bukhari corpus was added post-hoc} (not in the frozen 2026-04-26
morning PREREG.md); its result must be treated as exploratory, not
pre-registered.

(\texttt{expP9.NEW2}, 2026-04-26).} The §4.40.3 result that 50.1 \% of
Quranic verse-finals are \texttt{ن} is here extended to a 13-corpus
comparison.

\textbf{Quran's \texttt{ن}-dominance at p\_max = 0.501 is the highest
natural-letter terminal mass of any corpus tested, by a factor of 1.83×}
(next-highest natural-letter is Greek \texttt{ν} in the Iliad at 0.274).
All higher p\_max values (Pali, Rigveda, Avestan) are
transliteration-mark artefacts and should not be compared.
\textbf{Within Arabic-script corpora (8 corpora incl.~hadith), Quran
ranks \#1 by p\_max} with the next being \texttt{poetry\_islami} at
0.206 (a ratio of 2.43×). This formally settles the question raised in
§4.40.3: \textbf{\texttt{ن}-dominance is a Quran-distinctive structural
fact within Arabic-prose}, not a property of formal Arabic prose
generally. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/expP9\_v79\_batch\_diagnostics/NEW2\_supplement.json}.

\textbf{§4.41.3 Per-surah Σp̂² ≈ 1/2 bootstrap
(\texttt{expP9.expC1plus\_v2}, 2026-04-26).} The §4.40.3 falsification
of the closed-form \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 1/2} corpus-pool identity is here
re-tested at the \textbf{per-band-A-surah median} with 10 000 bootstrap
replicates. Result: \textbf{median band-A \texttt{Σp̂²\ =\ 0.4564} with
95 \% bootstrap CI {[}0.366, 0.657{]}}, which \textbf{includes 0.5}.
Verdict \texttt{PASS\_at\_half}. The closed-form \texttt{EL\_q\ =\ 1/√2}
therefore reduces to a per-band-A-surah-median identity (CI for the
median includes 1/2; sharper than the §4.40.3 mean-only result). The
corpus-pool falsification (\texttt{Σp̂²\_pool\ =\ 0.295}) remains in
force.

\textbf{§4.41.4 Per-surah EL boundary-distance ranking
(\texttt{expP9.N4}, 2026-04-26).} Of 114 Quran surahs, \textbf{107 lie
above the locked EL = 0.314 boundary}; 7 lie below. The 5 closest to the
boundary are: Q:042 (n=53, EL=0.346, +0.032), Q:022 (n=78, EL=0.273,
\textbf{−0.041}, BELOW), Q:013 (n=43, EL=0.357, +0.043), Q:057 (n=29,
EL=0.357, +0.043), Q:014 (n=52, EL=0.392, +0.078). These are the
project's most ambiguous Quran surahs by the EL law alone; they are also
the surahs the authentication tool should report with reduced
confidence. Source: \texttt{N4\_boundary\_distance.json}.

\textbf{§4.41.5 EL stress curve under terminal-letter corruption
(\texttt{expP9.N8}, 2026-04-26).} EL robustness against random
terminal-letter substitution: corruption fraction
\texttt{f\ ∈\ \{0.01,\ 0.05,\ 0.10,\ 0.20,\ 0.50\}}, AUC at \texttt{f}:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lrrrrrr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
f & 0.000 & 0.010 & 0.050 & 0.100 & 0.200 & 0.500 \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
AUC & 0.9971 & 0.9936 & 0.9934 & 0.9921 & 0.9850 & \textbf{0.9546} \\
median EL\_Q & 0.727 & 0.628 & 0.617 & 0.556 & 0.511 & 0.343 \\
\end{longtable}
}

\textbf{Maximum corruption fraction at which AUC ≥ 0.95 is
\texttt{f*\ =\ 0.50}} --- i.e.~EL alone retains AUC ≥ 0.95 even when
\textbf{half the verse-final letters of every band-A surah are replaced
by random Arabic letters}. This is the noise tolerance the
authentication tool can advertise.

\textbf{§4.41.6 Bag-of-verses null vs per-surah lock-on
(\texttt{expP9.N6}, 2026-04-26).} For each Quran surah of size n\_v,
draw n\_v verse-final letters iid from the corpus-pool PMF
(\texttt{Σp̂²\_pool\ =\ 0.295}, \texttt{ن}-dominated) and compute the
simulated max-final mass; compare to the observed max-final mass.
\textbf{43.9 \% of surahs (50 / 114) exceed the 99th percentile of the
iid-pool null} --- well above the 1 \% chance level but well below the
95 \% universal-lock-on threshold. Verdict
\texttt{FAIL\_consistent\_with\_pool\_iid} (under the strict 95 \%
threshold) but \textbf{PARTIAL\_lock\_on} under the relaxed 50 \%
threshold. Honest interpretation: about half of Quran surahs achieve
dominant-final concentration that exceeds what iid sampling from the
(already \texttt{ن}-saturated) corpus pool would produce; the other half
are surahs where the dominant final happens to be \texttt{ن} and are
therefore not statistically distinguishable from iid-pool sampling. The
result is consistent with §4.41.2's finding that \texttt{ن}-dominance is
corpus-wide, and with §4.41.3's finding that per-surah \texttt{Σp̂²}
median is statistically indistinguishable from 1/2.

\textbf{§4.41.7 Brown joint-anomaly synthesis on full-114 witnesses
(\texttt{expP9.N9}, 2026-04-26).} Combining four whole-Quran one-sided
p-values via Brown's method with conservative \texttt{ρ\ =\ 0.5}
correlation prior:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3000}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.3000}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 4\tabcolsep) * \real{0.4000}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Channel
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Source
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
one-sided p
\end{minipage} \\

EL (full 114) & \texttt{exp104} AUC = 0.9813, Hanley-McNeil z &
1.6·10⁻³ \\
R3 path-minimality & \texttt{expP4\_cross\_tradition\_R3} z = −8.92 &
2.3·10⁻¹⁹ \\
J1 mushaf smoothness & \texttt{expE17b\_mushaf\_j1\_1m\_perms} (1M-perm

Hurst H\_unit\_words & \texttt{expP4\_quran\_hurst\_forensics} H = 0.914

\end{longtable}
}

\textbf{Brown joint p (ρ=0.5) = 2.95·10⁻⁵}
(\texttt{log₁₀\ p\_joint\ =\ −4.53}); χ² T = 143.32 on df\_eff = 2.49.
\emph{(Numerical correction, audit patch D: patch B used
\texttt{p\_Hurst\ =\ 4·10⁻⁴} claiming ``2/5000 perms'' --- actual
\texttt{expP4\_quran\_hurst\_forensics.json} gives
\texttt{p\_one\_sided\ =\ 1.9996·10⁻⁴\ ≈\ 2/10001} (10 000 perms). The
corrected joint p tightens slightly from 3.28·10⁻⁵ to 2.95·10⁻⁵; verdict
unchanged.)} The Stouffer combination overflows because
\texttt{R3\ p\ =\ 2.3·10⁻¹⁹} saturates \texttt{norm.ppf} at +∞; Brown
handles this correctly. The joint p is conservative (ρ=0.5 is a
worst-case prior) and will tighten by 1--2 orders of magnitude when
replaced with the empirical 4×4 control-corpus correlation matrix.

\textbf{Honest disclosure (audit patch D)}: of the four channels
combined, only EL (channel 1) is uniquely Quran-extreme. \textbf{R3 z =
−8.92} is the \emph{4th most extreme} in
\texttt{expP4\_cross\_tradition\_R3.json} --- Rigveda (z = −18.93),
Hebrew Tanakh (z = −15.29), and Greek NT (z = −12.06) are all more
extreme than the Quran on R3. \textbf{Hurst H} ties (p ≈ 2·10⁻⁴) across
Quran, Hebrew Tanakh, Greek NT, and Rigveda. The Brown joint p therefore
measures ``how anomalously these four channels co-occur in the Quran,''
not ``how Quran-uniquely extreme each channel is.'' Source:
\texttt{N9\_brown\_synthesis.json} (raw) +
\texttt{audit\_patch.json::patch\_3\_brown\_synthesis} (corrected).

\textbf{§4.41.8 ن-dominance morphological forensics (\texttt{expP9.N7},
2026-04-26).} The §4.41.2 result that 50.1 \% of Quranic verse-finals
are \texttt{ن} is here decomposed by morphological role using CamelTools
1.5.7 \texttt{MorphologyAnalyzer.builtin\_db()}. For each of the 3 124
Quranic verses ending in \texttt{ن} (50.1 \% of 6 236), the verse-final
word is dediacritised and analysed; the most-frequent morphological
category across all returned analyses is taken. A 502-word sample from
the Arabic Bible serves as control.

Sound plural masc other case & 0.5 \% & 2.8 \% \\
Lexically-terminal-ن noun (\texttt{إنسان}, \texttt{سلطان}, \ldots) & 9.2
\% & \textbf{31.3 \%} \\
Verb other (sing, energetic) & 1.5 \% & 5.2 \% \\
Unanalysable by CamelTools & 7.7 \% & 12.0 \% \\
Other & 0.0 \% & 12.6 \% \\
\end{longtable}
}

Verdict \texttt{STYLISTIC\_rhyme\_choice\_dominant} under the
pre-registered threshold (sound-plural-masc total = \textbf{14.9 \%},
\textless{} 50 \%). However, the more honest decomposition is that
\textbf{80.5 \% of Quranic ن-finals are some morphological
\texttt{-ūna}/\texttt{-āni}/\texttt{-īna} form} (verb-pl + dual +
sound-plural together: 37.6 + 29.0 + 14.9 = 81.5 \%) --- the dominance
is therefore \textbf{partially morphological} (Arabic does have this
\texttt{-n}-ending inflection family) but \textbf{selectively deployed
at verse end} (the Arabic Bible accesses the same morphology and reaches
only \textbf{7.53 \% \texttt{ن}-finals overall} (audit patch D
correction; the patch-B text said 14.7 \%, which was actually the
Bible's \texttt{ا} rate). The \textbf{42.57-percentage-point gap} is not
explained by Arabic-language morphology alone. \emph{(Numerical
correction, audit patch D: the patch-B paper text wrote ``14.7 \%
ن-finals'' for the Bible --- that 14.7 \% is the Bible's \texttt{ا}
rate; Bible's actual ن rate is 7.53 \%, recomputed from 31 083 Bible
verse-finals in
\texttt{audit\_patch.json::patch\_1\_per\_corpus\_noon\_rate}. The
corrected gap STRENGTHENS the verse-end-selection interpretation rather
than weakening it.)}

\textbf{Per-corpus actual ن rate} (audit patch correction):

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lrrrc@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Corpus & n\_verse\_finals & p(ن) actual & p(ا) & dominant final \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{quran} & 6 236 & \textbf{0.5010} & 0.152 & \texttt{ن} \\
poetry\_islami & 10 295 & 0.1092 & 0.206 & \texttt{ا} \\
poetry\_abbasi & 76 499 & 0.1030 & 0.176 & \texttt{ا} \\

\textbf{The Quran's verse-final ن rate (50.10 \%) is 4.6× the
next-highest Arabic-prose rate (poetry\_islami 10.92 \%) and 6.7× the
Sahih Bukhari rate (7.33 \%).} Among 8 Arabic-script corpora, no other
reaches even 11 \%; the Quran reaches 50 \%.

\textbf{Two ambiguity caveats}: (i) CamelTools occasionally classifies
\texttt{-īn}/\texttt{-ūn} words as dual-masc
(\texttt{-ayni}/\texttt{-ūni}) where they could equally be
sound-plural-masc; the 29.0 \% dual figure is therefore an upper bound
on true dual interpretations. (ii) The verb-pl-3p/2p category includes
the energetic mood (\texttt{-anna}) and indicative
(\texttt{-ūna}/\texttt{-īna}); these are not disambiguated. Source:
\texttt{results/experiments/expP9\_v79\_batch\_diagnostics/N7\_noon\_morphology.json}.

\textbf{§4.41 net contribution to the v7.9-cand record:}

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Full-114 5-D classifier}: T² = 3 685 (\st{HIGHER than band-A's
  3 557} → \textbf{REFRAMED to STABLE per v7.9-cand patch E R50}
  (\texttt{expP12\_bootstrap\_t2\_ci}): bootstrap 95 \% CI of full-Quran
  T² = {[}3 127, 4 313{]} (median 3 693); the band-A locked T² = 3 557
  is \textbf{inside} the CI, so the two T² values are statistically
  indistinguishable. The qualitative ``large multivariate separation''
  finding survives intact: T² \textgreater{} 3 000 in 100 \% of
  bootstrap resamples; AUC = 0.9932 unchanged), AUC = 0.9932. The 5-D
  ellipsoid is a property of the whole Quran. (\texttt{expP7},
  \texttt{PASS\_full\_quran\_5D}).
\item
  \textbf{EL one-feature law passes against hadith} at AUC = 0.972 ---
  the most directly comparable Arabic prose. (\texttt{expP9.N1}).
\item
  \textbf{EL one-feature law downgraded to \texttt{PASS\_arabic\_only}}
  when Pali IAST transliteration corpora are included (\texttt{pali\_mn}
  AUC = 0.87, \texttt{pali\_dn} AUC = 0.90). The drop is a
  transliteration-marker artefact (Pali \texttt{.} final at 56--60 \%),
  not a natural-letter EL failure. Cross-tradition extension of the EL
  law is therefore \textbf{bounded to native-script corpora} in
  v7.9-cand.
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{ن}-dominance confirmed Quran-distinctive within
  Arabic}: Quran p\_max(ن) = 0.501 vs next-highest Arabic-incl-hadith
  corpus 0.206 (ratio 2.43×). Among natural-letter dominants across all
  13 corpora, Quran is \#1 by 1.83× (vs Greek \texttt{ν} at 0.274).
  (\texttt{expP9.NEW2\ supplement}).
\item
  \textbf{Per-surah Σp̂² ≈ 1/2 holds at the median}: 95 \% bootstrap CI
  {[}0.366, 0.657{]} includes 0.5. The §4.40.3 corpus-pool falsification
  stands; the per-surah-median identity passes.
  (\texttt{expP9.expC1plus\_v2}).
\item
  \textbf{EL is robust to 50 \% random terminal-letter corruption} ---
  AUC ≥ 0.95 holds. (\texttt{expP9.N8}).
\item
  \textbf{Brown joint p for the 4-witness EL+R3+J1+Hurst combo =
  3.3·10⁻⁵} (conservative ρ=0.5 prior). (\texttt{expP9.N9}).
\item
  \textbf{Per-surah ranking by EL boundary distance} identifies 7 / 114
  surahs below the EL = 0.314 boundary, with Q:022 the most extreme at
  EL = 0.273. (\texttt{expP9.N4}).
\item
  \textbf{Locks tightened}: \texttt{Phi\_M\_hotelling\_T2} pinned at 3
  557.34 ± 5.0 (was \texttt{expected:\ 0.0,\ tol:\ ∞}) on 2026-04-26.
  The integrity hole reported in the external review is closed.
  (\texttt{results\_lock.json}).
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{ن}-dominance is \emph{partially morphological} but
  \emph{deliberately verse-end-selected}}: 81.5 \% of Quranic ن-finals
  fit the Arabic \texttt{-ūna}/\texttt{-āni}/\texttt{-īna} inflection
  family (37.6 \% verb-pl-3p, 29.0 \% dual-masc, 14.9 \%
  sound-plural-masc), but the Arabic Bible accesses the same morphology
  and reaches only \textbf{7.53 \% \texttt{ن}-finals overall} (audit
  patch D correction; the patch-B text said 14.7 \%, which was actually
  the Bible's \texttt{ا} rate). The \textbf{42.57-percentage-point gap}
  is verse-end-selection, not Arabic-grammar-mandated.
  (\texttt{expP9.N7}, \texttt{STYLISTIC\_rhyme\_choice\_dominant}
  verdict; CamelTools 1.5.7).
\item
  \textbf{Audit patch D (2026-04-26 evening)} ran a zero-trust audit of
  the patch-B sprint and corrected: (a) Bible ن rate 14.7 \% → 7.53 \%;
  (b) Brown joint p 3.28·10⁻⁵ → 2.95·10⁻⁵ (corrected
  \texttt{p\_Hurst\ =\ 2·10⁻⁴}); (c) added Hebrew Tanakh + Greek NT to
  the §4.41.1 cross-tradition table (AUC = 0.982 / 0.962 respectively);
  (d) flagged R3 / Hurst as not-uniquely-Quran (4 corpora more extreme
  on R3); (e) disclosed hadith\_bukhari was added post-hoc. \textbf{No
  verdict flipped}; all corrections strengthen or preserve the v7.9-cand
  record. Source:
  \texttt{results/experiments/expP9\_v79\_batch\_diagnostics/audit\_patch.json}.
\end{enumerate}

Audit trail: \texttt{experiments/expP\{7,9\}\_*/PREREG.md},

\texttt{run\_supplement.py}, result JSONs under

\subsubsection{§4.42 --- Multi-compressor consensus closes the
Adiyat-864 detection ceiling (v7.9-cand patch F, 2026-04-26
night)}\label{multi-compressor-consensus-closes-the-adiyat-864-detection-ceiling-v7.9-cand-patch-f-2026-04-26-night}

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Three statistics, three questions} \emph{(framing prelude added
v7.9-cand patch G, 2026-04-26 night).} The paper carries three distinct
quantitative tools that answer three distinct questions and should not
be conflated. \textbf{(i) EL alone} (§4.5,
\texttt{exp89b}/\texttt{exp104}) is a 1-D
\emph{classification-simplicity} result: it answers ``what is the
smallest sufficient statistic that separates the Quran from its 4
719-unit Arabic peer pool?'' --- with band-A AUC = 0.9971 it is the
minimal blessed classifier and the natural headline for parsimony
reviewers. \textbf{(ii) The 5-D Hotelling T²} (§3.3, §4.1, §4.41;
\texttt{expP7}/\texttt{expP12}) is a
\emph{magnitude-of-multivariate-separation} result: it answers ``how
large is the geometric envelope around the EL axis that the four
contextual coordinates (\texttt{VL\_CV}, \texttt{CN}, \texttt{H\_cond},
\texttt{T}) carve in 5-D?'' --- with band-A T² = 3 557, full-Quran T²
point estimate 3 685, bootstrap 95 \% CI \texttt{{[}3\ 127,\ 4\ 313{]}}
(\texttt{expP12}, verdict \texttt{STABLE}). EL alone does not subsume
T²; the multivariate magnitude is what survives reviewers asking for an
effect-size scale. \textbf{(iii) The F53 multi-compressor consensus}
(§4.42, this section; \texttt{exp95c}/\texttt{d}) is a
\emph{forensic-integrity} result: it answers ``given a single-letter
consonant edit on a canonical surah, can we detect it at recall ≥ 0.999
with FPR ≤ 0.05?'' --- for Q:100 the answer is yes (recall 1.000, FPR
0.0248). All three answers are scoped to \textbf{Quran-vs-Arabic-peers}:
cross-tradition extensions of any of the three are pre-registered future
experiments (see §4.43 below for F53's universal-scaling next step
within the Quran, and \texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md} R09 / R48 / R52
for what cross-tradition data has \emph{already} refuted at the
per-feature level).
\end{quote}

The §4.18 / §4.21 Adiyat-864 benchmark uses the gzip-9 NCD detector and
reports recall = 99.07 \% (856 of 864 single-letter variants of Q:100
fire above the ctrl-p95 threshold τ = 0.0496) --- eight variants escape
detection. We show the remaining gap is a \textbf{compressor-specific
artefact}, not a fundamental limit of the Adiyat enumeration: under a
K=2 consensus rule across four standard compressors, recall =
\textbf{864/864 = 1.000} at half the false-positive rate.

\textbf{Protocol}
(\texttt{experiments/exp95c\_multi\_compressor\_adiyat/}, hash-locked
PREREG, seed = 42). For each of \{gzip-9, bz2-9, lzma-preset-9, zstd-9\}
we compute four parallel NCDs. The ctrl-null pool is identical to
§4.18's (200 Band-A units × 20 perturbations = 4 000 ctrl edits). Each
compressor gets its own ctrl-p95 threshold τ\_c.~A variant \emph{fires
under K-consensus} iff at least K of the four compressors flag it at
their own τ\_c.

\textbf{Per-compressor solo recall and consensus recall on Adiyat-864
(Q:100)}:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2000}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2667}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Detector
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
τ (ctrl-p95)
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
Variant recall
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
Ctrl-null FPR
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
gzip-9 (R12 baseline) & 0.04961 & 856 / 864 = 0.9907 & 0.0503 \\
bz2-9 & 0.29584 & 0 / 864 = 0.0000 & 0.0503 \\
lzma-preset-9 & 0.02857 & \textbf{864 / 864 = 1.0000} & 0.0545 \\
zstd-9 & 0.02998 & \textbf{864 / 864 = 1.0000} & 0.0505 \\
\textbf{K=1 (any-compressor)} & --- & 864 / 864 = 1.0000 & 0.1770 \\
\textbf{K=2 (≥ 2 of 4) --- headline} & --- & \textbf{864 / 864 = 1.0000}
& \textbf{0.0248} \\
K=3 (≥ 3 of 4) & --- & 856 / 864 = 0.9907 & 0.0037 \\
K=4 (unanimous) & --- & 0 / 864 = 0.0000 & 0.0000 \\
\end{longtable}
}

bz2-9 produces NCDs on a different scale (mean ≈ 0.20) because its
block-sort + RLE preserves single-letter edits as small additions to a
much larger compressed form. It anti-correlates with the other three on
the ctrl null (Spearman ρ ≈ −0.5), so K=4 (all-must-agree) collapses
recall; K=2 is the natural sweet spot.

The eight gzip misses concentrate at variant position 0 (8 of 27
variants miss under gzip alone); under K=2 consensus they all fire
because lzma-9 and zstd-9 each catch every one of the 864 variants at
their own ctrl-p95 τ. The gzip ``ceiling'' is therefore a property of
LZ77's match-finder behaviour on short concatenations, not of the Adiyat
structure.

\textbf{Robustness}
(\texttt{experiments/exp95d\_multi\_compressor\_robust/}, hash-locked
PREREG). The closure is fully seed-stable on Q:100:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lrlrrr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Sub-run & seed & surah & N\_var & K=2 recall & K=2 FPR \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
1 & 42 & Q:100 & 864 & 1.000000 & 0.0248 \\
2 & 137 & Q:100 & 864 & 1.000000 & 0.0325 \\
3 & 2024 & Q:100 & 864 & 1.000000 & 0.0285 \\
4 & 42 & Q:099 al-Zalzalah & 999 & 0.998999 & 0.0248 \\
\end{longtable}
}

Q:100 K=2 recall span across \{42, 137, 2024\} = \textbf{0.000000}
(perfectly seed-stable). Cross-surah generalisation to Q:099 al-Zalzalah
hits 998 / 999 = \textbf{0.998999} --- exactly one missed variant
(position 0, ب → و; gzip-solo catches it at NCD = 0.058, but lzma-solo
NCD = 0.018 and zstd-solo NCD = 0.022 fall below their stricter ctrl-p95
thresholds). K=1 (any-compressor) achieves 1.000 on Q:099 too, at the
cost of FPR = 0.177. Robustness verdict: \texttt{PARTIAL\_seed\_only}
per pre-registered ladder --- Q:100 fully closed, Q:099 generalises at
99.9 \%.

\textbf{What did \emph{not} work, registered honestly}. Two earlier
attempted closures of the same gzip-only ceiling are logged as
\textbf{failed null pre-registrations} (Category K of
\texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}, \emph{not} retractions of standing
claims):

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{exp95\_phonetic\_modulation}}
  (FAIL\_ctrl\_stratum\_overfpr) --- reweighting ctrl-edit NCDs by
  phonetic Hamming distance does not safely close the phonetic blind
  spot; recall drops to 0.985 and per-stratum ctrl FPR exceeds 0.05 in
  every stratum d ∈ \{1, \ldots, 5\}.
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{exp95b\_local\_ncd\_adiyat}} (FAIL\_window\_overfpr)
  --- 3-verse window-local NCD collapses recall to 0.399, because the
  noise floor of small-text NCDs scales together with the 1-letter
  signal. Window-NCD is \emph{strictly worse} than full-document NCD for
  single-letter forensics on short surahs; the intuition that ``smaller
  window → bigger relative signal'' fails empirically.
\end{itemize}

\textbf{Status}. The Adiyat-864 detection ceiling at 99.07 \% under
gzip-only is \textbf{closed at 100 \%} under a small, transparent
four-compressor consensus rule, with the false-positive rate cut roughly
in half. This rules out the simplest ``gzip codebook artefact''
objection to the §4.18 result and strengthens the forgery-resistance
argument: any forged Quran-imitation intended to evade detection must
now defeat four structurally different compressors simultaneously, not
just gzip's LZ77 dictionary.

\textbf{What this does \emph{not} claim}. Q:099 has one unrejected
variant at K=2, so the ``100 \% closure'' is currently Q:100-specific;
cross-surah generalisation lands at 99.9 \% on the one alternative short
Meccan surah tested. Closure on ≥ 3 more short Meccan surahs (Q:101,
Q:103, Q:104) would escalate this from ``Q:100 paper-grade'' to
``Adiyat-class universal.'' We do \textbf{not} claim the K=2 rule is
forgery-proof against a generator that is \emph{aware} of the rule (an
adversarial-forgery test against the multi-compressor consensus is on
the long-term track).

Audit trail:
\texttt{experiments/exp95c\_multi\_compressor\_adiyat/PREREG.md},
\texttt{experiments/exp95d\_multi\_compressor\_robust/PREREG.md}, result
JSONs at
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95c\_multi\_compressor\_adiyat/exp95c\_multi\_compressor\_adiyat.json}
and
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95d\_multi\_compressor\_robust/exp95d\_multi\_compressor\_robust.json}.
Failed-null pre-registrations:
\texttt{experiments/exp95\_phonetic\_modulation/},
\texttt{experiments/exp95b\_local\_ncd\_adiyat/}.

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{§4.43 --- Universal scaling of F53 across
all 114 surahs (\texttt{exp95e}, v7.9-cand patch G post-V1, \textbf{F54
FALSIFIED at V1 scope}; rescue path \texttt{exp95j} PASSES under a
different detector class,
\textbf{F55})}{§4.43 --- Universal scaling of F53 across all 114 surahs (exp95e, v7.9-cand patch G post-V1, F54 FALSIFIED at V1 scope; rescue path exp95j PASSES under a different detector class, F55)}}\label{universal-scaling-of-f53-across-all-114-surahs-exp95e-v7.9-cand-patch-g-post-v1-f54-falsified-at-v1-scope-rescue-path-exp95j-passes-under-a-different-detector-class-f55}

\begin{quote}
\textbf{Status (FALSIFIED at V1 scope, 2026-04-26 night; rescued by a
different detector class, 2026-04-26 night patch G post-V1-iii).} The
pre-registered verdict ladder of
\texttt{exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal} (PREREG hash
\texttt{ec14a1f6dcb81c3a54b0daeafa2b10f8707457ee4305de07d58ee7ede568e9a7},
locked in
\texttt{experiments/exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal/run.py\ ::\_PREREG\_EXPECTED\_HASH})
fired \textbf{\texttt{FAIL\_per\_surah\_floor}} on the V1 scope (139 266
variants, runtime 3 287 s on 6 workers). \textbf{F53's Q:100 closure
(§4.42) stands} --- the embedded Q:100 regression in this run reproduced
K=2 = 1.000 and gzip-solo = 0.9907 exactly --- but the
\textbf{universal-extrapolation hypothesis H37 / F54 has been retracted
as R53} in \texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md} Category L. A post-hoc
mechanistic envelope is reported in §4.43.0 below as an
\emph{observation}, not a finding; pre-registered envelope replication
on the SHORT scope ran as \texttt{exp95f\_short\_envelope\_replication}
and \textbf{completed with verdict
\texttt{FAIL\_envelope\_phase\_boundary} (2026-04-28, patch H V3)} ---
H39.1 correlation passes at full V1 strength (r = −0.8519) but H39.2
phase boundary fails at a single surah (Q:055 Al-Rahman). No F-number is
opened; see §4.43.0 for full numbers and FN07 in
\texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}.

\textbf{The universal-coverage \emph{question} is then answered, but by
a different detector class.} §4.43.2 below documents
\texttt{exp95j\_bigram\_shift\_universal} (H43, PREREG hash
\texttt{a65b795b37110de80e3382bd916603888fc4f073e55d987e19dd1fcb229082cd}),
which fired
\textbf{\texttt{PASS\_universal\_perfect\_recall\_zero\_fpr}} under a
frozen analytic-bound τ = 2.0 on the same V1 variant set, with recall =
1.000 across all 114 surahs and FPR = 0.000 across the full 548 796
(canon, peer) pair pool. F55 is added to \texttt{RANKED\_FINDINGS.md}
for this result. \textbf{F55 does not un-retract R53}: R53 retracted the
\emph{NCD-consensus} extrapolation; F55 is a fundamentally different
detector (symbolic bigram, no compression, no calibration), bounded
above by a proved theorem rather than tuned to data.
\end{quote}

§4.42 closes the gzip-only ceiling on \textbf{one} surah (Q:100 Adiyat)
and shows seed-stability + Q:099 partial generalisation (998 / 999). The
natural next question was: \textbf{does the K = 2 multi-compressor
consensus rule close single-letter forgery detection on every surah of
the Quran?} That was H37, pre-registered as
\texttt{exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal}. The V1-scope answer is
\textbf{no}.

\textbf{Headline result (V1 scope).} Aggregate K=2 recall =
\textbf{0.190} (target ≥ 0.999); K=1 = 0.269; K=3 = 0.114; \textbf{K=4 =
0.000} (no variant caught by all four compressors). Per-surah K=2
distribution:

ctrl-null K=2 FPR = \textbf{0.0248} (target ≤ 0.05 ✓ --- the consensus
rule itself is well-behaved against the null pool). Embedded Q:100

both matching \texttt{exp94} and \texttt{exp95c} exactly (no τ-drift, no
Q:100-drift). \textbf{bz2-solo recall = 0.000 across all 114 surahs}
(τ\_bz2 inherited from \texttt{exp95c} is too strict to fire on any V1
variant in this corpus while still false- positing at the locked-τ rate
of 0.0503; K = 2 consensus is unaffected because it requires only any 2
of \{gzip, bz2, lzma, zstd\} to agree). Receipt:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal/v1/\ exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal.json}
(n\_variants 139 266, runtime 3 287 s, all four hash sentinels pass).

\textbf{Protocol (frozen --- unchanged from pre-registration).} Same
four compressors \{gzip-9, bz2-9, lzma-preset-9, zstd-9\}, \textbf{same
τ thresholds frozen from \texttt{exp95c}} (no per-surah recalibration; a
τ-drift sentinel aborts the run if any compressor's τ loaded from the
receipt differs from the locked snapshot by more than \texttt{1·10⁻¹²}).
Variant enumeration scopes:

\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
Approx variants
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
6-core runtime
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{V1} (default, \textbf{headline --- falsified}) & first verse of
each surah, every consonant position × all 27 substitutes & ≈ 145 K
(actual 139 266) & 54.8 min (actual) \\
\texttt{SHORT} (envelope replication, \textbf{in flight}) & first three
verses of each surah, same enumeration & ≈ 355 K (actual 355 428) &
\textasciitilde{} 2 h (estimate) \\
\texttt{QUARTER} & uniform 25 \% random sample of \texttt{FULL} & ≈ 925
K & 5 -- 8 h \\
\texttt{HALF} & uniform 50 \% random sample of \texttt{FULL} & ≈ 1.85 M
& 10 -- 18 h \\
\texttt{FULL} & every interior letter × all 27 substitutes & ≈ 3.7 M &
18 -- 36 h \\
\texttt{SAMPLE} & uniform 10 \% random sample of \texttt{FULL}, same RNG
seed & ≈ 370 K & 2 -- 6.5 h \\
\end{longtable}
}

The PASS / FAIL verdict is computed against the V1 scope (the protocol
inheritance from \texttt{exp95c}); SHORT / QUARTER / HALF / FULL /
SAMPLE produce diagnostic \emph{consistency} receipts.

\textbf{Pre-registered verdict ladder} (strict order, first match wins;
\textbf{the V1 run fired branch 4}):

\begin{enumerate}
\def\labelenumi{\arabic{enumi}.}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{FAIL\_tau\_drift} --- any τ value drifts from the
  \texttt{exp95c} receipt by \texttt{\textgreater{}\ 1·10⁻¹²}.
  \emph{(V1: not fired; max\_drift = 0.0)}
\item
  \texttt{FAIL\_q100\_drift} --- embedded Q:100 regression sub-run
  misses the exp94/exp95c targets. \emph{(V1: not fired; ok = True)}
\item
  \texttt{FAIL\_consensus\_overfpr} --- aggregate K = 2 ctrl-null FPR
  \texttt{\textgreater{}\ 0.05\ +\ 1·10⁻⁶}. \emph{(V1: not fired; FPR =
  0.0248)}
\item
  \textbf{\texttt{FAIL\_per\_surah\_floor} --- at least one surah K = 2
  recall \texttt{\textless{}\ 0.99} on V1.} \emph{(V1: fired --- 70 /
  114 surahs at K=2 = 0.)}
\item
  \texttt{FAIL\_aggregate\_below\_floor} --- aggregate K = 2 recall
  \texttt{\textless{}\ 0.999}. \emph{(would have fired had branch 4 not
  pre-empted; aggregate K=2 = 0.190.)}
\item
  \texttt{PARTIAL\_per\_surah\_99\_aggregate\_99} --- every surah
  \texttt{≥\ 0.99} AND aggregate \texttt{∈\ {[}0.99,\ 0.999)}.
\item
  \texttt{PASS\_universal\_999} --- every surah \texttt{≥\ 0.99} AND
  aggregate \texttt{≥\ 0.999}.
\item
  \texttt{PASS\_universal\_100} --- every surah K = 2 recall = 1.000 AND
  aggregate = 1.000.
\end{enumerate}

\textbf{What \texttt{exp95e} established (and what it did not).} The V1
result \textbf{rules out} the universal-scaling hypothesis H37 at the
pre-registered recall floor: F53 is \textbf{not} a Quran-universal
forgery detector under the locked τ thresholds. The result \textbf{does
not} disturb the §4.42 Q:100 closure F53 --- the in-run regression test
reproduced it exactly. What the result \emph{does} establish, beyond
pre-registration, is a per-surah landscape that feeds directly into
design of follow-on tests: the 8 perfect-K2 surahs are exactly the 8
short late-Meccan chapters (\texttt{total\_letters\_28\ ≤\ 188} for all
8), and the 70 zero-K2 surahs are all long
(\texttt{total\_letters\_28\ ≥\ 873} for all 70).
\textbf{\texttt{exp95e} did not (and does not) make any cross-tradition
claim}; its scope was exactly the same edit class as \texttt{exp94} /
\texttt{exp95c} / \texttt{exp95d}, restricted to the canonical Hafs ʿan
ʿĀṣim text of the 114 Quran surahs. Cross-tradition F53 remains a
separate pre-registered future experiment (H38; see §4.43.1 below).

\textbf{§4.43.0 --- Mechanistic envelope (post-hoc \emph{observation},
not a claim).} The per-surah landscape is too clean to be coincidence
and too post-hoc to be a claim. Across all 114 surahs:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2143}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2143}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2857}}
  >{\raggedleft\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2857}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Predictor
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Target
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
Pearson r
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedleft
Spearman ρ
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\texttt{log10(total\_letters\_28)} & per-surah K=2 recall &
\textbf{−0.85} & \textbf{−0.85} \\
\texttt{v1\_letters\_28\ /\ total\_letters\_28} & per-surah K=2 recall &
\textbf{+0.83} & +0.80 \\
\texttt{v1\_letters\ /\ total\_letters} & gzip-solo recall & +0.75 &
+0.72 \\
\texttt{v1\_letters\ /\ total\_letters} & lzma-solo recall & +0.78 &
\textbf{+0.86} \\
\texttt{v1\_letters\ /\ total\_letters} & zstd-solo recall & +0.80 &
+0.76 \\
\end{longtable}
}

The phase boundary is sharp: \textbf{all 8} K=2-perfect surahs have
\texttt{total\_letters\_28\ ≤\ 188}, and \textbf{all 70} K=2-zero surahs
have \texttt{total\_letters\_28\ ≥\ 873}. The middling 36 surahs occupy
\texttt{92\ ≤\ total\_letters\_28\ ≤\ 2\ 065}. Inferred mechanism: bz2 /
lzma / zstd have \textbf{dictionary windows much larger than gzip's}
(\textasciitilde900 KiB / unbounded / \textasciitilde128 MiB vs gzip's
32 KiB), so single-letter perturbations in a short verse-1 are absorbed
against a long surah's full canon --- the per-letter NCD increment falls
below all four locked τ thresholds. Two outliers illustrate the
boundary: Q:002 al-Baqarah (\texttt{total\ =\ 26\ 268}, V1 = ``الم'')
and Q:004 an-Nisāʾ (\texttt{total\ =\ 16\ 351}) both achieve
\textbf{gzip-solo = 1.000} because the small 32 KiB gzip window remains
sensitive even at this length, but \textbf{lzma-solo = zstd-solo =
0.000} because their larger windows absorb the change → K=2 = 0 for
both. \textbf{This pattern was discovered on the V1 receipt itself and
is therefore reported as an observation, not a finding.} The
pre-registered envelope test (H39, filed as
\texttt{experiments/exp95f\_short\_envelope\_replication/PREREG.md},
PREREG hash
\texttt{83a7b25ac69e703604a82be5c6f7c1d597ccd953f07df7f624ccc1c55d972a14})
\textbf{ran on 2026-04-28 (patch H V3) on the SHORT-scope receipt (355
428 variants) and yielded \texttt{FAIL\_envelope\_phase\_boundary}}
(FN07, Category K of \texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}; failed null
pre-registration, not a retraction). H39.1 (correlation strength) PASSED
at full V1 strength: Pearson r = \textbf{−0.8519} (≤ −0.85). H39.2
(phase boundary) FAILED: of the 72 SHORT-scope upper-band surahs
(\texttt{total\ ≥\ 873}, required K=2 ≤ 0.10), \textbf{71 obey} and a
lone violator \textbf{Q:055 Al-Rahman} (\texttt{total\ =\ 1\ 666})
registers K=2 = \textbf{0.267}; all 21 lower-band surahs
(\texttt{total\ ≤\ 188}) satisfy K=2 ≥ 0.90. Per H39 PREREG §2.3,
\textbf{no candidate-finding F-number is opened}; the V1 envelope
remains an exploratory observation only. Mechanistic note (post-hoc, not
a claim): Al-Rahman's signature internal refrain (``فبأي آلاء ربكما
تكذبان'' 31×) lifts NCD-consensus sensitivity above what surahs of
comparable length normally achieve under the locked τ. Tooling:
\texttt{scripts/analyse\_exp95e\_envelope.py\ -\/-scope\ short},
\texttt{scripts/verdict\_h39\_envelope.py}; tables at
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal/\{v1,short\}/envelope\_table.csv};
verdict at
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95f\_short\_envelope\_replication/exp95f\_short\_envelope\_replication.json}.

\textbf{§4.43.1 --- H38 cross-tradition F53 (pre-registered future,
blocked on peer corpora).} Once \texttt{exp95e} produces a verdict, the
natural follow-on is whether the same K = 2 multi-compressor consensus
rule closes single-letter forgery detection on \textbf{canonical
scriptures of other oral- liturgical traditions} at recall ≥ 0.999 with
FPR ≤ 0.05. This requires \textbf{native peer corpora} for each
tradition --- Sanskrit-Devanagari peers for the Rigveda, Hebrew peers
for the Tanakh, Pali peers for the Tipiṭaka, Avestan peers for the Yasna
--- which are not currently in the project corpus pool. A
pre-registration stub
(\texttt{experiments/expP4\_F53\_cross\_tradition/PREREG.md}) is filed
under v7.9-cand patch G with the protocol locked and the
corpus-acquisition list as the single blocking gate. \textbf{No claim
about cross-tradition F53 universality is made by this paper.} The §4.42
/ §4.43 results are scoped to \textbf{Quran-vs-Arabic-peers}, consistent
with the rest of the v7.9-cand record.

\textbf{§4.43.2 --- Universal symbolic single-letter forgery detection
by frozen-τ bigram-shift (\texttt{exp95j},
\texttt{PASS\_universal\_perfect\_recall\_zero\_fpr}, F55).} The F54
falsification rules out the \emph{NCD-consensus} extrapolation under
locked τ thresholds, but it leaves open the question whether
\textbf{any} length-independent statistic detects single-letter
forgeries on every surah. Under v7.9-cand patch G post-V1 we
pre-registered three rescue paths in
\texttt{docs/reference/sprints/POST\_V1\_PATHS\_FORWARD\_2026-04-26.md}
(per-surah τ recalibration, asymmetric length-band split, bigram-shift
symbolic detector). Path B (\texttt{exp95h\_asymmetric\_detector}, H41)
ran on the V1 receipt and returned \texttt{FAIL\_no\_clean\_split\_p90}:
across a 108-rule grid of
\texttt{\{K1,\ K2,\ K3,\ K4\}\ ×\ \{gzip,\ bz2,\ lzma,\ zstd\}} solo
combinations partitioned at any length L₀, no asymmetric rule reaches a
0.90 per-surah floor. Path C-strict
(\texttt{exp95j\_bigram\_shift\_universal}, H43, PREREG hash
\texttt{a65b795b37110de80e3382bd916603888fc4f073e55d987e19dd1fcb229082cd})
runs a fundamentally different detector and \textbf{passes universally}.

The detector is the symbolic bigram-shift statistic \textgreater{}
\texttt{Δ\_bigram(canon\_X,\ candidate)\ :=\ ‖hist\_2(canon\_X)\ −\ hist\_2(candidate)‖₁\ /\ 2}
under \texttt{letters\_28} normalisation, with the \textbf{frozen} rule
\textgreater{} \emph{fire iff
\texttt{0\ \textless{}\ Δ\_bigram(canon\_X,\ candidate)\ ≤\ τ}, with
\texttt{τ\ =\ 2.0}}.

The threshold is \textbf{not data-tuned}; it is fixed by an analytic
theorem.

\textbf{Theorem 4.43.2} (single-letter substitution bigram-shift bound).
\emph{Let \texttt{c\ ∈\ Σ*} of length \texttt{n\ ≥\ 2}, and let
\texttt{v} be \texttt{c} with the character at position
\texttt{p\ ∈\ {[}0,\ n−1{]}} replaced by
\texttt{c\textquotesingle{}\_p\ ≠\ c\_p}. Then
\texttt{Δ\_bigram(c,\ v)\ ≤\ 2}, with equality only at interior
positions (\texttt{0\ \textless{}\ p\ \textless{}\ n−1}) in the absence
of bigram aliasing.} Proof: a substitution at an interior position
removes two bigrams \texttt{(c{[}p−1{]},\ c{[}p{]})} and
\texttt{(c{[}p{]},\ c{[}p+1{]})} and adds two bigrams
\texttt{(c{[}p−1{]},\ c\textquotesingle{}\_p)} and
\texttt{(c\textquotesingle{}\_p,\ c{[}p+1{]})}, contributing at most ±1
each to the L1 distance --- total L1 ≤ 4, hence \texttt{/2\ ≤\ 2}. Edge
positions (\texttt{p\ =\ 0} or \texttt{p\ =\ n−1}) remove and add only
one bigram each, giving \texttt{Δ\ ≤\ 1}. ∎ (Insertions and deletions
extend trivially with \texttt{Δ\ ≤\ 1.5}.)

By Theorem 4.43.2, \textbf{any} detector with τ ≥ 2.0 catches
\textbf{every} single-letter substitution variant of the canon, with
recall = 1.000 on every surah, by mathematics. The empirical question
reduces to whether the same threshold τ = 2.0 also rejects non-canonical
Arabic peer texts at FPR ≤ 0.05.

\textbf{Headline result.} Run \texttt{exp95j} (single core, 311 s, no
compression) applies the frozen detector to all 139 266 V1
single-consonant-substitution variants across all 114 surahs and to all
548 796 (canon, peer) pairs formed by the full non-Quran peer pool of 4
814 items in \texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m}. The pre-registered verdict
ladder fired branch 7,
\texttt{PASS\_universal\_perfect\_recall\_zero\_fpr}:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lrr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
Quantity & Observed & Pre-reg target \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
Aggregate recall & \textbf{1.000} (139 266 / 139 266) & 1.000 \\
Min per-surah recall & \textbf{1.000} (every surah perfect) & 1.000 \\
Aggregate FPR & \textbf{0.000} (0 / 548 796) & ≤ 0.05 \\
Max per-surah FPR & \textbf{0.000} (every surah zero) & ≤ 0.05 \\
\texttt{max(Δ\_var)} audit & \textbf{2.000} (theorem holds with
equality) & ≤ 2.0 \\
\texttt{min(Δ\_peer)} (pool floor) & \textbf{73.5} & --- \\
\end{longtable}
}

The closest peer pair in the entire 548 796-pair pool sits at
\texttt{Δ\_bigram\ =\ 73.5}, more than 36× the frozen threshold τ = 2.0.
The audit hook \texttt{max\_variant\_delta\ ≤\ 2.0} holds with equality,
confirming that the analytic theorem's tight upper bound is achieved on
this corpus and therefore the locked enumeration produced no
out-of-bound variant. Receipt:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95j\_bigram\_shift\_universal/exp95j\_bigram\_shift\_universal.json}.

\textbf{What this is and is not.}

\emph{This is}: a length-independent, alignment-free, calibration-free
symbolic single-letter forgery detector that --- by the theorem above
--- catches every 1-letter substitution variant on every surah, while
the empirical bigram distinctiveness of Quran-vs-Arabic-peers in
\texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m} pushes the closest peer pair to Δ = 73.5. The
threshold τ = 2.0 is \textbf{derived from a proved bound on the
substitution operation}, not tuned to any data. The recall = 1.000
result is a property of the substitution operation; the FPR = 0.000
result is an empirical fact about Quran vs.~Arabic peers in this corpus.

\emph{This is not}: a claim about Quranic structural distinctiveness
(the recall result holds for any text class; only the FPR result depends
on the corpus); a replacement for trivial deployable detectors (SHA-256
/ Levenshtein still detect any edit by exact match for forensic
integrity); an un-retraction of R53 (R53 retracted the
\emph{NCD-consensus} universal-extrapolation; F55 is a fundamentally
different detector class --- symbolic bigram, no compression, no
calibration); a cross-tradition claim (the empirical FPR check is for
Quran-vs-Arabic-peers in \texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m} only;
cross-tradition generalisation is a separate experiment with a separate
PREREG, logged as H44 stub).

\textbf{How F55 relates to F53 and to the F54 falsification.} F53
(§4.42) remains the closure of the gzip-only Adiyat-864 ceiling at Q:100
by K = 2 multi-compressor consensus, which is paper-grade as scoped. F54
(§4.43, retracted as R53) showed that the F53 \emph{NCD-consensus}
extrapolation does \textbf{not} hold across all 114 surahs at fixed
locked-τ. F55 (this section) shows that a different detector class ---
purely symbolic, calibration-free, bounded by a theorem --- succeeds at
exactly the universal-coverage question that F54 failed. The two results
coexist: F53 closes a specific case under a compression-based detector;
F55 closes the universal case under a symbolic detector. The mechanistic
envelope (§4.43.0) describes a property of the NCD-side detector under
locked τ, not a property of the substitution operation itself.

\textbf{Predecessor record (path C-calibrated,
\texttt{exp95i\_bigram\_shift\_detector}).} Before locking τ at 2.0 by
theorem, we pre-registered the same statistic with τ calibrated as the
5th percentile of a length-matched ctrl-Δ distribution (PREREG hash
\texttt{9a67de356aff74aef306d38b2e6df829943a1472e7b544345814b4887b03e53c}).
The H42 PREREG audit hook required at least one length-matched ctrl peer
per surah; Q:108 (62 letters) has no peer in the
\texttt{{[}0.5n,\ 1.5n{]}\ =\ {[}31,\ 93{]}} window in
\texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m}, so the audit fired and the pre-registered
verdict was \texttt{FAIL\_audit\_hook\_violated}. The substantive
numbers from that run (variant Δ ∈ {[}1.0, 2.0{]} across all 139 266
variants; length-matched peer Δ ≥ 58.5 across all 5 589 matched pairs)
were already pointing to a clean PASS, but the audit hook is honoured
per pre-registration and the design space pivots to the calibration-free
H43 / F55 above. Receipt:
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95i\_bigram\_shift\_detector/exp95i\_bigram\_shift\_detector.json}.

Audit trail:
\texttt{experiments/exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal/PREREG.md}
(hash
\texttt{ec14a1f6dcb81c3a54b0daeafa2b10f8707457ee4305de07d58ee7ede568e9a7}),
\texttt{experiments/exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal/run.py},
smoke test at
\texttt{experiments/exp95e\_full\_114\_consensus\_universal/\_smoke\_test.py},
orchestration notebook at
\texttt{pipeline/full\_quran\_consensus.ipynb}, rescue-path receipts at
\texttt{experiments/exp95h\_asymmetric\_detector/} (H41,
FAIL\_no\_clean\_split\_p90),
\texttt{experiments/exp95i\_bigram\_shift\_detector/} (H42,
FAIL\_audit\_hook\_violated),
\texttt{experiments/exp95j\_bigram\_shift\_universal/} (H43,
PASS\_universal\_perfect\_recall\_zero\_fpr), and the planning doc
\texttt{docs/reference/sprints/POST\_V1\_PATHS\_FORWARD\_2026-04-26.md}.

\subsubsection{4.44 --- Multi-Scale Forgery Cascade (MSFC): consolidated
architecture + gate-by-gate amplification
audit}\label{multi-scale-forgery-cascade-msfc-consolidated-architecture-gate-by-gate-amplification-audit}

The frozen-τ bigram-shift detector of §4.43.2 closes the
universal-coverage question for single-letter forgeries by mathematics.
It does not, on its own, license a Quran-uniqueness claim --- the recall
= 1.000 result is a property of the substitution operation, not of the
text. To make explicit which parts of the forgery-detection pipeline are
Quran-distinctive and which are universal, this section consolidates the
\textbf{Multi-Scale Forgery Cascade (MSFC)} as a two-gate architecture,
then reports a pre-registered amplification audit on each candidate
sub-gate of Gate 2.

\paragraph{4.44.1 --- Architecture}\label{architecture}

The cascade decomposes the forgery question into two distinct
sub-questions:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}
  >{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{(\linewidth - 6\tabcolsep) * \real{0.2500}}@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
\begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Gate
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Sub-question
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Statistic
\end{minipage} & \begin{minipage}[b]{\linewidth}\raggedright
Quran-distinctive?
\end{minipage} \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{1 --- Membership} & ``Is the candidate text in the Quran
multivariate cluster at all?'' & 5-D Φ\_M Hotelling T² (\texttt{§4.1}) &
YES (locked, AUC = 0.998) \\
\textbf{2 --- Edit detection} & ``Given Gate 1 passed, has the candidate
been altered from canon?'' & Sub-gates 2A--2D (below) & mixed (per
sub-gate) \\
\end{longtable}
}

Gate 1 is structurally Quran-only: there exists no analogous
multivariate classifier separating any other Arabic register from the
rest of Arabic prose. The MSFC's Quran-uniqueness backbone therefore
lives at Gate 1.

Gate 2 is the \emph{forensic detection} layer. Each sub-gate is
evaluated under a single pre-registered amplification question:
\emph{``is the per-edit detectability uniquely amplified for canon =
Quran among the 7 Arabic corpora in \texttt{phase\_06\_phi\_m}?''} ---
i.e., even though the underlying statistic may be universal mathematics,
does the Quran's instance produce the largest signal? The audits below
answer this gate-by-gate.

\paragraph{4.44.2 --- Gate 2A: Δ\_bigram safety margin --- H44
FAIL\_quran\_not\_top\_1
(R54)}\label{gate-2a-ux3b4_bigram-safety-margin-h44-fail_quran_not_top_1-r54}

\texttt{exp95k\_msfc\_amplification} (PREREG hash
\texttt{a6331765ac99eb9388fb82b811326310c86b77e971d0522050a8107dab3ac822})
computed
\texttt{safety\_margin(C)\ :=\ min\ over\ u\ in\ C,\ p\ not-in-C\ of\ bigram\_l1(hist\_2(u),\ hist\_2(p))\ /\ 2}
for each of the 7 Arabic corpora as canon. The pre-registered hypothesis
was that Quran has the strictly largest safety margin by margin
\textgreater{} 5 \% over next. Verdict:
\texttt{FAIL\_quran\_not\_top\_1} --- Quran ranks \textbf{4 of 7}:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}rlr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
rank & corpus & safety margin \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
1 & ksucca & 427.0 \\
2 & hindawi & 100.0 \\
3 & arabic\_bible & 84.0 \\
\textbf{4} & \textbf{quran} & \textbf{55.0} \\
5 & poetry\_jahili & 39.0 \\
6 & poetry\_islami & 11.0 \\
7 & poetry\_abbasi & 11.0 \\
\end{longtable}
}

The bigram-shift detector's safety margin is universal mathematics, not
Quran-distinctive: small or specialised vocabularies (ksucca's
Quran-sciences corpus, hindawi's modern novelistic prose,
arabic\_bible's Christian translation register) all produce larger
safety margins than the Quran. The \textbf{F55 detector receipt is
unaffected} (recall = 1.000 by theorem, FPR = 0.000 against Arabic
peers); only the implicit \emph{amplification ranking} claim is
retracted as \texttt{R54}.

\paragraph{4.44.3 --- Gate 2C: EL-fragility --- H45
PASS\_quran\_strict\_max
(F56)}\label{gate-2c-el-fragility-h45-pass_quran_strict_max-f56}

After R54, \texttt{exp95l\_msfc\_el\_fragility} (PREREG hash
\texttt{49cea95bade2dea3dd79c1cf29f5d9c98545d7d50b2cebf2ff44dc6f6debf965})
tested a verse-final-letter substitution amplification. Define

\begin{verbatim}
EL_fragility(C) := p_max(C) × (27/28) + (1 − p_max(C)) × (1/28)
\end{verbatim}

where \texttt{p\_max(C)} is the canon's maximum verse-final-letter
frequency. \texttt{EL\_fragility(C)} is the analytical probability that
a uniformly random 1-letter substitution at a uniformly random
verse-final position in \texttt{C} changes whether the verse ends with
\texttt{C}'s top-frequency verse-final letter. Pre-registered hypothesis
H45: Quran has the strictly largest \texttt{EL\_fragility} by margin
\textgreater{} 1.5× over the next-ranked corpus.

Verdict: \texttt{PASS\_quran\_strict\_max}. Per-corpus ranking:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}rlrrc@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
rank & corpus & EL\_fragility & p\_max & letter \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{1} & \textbf{quran} & \textbf{0.5009} & \textbf{0.5010} &
\texttt{ن} \\
2 & poetry\_islami & 0.2453 & 0.2257 & \texttt{ا} \\
3 & ksucca & 0.2312 & 0.2105 & \texttt{ه} \\
4 & arabic\_bible & 0.2259 & 0.2048 & \texttt{ه} \\
5 & poetry\_jahili & 0.2243 & 0.2030 & \texttt{ا} \\
6 & poetry\_abbasi & 0.2142 & 0.1922 & \texttt{ا} \\
7 & hindawi & 0.1895 & 0.1656 & \texttt{ه} \\
\end{longtable}
}

Margin ratio \texttt{Quran\ /\ next\ =\ 2.042×}. Audit
\texttt{p\_max(quran)\ =\ 0.5010} matches \texttt{§4.5} locked target
0.501 ± 0.02. Empirical confirmation on 10,000 random verse-final
substitutions per corpus (RNG seed 95000) replicates the ranking;
absolute empirical-vs-analytical numbers differ by ≈ 0.02 because the
PREREG analytical formula assumes uniform-over-28 substitutions while
the empirical loop draws uniform-over-27 alternatives --- both
definitions rank Quran \#1 by the same \textasciitilde2× margin.

\textbf{Sub-gate 2C is therefore Quran-distinctive}: per-edit
detectability of verse-final-letter substitutions is uniquely amplified
for canon = Quran among the 7 Arabic corpora tested. Sub-gate 2C
replaces sub-gate 2A as the Gate-2 amplification layer in the cascade.
F56 added at row 56 of \texttt{RANKED\_FINDINGS.md}.

Wall-time: 3.6 s.

\paragraph{4.44.4 --- Gate 2D: 5-D Φ\_M Mahalanobis displacement --- H46
BLOCKED (structural
insensitivity)}\label{gate-2d-5-d-ux3c6_m-mahalanobis-displacement-h46-blocked-structural-insensitivity}

\texttt{exp95m\_msfc\_phim\_fragility} (PREREG hash
\texttt{8d4e7dbb6d7d7fd8948f560a1f0a5e260d338f35ad4213e3e1c3c633960328c6})
attempted to replicate the Gate 2C pass at the multivariate fingerprint
level: for each Arabic corpus, sample N = 20 random consonant
substitutions on K = 3 median-length canon units, compute the
Mahalanobis displacement \texttt{d\_M(canon,\ edit;\ S\_C\^{}\{-1\})} in
the corpus's own metric, and rank corpora by median d\_M.

The verdict ladder fired \texttt{FAIL\_audit\_features\_drift} at the
band-A T² audit (recomputed value 2,292 vs locked 3,557 --- a
consequence of \texttt{MIN\_VERSES\_PER\_UNIT\ =\ 5} dropping a small
number of control units that \texttt{expP7\_phi\_m\_full\_quran} admits
at \texttt{MIN\_VERSES\ =\ 2}). Independent of the audit, \textbf{all 7
corpora produced phim\_fragility = 0.0000}. The reason is structural:
the canonical 5-D features (\texttt{el\_rate}, \texttt{vl\_cv},
\texttt{cn\_rate}, \texttt{h\_cond\_roots}, \texttt{h\_el}) are
sensitive only to verse-final letter changes and verse-first-word
changes. For typical Arabic verses, \textgreater{} 96 \% of consonant
positions are mid-verse-and-mid-word, where a single substitution does
not change any feature. The median Mahalanobis displacement over
mostly-zero per-edit displacements is zero.

This is \textbf{consistent with \texttt{§4.20\ /\ R5}}: the canonical
5-D Φ\_M operates at the rhyme / structural-coherence scale, not the
letter-substitution scale. H46 is therefore unanswerable with the
canonical 5-D features. A fresh PREREG H47
(\texttt{exp95n\_msfc\_letter\_level\_fragility}, hash
\texttt{3d5cfcc94d215c3fc992647108a025de6550df8e86ffa60085fdf4c702ed8eaf})
rescues the question by switching to a letter-level 5-D feature vector
\texttt{Ψ\_L\ =\ {[}H\_2,\ H\_3,\ Gini,\ gzip\_ratio,\ log10(n\_distinct\_bigrams){]}}
that responds to interior consonant substitutions by construction
(zero-displacement-fraction = 0 for all 7 corpora). The structural blind
spot is resolved.

Verdict on H47: \texttt{FAIL\_quran\_not\_top\_1} --- Quran ranks
\textbf{6 of 7} by letter-level median Mahalanobis edit-fragility:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}rlrr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
rank & corpus & phim\_lvl\_fragility & smallest cov eig \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
1 & poetry\_islami & 0.1641 & 2.00·10⁻⁴ \\
2 & poetry\_abbasi & 0.1357 & 1.98·10⁻⁴ \\
3 & poetry\_jahili & 0.1163 & 1.63·10⁻⁴ \\
4 & hindawi & 0.0928 & 8.26·10⁻⁵ \\
5 & arabic\_bible & 0.0678 & 1.86·10⁻⁴ \\
\textbf{6} & \textbf{quran} & \textbf{0.0623} & \textbf{3.14·10⁻⁴} \\
7 & ksucca & 0.0224 & 6.64·10⁻⁵ \\
\end{longtable}
}

\textbf{Mechanism}: Quran's per-surah letter-level features have the
\emph{largest} natural spread of the 7 corpora (smallest covariance
eigenvalue is \emph{largest} for Quran). Smaller cov eig in poetry ⇒
larger Sinv eig ⇒ larger Mahalanobis amplification per 1-letter edit.
The Quran's verse-level / rhyme distinctiveness does NOT transfer to
letter-level multivariate tightness; the Quran spans multiple registers
(Meccan / Medinan / narrative / legal / liturgical) which makes its
per-surah letter statistics more heterogeneous than per-poem statistics
within a poetry corpus. The result is logged as \textbf{R55} in the
retractions registry. Sub-gate 2D therefore fails under both candidate
feature sets tested (canonical 5-D blocked structurally; letter-level
5-D rejected by ranking) --- the MSFC's Quran-distinctive backbone is
confirmed to be Gate 1 + Gate 2C only.

The MSFC's Quran-distinctive backbone is therefore \textbf{Gate 1
multivariate fingerprint + Gate 2C EL-fragility amplification}. The
detector receipts (F53 for Q:100 NCD-consensus; F55 for universal
symbolic 1-letter coverage) are universal-or-Q:100-only; the
\emph{amplification} statements (Quran outlier in Φ\_M, Quran rank 1 in
EL-fragility by 2×) are the parts that mark the Quran as the extremum
among Arabic texts in this project.

Audit trail: \texttt{experiments/exp95k\_msfc\_amplification/} (H44

\texttt{experiments/exp95n\_msfc\_letter\_level\_fragility/} (H47 FAIL,

in Category L of \texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{4.45 --- Joint per-dimension extremum: a Bayesian-likelihood
scaffold and its honest negative
result}\label{joint-per-dimension-extremum-a-bayesian-likelihood-scaffold-and-its-honest-negative-result}

\subsubsection{4.45.1 --- Motivation}\label{motivation}

The closing question of this project's v7.9-cand sprint is the
explicitly post-scientific one the user asked: \emph{``is there anything
more to advance the experiment further or prove the Quran's uniqueness
--- beyond science?''} The honest answer (developed in \texttt{§5} and
\texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md} Category L) is that science can
deliver a \emph{probability calculation} but cannot supply the prior
that turns a probability into a metaphysical conclusion. The cleanest
single-step move available \emph{inside calculation} is the
joint-extremum-likelihood scaffold tested here.

\texttt{H48} (\texttt{exp95o\_joint\_extremum\_likelihood}, PREREG hash
\texttt{31eaf358d10a500405348a65e29dc52245003e923d29426628a878e591fbc660})
asks: across a pre-registered panel of K = 10 features drawn from the
project's two locked feature spaces (5-D Φ\_M verse-aggregate + 5-D Ψ\_L
letter-level), how many dimensions does the Quran sit at extremum (rank
1 OR rank 7) on, and is that count significant under explicit
correlation correction?

\subsubsection{4.45.2 --- Pre-reg verdict}\label{pre-reg-verdict}

\texttt{FAIL\_audit\_el\_rate\_quran\_drift}. The audit hook for
\texttt{el\_rate(quran)} against the locked PAPER \texttt{§4.5} target
\texttt{0.7271\ ±\ 0.02} fired because the locked target is at band-A
scope (15 ≤ n\_verses ≤ 100) while the panel uses
\texttt{MIN\_VERSES\_PER\_UNIT\ =\ 2} (all 114 surahs); actual =
\texttt{0.7063}, drift = \texttt{0.0208}, just over by \texttt{0.0008}.
The pre-reg audit verdict is honoured. The companion audit
\texttt{p\_max(quran)\ ≈\ 0.501} PASSED (actual 0.50096, drift
\texttt{4·10⁻⁵}), confirming corpus identity is intact.

\subsubsection{4.45.3 --- Substantive numbers (treated as exploratory
observation)}\label{substantive-numbers-treated-as-exploratory-observation}

Independent of the audit, the substantive panel ranking gives:

{\def\LTcaptype{none} % do not increment counter
\begin{longtable}[]{@{}lr@{}}
\toprule\noalign{}
corpus & S (extremum count of 10) \\
\midrule\noalign{}
\endhead
\bottomrule\noalign{}
\endlastfoot
\textbf{ksucca} & \textbf{7} \\
\textbf{quran} & \textbf{4} \\
poetry\_jahili & 3 \\
poetry\_islami & 2 \\
poetry\_abbasi & 2 \\
hindawi & 2 \\
arabic\_bible & 0 \\
\end{longtable}
}

Quran is \textbf{not} the joint extremum --- \texttt{ksucca} (a 41-unit
specialised Quran-sciences vocabulary) collects more extremum positions
because its small specialised vocabulary distorts most features. The
naive null \texttt{P(S\ ≥\ 4\ \textbar{}\ Bin(10,\ 2/7))} =
\texttt{0.313} (not significant). The unit-level permutation null over
\texttt{100,000} trials gives
\texttt{P(max-S\ over\ 7\ corpora\ ≥\ S\_obs)\ =\ 1.000} (under random
label permutation, \emph{some} corpus always achieves ≥ 4 extremum
positions). \textbf{Joint per-dimension extremum is not
Quran-distinctive on this panel.}

\subsubsection{\texorpdfstring{4.45.4 --- Honest substructure (the part
that \emph{is}
interesting)}{4.45.4 --- Honest substructure (the part that is interesting)}}\label{honest-substructure-the-part-that-is-interesting}

Quran's 4 extremum positions are concentrated entirely on \textbf{rhyme
/ verse-structural axes}:

The Quran takes \textbf{3 of 3} pure-rhyme Φ\_M extremum opportunities
(top el\_rate, top cn\_rate, lowest h\_el = strongest rhyme
concentration), plus the cross-space Gini at rank 1. It takes \textbf{0
of 5} rhyme-blind letter-level extremum opportunities (H\_2 = 4, H\_3 =
4, gzip\_ratio = 5, log10\_nb = 4). This is a remarkable asymmetry.

The refined understanding: \textbf{Quran-distinctiveness lives at the
rhyme / verse-structural scale, not at the letter-level scale.} This
explains mechanistically why Gate 1 (rhyme-aware 5-D Φ\_M classifier)
achieves AUC = 0.998 (\texttt{§4.1}), Gate 2C (EL-fragility,
rhyme-aware) achieves Quran rank 1 by 2.04× (\texttt{§4.44.3}, F56),
while Gate 2D' (letter-level 5-D Ψ\_L) finds Quran rank 6 of 7 (R55) and
the joint per-dimension panel finds Quran rank 2 of 7 (R56). Same
project, same corpora, same statistics, mechanistically consistent
picture.

\subsubsection{4.45.5 --- What R56 means for the project's locked
claims}\label{what-r56-means-for-the-projects-locked-claims}

The locked Quran-distinctive claims are \textbf{not} retracted because
they are not per-dimension extremum claims:

\subsubsection{4.45.6 --- Bottom line for the user-asked
Bayesian-likelihood
question}\label{bottom-line-for-the-user-asked-bayesian-likelihood-question}

The strongest defensible scientific sentence the project can make about
Quran-distinctiveness, \emph{after} this Bayesian-likelihood scaffold,
is:

\begin{quote}
\emph{Among 14 Arabic + sacred-text corpora tested at AUC = 0.998 in 5-D
Φ\_M space, with single-feature amplifications of EL = 0.7271 (single
feature, AUC 0.997), p\_max(verse-final) = 0.501 (2.4× next), and
EL-fragility 2.04× next, and with 1-letter forgery detection at recall =
1.000 by analytic theorem, the Quran sits at the multivariate edge of
the rhyme / verse-structural feature space and at mid-pack on
rhyme-blind letter-level features. The project's locked statistics are
reproducible, theorem-backed where applicable, and stable across the 5
canonical riwayat; they are NOT joint-per-dimension-extremum across all
feature spaces tested (\texttt{ksucca} has more extremum positions on a
10-feature panel; R56).}
\end{quote}

That sentence is the cleanest defensible scientific \emph{premise} the
project can deliver. Whether that premise is \emph{sufficient} for any
metaphysical conclusion is --- explicitly --- outside this paper's scope
and outside any experiment's reach. The project provides the locked,
reproducible, falsifiable evidence; the prior, the inferential ladder,
and the philosophical conclusion are the reader's responsibility.

Audit trail: \texttt{experiments/exp95o\_joint\_extremum\_likelihood/};
receipt at
\texttt{results/experiments/exp95o\_joint\_extremum\_likelihood/\ exp95o\_joint\_extremum\_likelihood.json}.
Hypothesis row:
\texttt{docs/reference/findings/HYPOTHESES\_AND\_TESTS.md} H48.
Retraction: R56 in Category L of \texttt{RETRACTIONS\_REGISTRY.md}.

\begin{center}\rule{0.5\linewidth}{0.5pt}\end{center}

\subsection{4.46 --- Φ\_master: the corrected master scalar (whole
Quran)}\label{ux3c6_master-the-corrected-master-scalar-whole-quran}

\subsubsection{4.46.1 --- Motivation}\label{motivation-1}

By 2026-04-27 morning the project had 56 paper-grade locked findings but
no single scalar summary. An earlier internal \texttt{I²} proposal used
\textbf{ad-hoc multiplicative weights} and \textbf{hand-placed
constants} (notably a fiat 100-nat term for F55) that broke its
probabilistic interpretation. The 2026-04-27 afternoon feedback
identified four corrections required: (1) every Φ\_master term must be a
real log-likelihood ratio with \textbf{no ad-hoc constants}; (2) the
Bayes-factor framing must address the circularity of using Quran-derived
parameters in a Quran likelihood, via both OSF pre-registration and
leave-one-control-corpus-out cross-validation; (3) the comparison class
today is ``best naturally-occurring Arabic prose'' --- ``best deliberate
human forgery'' is unmeasured; (4) the self-describing accuracy of the
text is a measurable meta-finding (F57) deserving its own
pre-registration.

This section delivers the corrected single number under those four
constraints. \textbf{Scope (user-mandated 2026-04-27 13:55 UTC+02:00)}:
whole 114-surah Quran; no band restrictions.

\subsubsection{4.46.2 --- The corrected
formula}\label{the-corrected-formula}

\begin{verbatim}
Φ_master(text) = T1 + T2 + T3 + T4 + T5 + T6     [units: nats]
\end{verbatim}

where each term is a real log-likelihood ratio:

The \textbf{F55 term is 12.12 nats, not 100}. Clopper-Pearson 95 \%
one-sided upper bound on the empirical FPR given 0 successes in N =
548,796 peer pairs is \texttt{1\ −\ 0.05\^{}(1/N)\ ≈\ 6.72·10⁻⁶}, giving
\texttt{log(1\ /\ 6.72·10⁻⁶)\ ≈\ 12.12} nats. Honest, falsifiable,
principled.

(out-of-sample)}\label{headline-in-sample-and-robustness-out-of-sample}

verdict \texttt{PASS\_phi\_master\_locked}.

\textbf{Robust Bayes-factor floor}: even when poetry\_abbasi (the
largest control corpus, 60 \% of the null pool by row count) is held out
--- halving Σ rank --- Φ\_master remains at \textbf{1,634.49 nats}, a
Bayes factor of \textbf{10⁷⁰⁹}. The bootstrap p05 is \textbf{1,759.72
nats} (BF ≈ 10⁷⁶⁴). Both are well above the pre-registered 1,500-nat
floor.
